When a Traveler Intends 15 Days of Stay, He Becomes a Resident
Establishes the Hanafi ruling on residency and qasr using mafhum mukhalafah and resolves an objection via ijma'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a traveler becomes a resident and explain the role of mafhum mukhalafah and ijma' in deriving it.

Core Idea
Intending 15 days transforms the traveler into a resident, ending qasr — and ijma' overrides the literal text for shorter stays.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah explores how the Quranic permission for qasr is tied to travel (ضرب فی الارض). Using mafhum mukhalafah, the author argues that intending residence removes the travel condition, thus requiring full prayers. A potential objection — that even a short stay should end qasr — is resolved by invoking ijma', which preserves the concession for stays under four days.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Dalil and its Mafhum
Locate the Quranic verse cited and understand how the author uses mafhum mukhalafah to derive the condition for qasr.
The verse permits qasr when travelling; its converse implies impermissibility when not travelling.
2
Apply to Intending Residence
When a traveler intends iqamah (residence), he ceases to be travelling, so qasr is no longer permitted.
The Hanafi school requires an intention of at least 15 days to complete the state of residence.
3
Recognize the Objection
The text raises an objection: if the absence of travel is the criterion, then even a short stay (less than 4 days) should also remove qasr.
This objection is based on a literal reading of the mafhum.
4
Understand the Role of Ijma'
The Hanafi school leaves the literal text due to ijma' — the consensus that a stay of less than 4 days does not make one a resident.
This illustrates that ijma' can override a textual implication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة المسافر اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم الْأَرْضِ فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ اَنْ تَقْصُرُوا مِنَ الصَّلوةِ اس آیت میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے ضرب فی الارض یعنی چلنے سے قصر کو مباح کیا ہے اس کا مفہوم مخالف یہی کہ اگر ضرب فی الارض نہ ہو تو قصر مباح نہیں ہے پس جب مسافر نے اقامت کی نیت کی تو اس نے ضرب فی الارض کو چھوڑ دیا۔ اور جب ضرب فی الارض کو چھوڑ دیا تو اس کے واسطے قصر کرنا مباح نہ رہا لیکن اس پر سوال ہوگا کہ اگر چار دن سے کم قیام کی نیت کرے تو بھی قصر کرنے کی اجازت نہ ہونی چاہئے کیونکہ ضرب فی الارض اس صورت میں بھی نہیں پایا گیا۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ نص کا تقاضا تو یہی ہے کہ چار دن سے کم قیام کرنے سے قصر کا حکم باقی نہ رہے۔ مگر ہم نے دلیل اجتماع کی وجہ سے چار دن سے کم میں اس نص کو ترک کر دیا ہے اس لئے کہ اس س کم قیام کی نیت سے مقیم ہونے کا کوئی قائل نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of the Traveler's Prayer. Ashraf al-Bidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume 2. '...in the earth, there is no sin upon you if you shorten the prayer.' In this verse, Allah has permitted qasr due to moving about in the land, i.e., travelling. Its converse is that if there is no moving about, then qasr is not permitted. So when a traveler intends residence, he has abandoned moving about. And when he has abandoned moving about, then for him qasr is not permissible. But there is a question: If he intends to stay less than four days, then also qasr should not be permitted because moving about is also not found in this case. The answer is that the textual requirement is that staying less than four days would remove the ruling of qasr. But we have left this text due to ijma' (consensus) for staying less than four days, because no one says that intending such a short stay makes one a resident.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the traveler's prayer. It first cites the Quranic verse (Surah al-Nisa: 101) which permits shortening prayer when travelling. The author uses the concept of mafhum mukhalafah (inverse implication) to argue that when one is not travelling (i.e., has no ضرب فی الارض), qasr is not permitted. Therefore, if a traveler intends to settle (اقامت), he is no longer in a state of travel and must pray full prayers. However, a potential objection arises: if a traveler intends to stay less than four days, he is also not 'moving about' actively, so why is qasr still allowed? The answer is that the literal text (نص) would indeed suggest that even a short stay should remove the concession, but the Hanafi school leaves this literal meaning due to ijma' (consensus) of the scholars, who unanimously agree that a stay of less than four days does not make one a resident. This illustrates the principle that ijma' can override a literal textual implication.

Key Terms
ضرب فی الارض (ḍarb fī al-arḍ): Moving about in the land, i.e., travelling.
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'ah prayers to two rak'ahs while travelling.
اقامت (iqāmah): The state of being a resident (muqim), which ends the concession of qasr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following makes a traveler a resident (muqim) such that he must pray full prayers?
A) Intending to stay for any period
B) Intending to stay for 15 days
C) Intending to stay for 4 days
D) Staying without any intention

Key Takeaway
Intending to stay 15 days or more transforms a traveler into a resident, obligating full prayers; shorter stays preserve the concession of qasr due to ijma'.

Intention as a Condition for Residency: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Presents the dispute on whether intention is required to become a resident

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the necessity of intention to become a resident (muqim), explain the proof each school uses, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Without intention to stay 15+ days, a traveler remains a traveler in Hanafi fiqh—even after a year.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether a traveler must intend to stay in a place to become a resident (muqim) and thus start praying full prayers. The Hanafi school insists on intention; the Shafi'i school does not. Understanding this dispute helps you apply the correct ruling when advising travelers.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its basis
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding intention for residency and the Quranic principle (mafhum mukhalafah) that supports it.
The Hanafi position is that intention is a condition; without it, one remains a traveler even after 15 days.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Identify the Shafi'i view and the evidence from 'Uthman's statement that does not mention intention.
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the saying of 'Uthman: 'Whoever stays four days, let him pray full prayer.'
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
Understand how the Hanafi school critiques the Shafi'i evidence: the statement's lack of mention does not prove negation.
The Hanafi response: the sahabi's statement is not explicit about intention, and the Quranic principle overrides it.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Apply the dispute to a real scenario: a traveler stays long without intending to stay permanently; what prayer ruling applies?
Hanafi: qasr continues; Shafi'i: full prayer after 4 days.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
Identify which position is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school and why.
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) due to stronger Quranic evidence and practice of early companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اقامت کے لئے نیت شرط ہے دوسرا اختلاف یہ ہے کہ اقامت کے لئے ہمارے نزدیک اصل نیست شرط ہے چنانچہ ہمارے نزد یک بلانیت اقامت مقیم نہیں ہوگا۔ خواہ پندرہ دن سے زائد قیام کرے۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک مقیم ہونے کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل حضرت عثمان کا قول من اقام اربعا اہم ہے یعنی جو شخص چار دن قیام کرے وہ پوری نماز پڑھے اس قول میں نیت کا ذکر نہیں ہے لہذا ثابت ہوا کہ مقیم ہونے کے لئے نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
Intention is a condition for residence. The second difference is that for residence, according to us, intention is a condition. Thus, according to us, without intention, one does not become a resident, even if he stays more than fifteen days. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, intention is not a condition for becoming a resident. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is the statement of Hadrat 'Uthman: 'Whoever stays four days, he should pray full prayer.' In this statement, intention is not mentioned, so it is established that intention is not necessary for becoming a resident.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage presents a clear inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafi position, attributed here to Abu Hanifa and the school, is that intention (niyyah) to stay is a necessary condition for a traveler to become a resident (muqim). Without it, even if one physically stays for a long period, he remains a traveler and may continue to pray qasr. Imam al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, does not require intention; rather, he considers actual stay (usually 4 days or more) as sufficient to make one a resident. His evidence is a statement attributed to Caliph 'Uthman (radiallahu 'anhu) which instructs one who stays four days to pray full prayer, without mentioning intention. The Hanafi school would respond by maintaining that the sahabi's statement is not necessarily exhaustive, and the principle of intention is derived from the Quranic mafhum mukhalafah as discussed earlier.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention to stay for a specific period (15 days) which is a condition for becoming a resident in the Hanafi school.
اقامت (iqāmah): The state of being a resident, which ends the concession of qasr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What evidence does Imam al-Shafi'i use to argue that intention is not required for becoming a resident?
A) A Quranic verse
B) A hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him)
C) The statement of 'Uthman (radiallahu 'anhu)
D) Analogy with prayer

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, intention to stay for at least 15 days is a condition for a traveler to become a resident; without it, qasr remains valid even after extended stay.

Deriving the 15-Day Residency Rule via Qiyas
Explains the qiyas (analogy) used to set 15 days as minimum residency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi qiyas that establishes the 15-day minimum for iqāmah and identify the common effective cause ('illa).

Core Idea
The 15-day residency rule is derived by analogy: just as tuhr restores worship obligations, iqāmah restores full prayer.

This passage from Al-Hidayah reveals the systematic reasoning behind a key Hanafi ruling: the 15-day minimum stay that ends a traveler's concession to shorten prayer. Imam Abu Hanifa does not simply declare the number—he builds a careful analogy (qiyas) on the period of purity (tuhr) between menstrual cycles. By understanding this derivation, you will see how Hanafi jurists used analogical reasoning to determine shar'i limits and how the statements of Companions served as supporting evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case (asl) and its ruling
The original case is the period of purity (tuhr) after hayd. In Hanafi fiqh, the minimum tuhr is 15 days. During this period, worship obligations that were suspended due to hayd (e.g., prayer, fasting) become binding again.
This is a known shar'i ruling from texts on taharah.
2
Identify the new case (far') and the problem it poses
The new case is the period of residence (iqāmah) for a traveler. A traveler may halt for a long time, and it becomes necessary to determine when he is no longer a traveler (musafir) but a resident (muqim), so that full prayer becomes obligatory.
The distinction between a mere halt and residence requires a specific duration.
3
Determine the common effective cause ('illa)
The common 'illa is that both tuhr and iqāmah are causes for the return of obligations that were previously dropped. Just as tuhr restores worship obligations after hayd, iqāmah restores the obligation of full prayer after travel.
This is called 'being a cause for obligation' (مُوجِب ہونا).
4
Apply the analogy (qiyas) to derive the ruling for the new case
Since the 'illa is shared, the ruling of the original case (15 days) is transferred to the new case. Therefore, the minimum iqāmah is also 15 days.
This is a jali (clear) qiyas.
5
Support the ruling with Companion statements
The author of Al-Hidayah cites the statements of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar explicitly stating the 15-day rule. Since the determination of such limits (muqaddarat shar'iyyah) is beyond reason, the athar of a Companion carries the weight of a marfu' hadith.
This strengthens the derivation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اقامت کے لئے پندرہ یوم کا اعتبار کرنے میں امام اعظم کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسافر کے لئے یہ ضروری نہیں ہے کہ وہ شب وروز ۲۴ گھنٹے چلتا ر ہے۔ بلکہ وہ بسا اوقات ٹھہرتا بھی ہے اور کافی دیر تک ٹھہر جاتا ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ سفر اور لبث ( ٹھہرنا دونوں جمع ہو جاتے ہیں۔ یہ بات بھی اظہر من الشمس ہے کہ ٹھہرنے کا نام ہی اقامت اور مقیم ہونا ہے پس چونکہ ان دونوں کے درمیان فرق کرنے کے لئے ایک مدت کا اعتبار کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اس لئے ہم نے مدت طہر پر قیاس کر کے مدت اقامت پندرہ یوم مقرر کی ہے۔ رہی بات یہ کہ قیاس کی علت مشترک کیا ہے۔ سو اس بارے میں صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ مدت طہر اور مدت اقامت دونوں کا موجب ہونا علت مشترکہ ہے۔ یعنی حیض کی وجہ سے جو عبادت ساقط ہوگئی تھی مدت طہر کی وجہ سے جس طرح وہ عود کر آتی ہے اس طرح سفر کی وجہ سے ساقط شدہ عبادت بھی مدت اقامت کی وجہ سے عود کر آتی ہے پس اس قیاس کی بنیاد پر جس طرح ادنی مدت طہر پندرہ دن ہیں اسی طرح ادنی مدت اقامت بھی پندرہ یوم ہوں گے ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ طہر کی ضد حیض کی ادنیٰ مدت تین دن ہیں۔ تو اقامت کی ضد سفر کی ادنی مدت بھی تین دن ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مدت اقامت کا پندرہ دن ہونا حضرت ابن عباس اور حضرت ابن عمر رضی اللہ عنہم سے بھی مروی ہے۔ چنانچہ مجاہد نے روایت کی ہے عن ابن عباس وابن عمر رضى الله عنهما قالا اذا دخلت بلدة وانت مسافر وفي عزمک ان تقيم بها خمسة عشر يوما فاكمل الصلوة وان كنت لاتدرى متى تظعن فاقصر یعنی ان دونوں حضرات صحابہ نے فرمایا کہ جب تو کسی شہر میں داخل ہو۔ حالانکہ تو مسافر ہے۔ اور تیرا ارادہ پندرہ دن قیام کا ہے تو نماز پوری پڑھ اور اگر تجھ کو یعلم نہیں کہ کب سفر کرے گا تو تو قصر کرتا رہ ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ پندرہ دن کی تحدید مقدرات شرعیہ میں سے ہے اور ایام کی تقدیر وتحدید ایسی چیز ہے جس کی طرف عقل بھی راہ یاب نہیں ہے۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ مالا يعقل کے اندر اثر صحابی بمنزلہ خبر اور حدیث کے ہوتا ہے۔ گویا ابن عباس اور ابن عمر نے پندرہ یوم کی تحسین حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے سن کر بیان کی ہے۔
Regarding the adoption of fifteen days for residence, the proof of Imam al-A'zam (Abu Hanifa) is that it is not necessary for a traveler to be continuously moving night and day. Rather, he sometimes halts and stays for a long time. Hence it is understood that travel and halt (staying) can be combined. It is also clearer than the sun that staying is called iqāmah and being a muqim. Since it is necessary to specify a period to distinguish between them, we have set the period of residence as fifteen days by analogy (qiyas) on the period of purity (tuhr). As for the common effective cause ('illa) of the analogy, the author of al-Hidayah said that 'being a cause for obligation' is the common 'illa: just as the obligation of worship that was dropped due to hayd returns due to the period of tuhr, similarly the obligation dropped due to travel returns due to the period of residence. So based on this analogy, just as the minimum tuhr is fifteen days, the minimum residence is also fifteen days. This is also why the minimum hayd (the opposite of tuhr) is three days, and the minimum travel (the opposite of residence) is also three days. The author of al-Hidayah says that the determination of fifteen days for residence is also narrated from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar (radiallahu 'anhuma). Thus, Mujahid narrated from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar that they said: 'When you enter a town while you are a traveler and you intend to stay there for fifteen days, then complete the prayer. And if you do not know when you will depart, then shorten.' The meaning is that these two Companions said that when you enter a city while you are a traveler and you intend to stay for fifteen days, pray full; and if you do not know when you will travel, continue shortening. The author of al-Hidayah said that the limitation of fifteen days is among the shar'i determined limits (muqaddarat shar'iyyah), and the determination of days is something that reason cannot grasp. And the rule is that in matters that are not rational, the effect of a Companion (athar sahabi) is like a report (khabar) and hadith. So it is as if Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar heard this determination of fifteen days from the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam) and narrated it.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed proof for the 15-day minimum stay to become a resident. Imam Abu Hanifa first establishes that a traveler can both travel and halt; these are not mutually exclusive. To distinguish between a mere halt and actual residence (iqāmah), a specific duration is needed. He then draws an analogy (qiyas) with the period of purity (tuhr) from hayd. In Hanafi fiqh, the minimum duration of tuhr is 15 days, and during this period, the obligations of worship (like prayer and fasting) that were suspended due to hayd become binding again. Similarly, the obligations of full prayer that were lifted due to travel become binding again after a 15-day residence. The common 'illa is that both (tuhr and iqāmah) are causes for the return of obligations. The minimum opposite periods also correspond: minimum hayd is 3 days, minimum travel is 3 days (as per another rule). To further support this, the author quotes a narration from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn 'Umar that explicitly states the 15-day rule. Since the determination of such limits (muqaddarat shar'iyyah) is beyond rational deduction, the statement of a Companion (athar sahabi) carries the weight of a marfu' hadith (attributed to the Prophet). Thus, the 15-day rule is firmly established in the school.

Key Terms
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive the 15-day residency period from the period of purity (tuhr).
مدت طہر (muddat al-ṭuhr): The period of purity between two menstrual cycles, minimum 15 days in Hanafi fiqh.
مقدرات شرعیہ (muqaddarāt sharʿiyyah): Shar'i (divinely legislated) determined quantities or limits that are not known by reason alone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the common effective cause ('illa) in the analogy between tuhr (purity) and iqāmah (residence)?
A) Both are periods of three days
B) Both involve travel
C) Both are causes for the return of obligations that were previously dropped
D) Both are determined by consensus

Key Takeaway
The 15-day minimum for residency is established by a clear qiyas on the period of purity, supported by the statements of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar, and is a shar'i determined limit (muqaddar shar'i).

Residency Valid Only in Town or Village: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Explains the condition of location for valid iqamah and an intra-Hanafi exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that iqamah is valid only in a settled area and identify the exception made by Abu Yusuf for shepherds.

Core Idea
Iqamah only valid in a settled area; shepherds in wilderness may be an exception per Abu Yusuf.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a critical condition for becoming a resident (muqim) during travel: the location must be a town or village. While the majority position is strict, a notable intra-Hanafi difference from Abu Yusuf allows an exception for shepherds who set up camp with access to grass and water. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply the ruling in diverse scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for valid iqamah
The passage states that iqamah is valid only in a town (balada) or village (qarya). What does this imply for intending to stay in a wilderness (jangal)?
The condition is about the location's settled nature, not just the duration of stay.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf differs: if shepherds pitch tents in a place with grass and water and intend 15 days, they become residents. How does this modify the condition?
Abu Yusuf's view focuses on actual stability rather than administrative designation.
3
Trace the transmission weight
The majority view is zahir al-riwayah (the apparent transmission). What does this tell us about its authority in the school?
Zahir al-riwayah is the primary reliance for fatwa, but other valid views are recorded.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a traveler who stays in a desert rest area for 20 days. Determine his residency status according to both views.
Per majority he remains a musafir; per Abu Yusuf, if he sets up a camp with provisions, he becomes muqim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ امام ابوالحسن قدوری کا اقامت کے لئے بلدہ یا قریہ کی قید لگانا اس طرف مشیر ہے کہ جنگل میں اقامت کی نیت کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ یہی ظاہر الروایۃ ہے۔ اگر چہ قاضی ابو یوسف نے فرمایا ہے کہ چرواہے اگر گھاس پانی کی جگہ خیمہ زن ہو جائیں پندرہ دن ٹھہرنے کی نیت کر لیں تو مقیم ہو جائیں گے۔
The author of al-Hidayah says that Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri's restriction of residence to a town (balada) or village (qarya) indicates that intending residence in a wilderness is not valid. This is the apparent (zahir al-riwayah) position. Although Qadi Abu Yusuf has said that if shepherds pitch tents in a place of grass and water and intend to stay for fifteen days, they become residents.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage highlights an intra-Hanafi difference. The majority position (apparent from the transmission, ظاہر الروایۃ) is that for a traveler's intention to iqāmah to be effective, the location must be a settled area like a town (balda) or village (qarya). Intending to stay in a desert or wilderness (jangal) does not make one a resident, even with the intention of 15 days. This is supported by Imam al-Quduri's phrasing. However, Qadi Abu Yusuf makes an exception for shepherds (charwahay) who settle in a place with grass and water and intend 15 days: they do become residents. This difference reflects different considerations of stability: the wilderness generally does not provide the stability of a settled community, but shepherds who set up camp in a specific location may have sufficient stability. The relied-upon position for fatwa is the zahir al-riwayah (the majority view), but Abu Yusuf's view is also noted in the school.

Key Terms
بلدہ (balada): A town or city; a settled area where iqāmah is valid.
قریہ (qarya): A village, similar to a town in terms of being a settled area.
جنگل (jangal): Wilderness or desert; not a valid place for iqāmah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent position (zahir al-riwayah) of the Hanafi school, where is a traveler's intention to stay 15 days valid for becoming a resident?
A) Any place including wilderness
B) Only in a mosque
C) In a town or village (settled area)
D) Only in one's hometown

Key Takeaway
For iqamah to be valid, the location must be a settled area; the majority restricts it to towns/villages, while Abu Yusuf allows an exception for shepherds.

Salah — Prayer

Traveler Indefinitely Staying Without Intention: Continues Qasr
Ruling: A traveler who does not intend 15 days but stays for years continues qasr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a traveler must pray qasr as long as he has not intended a 15-day stay, and apply it to cases of indefinite stay.

Core Idea
A traveler remains a traveler as long as he has not intended a 15-day stay — even if his actual stay extends to years.

The Hanafi school has a precise criterion for what makes a traveler become a resident: the intention to stay for at least 15 days. Without that intention, no matter how long the actual stay, the traveler continues to pray qasr. This lesson unpacks that rule, its evidence from the Companions, and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify that a traveler who enters a city without intending to stay 15 days remains a traveler and must pray qasr, even if he stays for years.
This is the core ruling of the passage.
2
Identify the condition
The decisive factor is the intention (niyyah) to stay for 15 consecutive days. Without that intention, he does not become a resident.
Intention of 15 days triggers residency.
3
Trace the evidence
The proof comes from the practice of Companions: Ibn Umar (6 months in Azerbaijan), Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas (2 months), and Alqamah ibn Qays (2 years) — all prayed qasr because they had not intended 15 days.
Companion practice is a valid source in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that if a traveler stays 4 days or more, full prayer becomes obligatory regardless of intention.
This difference has practical consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک شہر سے آج کل نکلنے کا ارادہ کیا لیکن دو سال تک ٹھہرارہا تو نماز قصر پڑھے گا الودخل مصرا على عزم ان يخرج غدا او بعد غد ولم ينو مدة الاقامة حتى بقى على ذلك سنین قصر لان بن عمر اقام باذر بيجان ستة اشهر وكان يقصر وعن جماعة من الصحابة مثل ذلك رجمہ اور اگر کوئی مسافر شہر میں اس ارادہ کے ساتھ داخل ہوا کہ کل یا پرسوں کوچ کرے گا اور مدت اقامت کی نیت نہیں کی یہاں تک کہ اس ارادہ کے ساتھ چند سال ٹھہرارہا تو قصر کرتا رہے گا۔ کیونکہ ابن عمر نے آزربیجان میں چھ ماہ قیام کیا حالانکہ قصر پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ صحابہ کی ایک جماعت سے اس کے مثل مروی ہے۔ شریح پہلے مسئلہ میں گذر چکا ہے کہ اقامت کے واسطے پندرہ دن کے قیام کی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے اس پر متفرع کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ اگر مسافر کسی شہر میں اس نیت کے ساتھ داخل ہوا کہ کل یا پرسوں روانہ ہو جاؤں گا۔ مدت اقامت یعنی پندرہ روز کے قیام کی نیت نہیں کی حتی کہ اسی آج کل میں چند سال گذر گئے تو یہ قصر پڑھتا رہے گا مقیم نہیں کہلائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر نے مقام آذربیجان میں چھ ماہ قیام کی مگر چونکہ حضرت ابن عمر نے بیک وقت پندرہ دن قیام کرنے کی نیت نہیں کی تھی اس لئے وہ قصر نماز ہی پڑھتے ہے۔ اس کے مثل دوسرے صحابہ سے مروی ہے۔ چنانچہ سعد ابن ابی وقاص کے بارے میں مروی ہے۔ کہ انہوں نے نیشا پور کے کسی ہاؤں میں دو ماہ قیام کیا اور قصر پڑھتے رہے اسی طرح علقمہ بن قیس نے خوارزم میں دو سال قیام کیا اور قصر نماز پڑھی۔
He intends to leave a city today or tomorrow, but stays for two years; he will pray qasr. The matn says: 'And if he enters a city with the intention of leaving tomorrow or the day after, and he does not intend a specific duration of stay, and he remains like that for years, he shortens, because Ibn 'Umar stayed in Azerbaijan for six months and used to shorten. And similar reports are narrated from a group of Companions.' The commentary: And if a traveler enters a city with the intention of departing tomorrow or the day after, and he does not intend a specific duration of stay (i.e., fifteen days), even if he remains with that intention for several years, he will continue to shorten his prayer and will not be called a resident. The proof is that 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar stayed in Azerbaijan for six months, but because he had not intended to stay for fifteen days at once, he used to pray qasr. Similar is narrated from other Companions. For example, it is narrated about Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas that he stayed in a place in Nishapur for two months and prayed qasr. Similarly, 'Alqamah ibn Qays stayed in Khwarazm for two years and prayed qasr.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage applies the general rule: a traveler who enters a city without intending to stay for 15 days remains a traveler indefinitely, even if his actual stay extends to years. His intention to leave 'tomorrow or the day after' prevents him from becoming a resident. The proof comes from the practice of several Companions, most notably Ibn 'Umar who stayed in Azerbaijan for six months but did not intend a 15-day stay, thus he prayed qasr. Similarly, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas stayed two months and 'Alqamah two years. This reinforces the Hanafi principle that intention (niyyah) of a 15-day stay is the decisive factor, not the actual duration of stay. The passage also shows that the Hanafi school relies on the actions of the Companions as evidence when the Quran and Sunnah are not explicit.

Key Terms
قصر (qasr): Shortening the prayer while in a state of travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He was forced to stay
B) He did not intend to stay 15 days at once
C) He was not in a city
D) He forgot to pray full

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on qasr hinges on the traveler's intention to stay 15 days, not the actual length of stay.

Army in Enemy Territory: Intention of Stay Invalid
Ruling with reasoning for army's prayer during campaign

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for an army's prayer when intending to stay in enemy territory and explain why the intention does not make them residents.

Core Idea
An army remains travelers in prayer even with a 15-day intention because enemy territory lacks the definitive stability required for residence.

This lesson clarifies a practical scenario in the law of travel and prayer: when Muslim soldiers enter enemy territory and intend to stay, do they become residents who must pray full prayers? The Hanafi school holds that they do not, due to the inherent uncertainty of war. We examine the text from Al-Hidayah and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the prayer of an army in enemy territory. The ruling is that they must pray qasr (shortened prayer).
The matn states 'they shorten' directly.
2
Identify the condition that would change the ruling
If the army were to become residents (muqim), they would pray full prayers. The condition for becoming a resident through intention of stay is that the place must be a dar iqamah (place of definitive stability).
The commentary emphasizes 'definitive stability and settlement.'
3
Understand why the condition is not met
The army in enemy territory is between defeat (flight) and victory (settlement). This uncertainty means the place lacks definitive stability, so it is not a dar iqamah. Hence, intention of stay is invalid.
The text compares this to a forest in dar al-Islam, which also lacks stability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لشکر کی دار الحرب میں اقامت کی نیت معتبر ہے یا نہیں إذا دخل العكسر ارض الحرب فنو والاقامة بها قصروا وكذا اذا حاصروا فيها مدينة أو حصنا لان الداخل ين ان يهزم فيفروبين ان يهزن فيقر فلم تكن داراقامة رجمہ اور جب اسلامی لشکر کفار کے ملک میں داخل ہوا اور اس میں پندرہ دن ٹھہرنے کی نیت کی تو کبھی قصر کریں گے۔ اور یوں ہی ب دار الحرب میں کسی شہر یا قلعہ کا محاصرہ کیا ہو۔ کیونکہ داخل ہونے والا شکر (دوباتوں کے درمیان ) متردد ہے ایک یہ کہ شکست کھا کر بھاگ جائے دوم یہ کہ شکست دے کر قیام پذیر ہو جائے اس لئے یہ دارا قامت نہیں ہوگا۔ شریح اسلامی لشکر نے دار الحرب میں داخل ہو کر پندرہ دن کے قیام کی نیت کی تو بھی حکم یہ ہے کہ یہ فوجی مسلمان قصر نماز پڑھیں ۔ ہی حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ اسلامی فوج نے دار الحرب میں گھس کر کسی شہر یا قلعہ کا محاصرہ کر لیا ہو۔ حاصل یہ کہ دارالحرب کے اندر اسلامی لشکر کی اقامت کے سلسلہ میں نیت معتبر نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اقامت کی نیت کا محل وہ جگہ ہوتی ہے جہاں انسان کو حتمی طور پر قرار اور ٹھہراؤ میسر ہو۔ در یہاں صورت یہ ہے کہ اسلامی لشکر قرار اور فرار کے مابین متردد ہے۔ اس لئے کہ شکست کی صورت میں راہ فرار اختیار کرنی پڑے گی۔ در فتح کی صورت میں قرار نصیب ہوگا ۔ پس فرار اور قرار کی کشمکش میں دارالحرب کو اسلامی لشکر کے لئے دارا قامت نہیں کہا جاسکتا۔ جیسے دارالاسلام میں جنگل دارا قامت نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ جنگل میں اقامت کی نیت معتبر نہیں ہے۔
Is intention of residence valid for an army in enemy territory? The matn says: 'When an army enters enemy territory and intends to stay there, they shorten. Similarly, if they besiege a city or fortress there. Because the one entering is between two possibilities: either they are defeated and flee, or they defeat and settle. So it is not a place of residence.' The commentary: And when an Islamic army enters the land of disbelievers and intends to stay for fifteen days, they will still shorten. Similarly, if they besiege a city or fortress in enemy territory. Because the entering army is uncertain between two matters: one is that they may be defeated and flee, second is that they may achieve victory and settle. Therefore, it will not be a place of residence. The commentary: When an Islamic army enters enemy territory and intends to stay fifteen days, the ruling is that these Muslim soldiers will pray qasr. The same ruling applies when the Islamic army enters enemy territory and besieges a city or fortress. The conclusion is that in enemy territory, the intention of stay is not valid for the Islamic army. Because the place for intention of residence is where a person has definitive stability and settlement. In this case, the Islamic army is between stability and flight. Because if defeated, they must flee; if victorious, they will settle. Thus, in the conflict between flight and stability, enemy territory cannot be called a place of residence for the Islamic army. Just as in dar al-Islam, a forest (wilderness) is not a place of residence, so intention of stay there is invalid.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific scenario: an army (or military force) that enters enemy territory (dar al-harb). Even if the soldiers intend to stay for 15 days, this intention does not make them residents, and they continue to pray qasr. The reason is that the army's presence is uncertain: they may be defeated and forced to flee, or they may be victorious and settle. True residence requires a place of definitive stability (qarār) and settlement. The uncertainty here prevents the place from being considered a 'dar iqāmah' (place of residence). The text draws an analogy with a forest in dar al-Islam: just as a forest cannot be a place of residence because it lacks settled habitation, similarly enemy territory lacks the stability required for residence. This ruling ensures that soldiers maintain the concession of qasr even if they stay for a long period, as their presence is contingent on military fortunes.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Enemy territory; a land under non-Muslim control where Muslims cannot establish permanent settlement.
دار اقامت (dār iqāmah): A place of residence where one has definite stability and settlement.
قصر (qasr): Shortening the prayer from 4 rakats to 2 for travelers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does an Islamic army not become a resident even if they intend to stay 15 days in enemy territory?
A) Because the land is not owned by Muslims
B) Because they are uncertain between victory and defeat
C) Because they do not pray in congregation
D) Because the intention must be made at home

Key Takeaway
An army in enemy territory remains travelers for prayer because the land lacks the definitive stability needed for intention of stay to be valid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Traveler Who Does Not Intend Fifteen Days Stays a Traveler
Ruling with proof from Sahaba examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a traveler becomes a resident (muqim) and apply the condition of intending 15 days, using the example of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Intention of 15 days makes a resident; duration alone does not.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on when a traveler transitions to a resident. The key factor is the intention to stay 15 days, not the actual length of stay. We will look at the evidence from the Companions, especially Ibn Umar, who stayed in Adharbayjan for six months yet continued to shorten his prayers because he did not intend to stay 15 days. Understanding this ruling helps avoid the common mistake of assuming that a long stay automatically makes one a resident.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The passage states that a traveler who enters a city with the intention to leave soon (e.g., 'tomorrow or the day after') remains a traveler even if he stays for years. The condition is not intending a 15-day stay.
2
Recognize the proof from Sahaba
The author cites the action of Ibn Umar and other Companions who stayed for extended periods without intending 15 days and continued to pray qasr. Note the specific cases: Ibn Umar (6 months), Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas (2 months), Alqamah ibn Qays (2 years). The proof demonstrates that intention, not duration, is decisive.
3
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a traveler who stays in a city for 3 months but never intends to stay 15 days, he remains a traveler and must pray qasr. If he later forms the intention to stay 15 days, he becomes a resident from that moment.
4
Contrast with other schools
The Hanafi school uses 15 days; the Shafi'i school uses 4 days (three full days plus entry/exit). This difference shows how the criterion of intention interacts with different time thresholds.
The mukhtalaf fih box will detail this further.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة المسافر یا پندرہ دن ٹھہرنے کی نیت کر لیں تو مقیم ہو جائیں گے۔ ایک شہر سے آج کل نکلنے کا ارادہ کیا لیکن دو سال تک ٹھہرارہا تو نماز قصر پڑھے گا الودخل مصرا على عزم ان يخرج غدا او بعد غد ولم ينو مدة الاقامة حتى بقى على ذلك سنین قصر لان بن عمر اقام باذر بيجان ستة اشهر وكان يقصر وعن جماعة من الصحابة مثل ذلك رجمہ اور اگر کوئی مسافر شہر میں اس ارادہ کے ساتھ داخل ہوا کہ کل یا پرسوں کوچ کرے گا اور مدت اقامت کی نیت نہیں کی یہاں تک کہ اس ارادہ کے ساتھ چند سال ٹھہرارہا تو قصر کرتا رہے گا۔ کیونکہ ابن عمر نے آزربیجان میں چھ ماہ قیام کیا حالانکہ قصر پڑھا کرتے تھے۔ صحابہ کی ایک جماعت سے اس کے مثل مروی ہے۔ شریح پہلے مسئلہ میں گذر چکا ہے کہ اقامت کے واسطے پندرہ دن کے قیام کی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے اس پر متفرع کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ اگر مسافر کسی شہر میں اس نیت کے ساتھ داخل ہوا کہ کل یا پرسوں روانہ ہو جاؤں گا۔ مدت اقامت یعنی پندرہ روز کے قیام کی نیت نہیں کی حتی کہ اسی آج کل میں چند سال گذر گئے تو یہ قصر پڑھتا رہے گا مقیم نہیں کہلائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر نے مقام آذربیجان میں چھ ماہ قیام کی مگر چونکہ حضرت ابن عمر نے بیک وقت پندرہ دن قیام کرنے کی نیت نہیں کی تھی اس لئے وہ قصر نماز ہی پڑھتے ہے۔ اس کے مثل دوسرے صحابہ سے مروی ہے۔ چنانچہ سعد ابن ابی وقاص کے بارے میں مروی ہے۔ کہ انہوں نے نیشا پور کے کسی ہاؤں میں دو ماہ قیام کیا اور قصر پڑھتے رہے اسی طرح علقمہ بن قیس نے خوارزم میں دو سال قیام کیا اور قصر نماز پڑھی۔
Chapter on the Prayer of the Traveler. Or if they intend to stay fifteen days then they become residents. A person intends to leave a city 'today or tomorrow' but stays for two years, then he will pray qasr. And if he enters a city with the intention to leave tomorrow or the day after, and he does not intend a period of residence, even if he remains like that for years, he shortens. Because Ibn Umar stayed in Adharbayjan for six months and he was shortening. And from a group of the Companions similar to that. Translation: And if a traveler enters a city with the intention to leave tomorrow or the day after, and he does not intend a period of residence, until he stays with that intention for several years, then he will continue to shorten. Because Ibn Umar stayed in Azerbaijan for six months while he used to pray qasr. Similar is narrated from a group of the Companions. Shuraih has passed in the first issue that for residence it is necessary to intend a fifteen-day stay. Building on that, he said: If a traveler enters a city with the intention to leave tomorrow or the day after, and he does not intend a period of residence i.e. fifteen days, even if several years pass in this 'today or tomorrow', then he will continue to pray qasr and will not be called a resident. The proof is that Abdullah ibn Umar stayed in the place of Azerbaijan for six months, but since Ibn Umar did not intend to stay fifteen days at one time, he used to pray qasr. Similar is narrated from other Companions. For example, it is narrated about Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas that he stayed in some village of Nishapur for two months and continued to pray qasr. Similarly, Alqamah ibn Qays stayed in Khwarazm for two years and prayed qasr.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the situation of a traveler who enters a city not intending to stay a full period of residence (15 days in the Hanafi school). Even if he remains for many years, he remains a traveler and must shorten his prayers. The key condition is intention: as long as he does not intend to stay 15 consecutive days, he does not become a resident. The proof comes from the actions of the Companions, notably Ibn Umar who stayed in Adharbayjan for six months without intending 15 days and continued to pray qasr. The same is reported from Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and Alqamah ibn Qays. The commentary emphasizes that intention, not duration, is the criterion.

Key Terms
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'ah prayers (zuhr, asr, isha) to two rak'ahs while traveling.
مقیم (muqim): A resident who prays the full four rak'ahs.
اقامت (iqamah): Residence, specifically the intention to stay in one place for a period of 15 days or more.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the condition for a traveler to become a resident (muqim) such that he must pray full prayers?
A) Staying for more than 15 days regardless of intention
B) Intending to stay for 15 days or more
C) Staying for 6 months
D) Intending to leave after 2 days

Key Takeaway
A traveler becomes a resident only by intending to stay 15 days; duration alone does not change the ruling.

Army in Dar al-Harb Cannot Intend Residence
Ruling on army's intention to stay in enemy territory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shortening prayer for an army in dar al-harb and explain the legal reasoning based on uncertainty of stable settlement.

Core Idea
An army in enemy territory is always a traveler—no intention of residence is valid due to uncertainty.

The Hanafi school holds that a Muslim army entering dar al-harb must always pray qasr, even if they intend to stay fifteen days or more. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof, showing how the nature of the place prevents valid intention of residence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State that the army must shorten prayer (qasr) despite intending to stay.
2
Understand the condition
The intention of residence (niyyat al-iqamah) is not valid in dar al-harb for an army due to the uncertain outcome of war.
3
Analyze the evidence
The ruling is based on qiyas: just as a forest in dar al-islam is not a place of residence, so too dar al-harb is not a place of residence for an army.
The analogy hinges on lack of stability.
4
Apply to scenarios
The same applies whether the army is encamped or besieging a city.
5
Conclude
Thus the army remains travelers (musafir) until they actually settle in a place that qualifies as dar al-iqamah.

Source Text

When the army enters the land of war and they intend residence there, they still shorten. Likewise if they besiege a city or fortress there, because the one who enters is between two possibilities: either he is defeated and flees, or he defeats and remains. So it is not a place of residence. Translation: And when the Islamic army enters the land of the disbelievers and intends to stay fifteen days there, then they will still shorten. And similarly if they besiege a city or fortress in dar al-harb. Because the entering army is uncertain between two things: one is that they are defeated and flee; the second is that they defeat and settle. Therefore this will not be a place of residence. Explanation: If the Islamic army enters dar al-harb and intends to stay fifteen days, the ruling is still that these Muslim soldiers pray qasr. The same ruling applies when the army penetrates dar al-harb and besieges a city or fortress. The conclusion is that in dar al-harb, the army's intention for residence is not valid. Because the place for intention of residence is where a person has definitive settlement and stability. Here the army is between settlement and flight. Because in case of defeat they must flee, and in case of victory they settle. In this conflict between flight and settlement, dar al-harb cannot be called a place of residence for the army, just as in dar al-islam, a forest is not a place of residence. This is why intention of residence in a forest is not valid.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage delivers a ruling and its reasoning. It addresses the situation of a Muslim army that enters enemy territory (dar al-harb). Even if they intend to stay 15 days or more, they must still shorten their prayers because they are not established residents. The reason is that an army is uncertain about the outcome: they may be defeated and have to retreat, or they may win and settle. This uncertainty means they cannot form a valid intention of residence. The place itself is not a 'dār iqāmah' (abode of residence). The rule applies both when the army is stationed in the land and when besieging a city or fortress. Comparatively, even in dar al-islam, a forest (jungle) is considered a place where intention of residence is not valid because it lacks permanent settlement.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where Islamic law is not enforced and war is permitted.
دار الاقامة (dar al-iqamah): A place where one can settle permanently with stability, like a city with permanent buildings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because the army is uncertain about defeat or victory, preventing stable settlement
C) Because the army has no intention to stay
D) Because the army is not allowed to pray full prayers

Key Takeaway
An army in dar al-harb must shorten prayer even if they intend to stay, because the territory lacks stability for valid residence.

Siege and Residence: Can the Army Intend to Stay?
Dispute on whether army can intend residence while besieging rebels

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the validity of a besieging army's intention to reside and apply the mufta bihi ruling to determine qasr or tamam.

Core Idea
A besieging army cannot validly intend 15 days of residence, so they pray qasr — uncertainty in the result defeats stability.

When a Muslim army lays siege to rebels in dar al-islam, a fiqhi question arises: can the soldiers intend to stay for 15 days, thus becoming muqim and praying tamam? The Hanafi school has a nuanced dispute. Abu Hanifa holds that their uncertain condition nullifies any intention of residence. Imam Zufar allows it if the army has the upper hand, and Imam Abu Yusuf permits it only if they occupy permanent mud houses. This lesson unpacks the positions and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and scenario
Recognize that the ruling concerns a Muslim army besieging rebels (ahl al-baghy) in dar al-islam, but outside a city or at sea. The army's status (musafir or muqim) depends on whether they can validly intend 15 days of residence.
2
State the Hanafi default (Abu Hanifa)
According to Abu Hanifa, the army's intention to reside is invalid in all cases because their condition is between defeat and victory — uncertainty nullifies settlement. Thus they remain musafir and must pray qasr.
3
Note the ikhtilaf of Imam Zufar
Imam Zufar holds that if the army has the upper hand (shawka), the intention is valid because they appear able to settle. In that case, they pray tamam; otherwise qasr.
4
Note the ikhtilaf of Imam Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf further restricts validity to only when the army occupies permanent mud houses (buyut al-madar). If they are in tents, intention is invalid and they pray qasr.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa: the army always prays qasr regardless of strength or dwelling. This is the fatwa given due to the inherent uncertainty of siege warfare.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا اذا حاصروا اهل البغى فى دار الاسلام فى غير مصر او حاصر وهم في البحر لان حالهم مبطل وعند زفر يصح فى الوجهين اذا كانت الشوكة لهم للتمكن من القرار ظاهر اول عند ابي يوسف يصح اذا كانوا في بيوت المدر لانه موضع اقامة رجمہ اور یونہی جب لشکر اسلام نے دار الاسلام کے اندر شہر کے علاوہ میں باغیوں کا محاصرہ کیا یا سمندر میں انکا محاصرہ کیا۔ کیونکہ ان کی حالت ان کے ارادہ کو باطل کرتی ہے۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں صحیح ہے بشرطیکہ شوکت لشکر اسلام کو حاصل ہو۔ کیونکہ بظاہر ان کو ٹھہر نے پر قابو حاصل ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس وقت صحیح ہے جبکہ اسلامی لشکر کا قیام مٹی کے گھروں میں ہو اس لئے کہ وہ پھہرنے کی جگہ ہیں
And likewise when they besiege the people of rebellion (ahl al-baghy) in dar al-islam outside a city, or they besiege them in the sea, because their condition nullifies (their intention). And according to Zufar, it is valid in both cases if they have the upper hand (al-shawka), because they are apparently able to settle. First? According to Abu Yusuf, it is valid if they are in houses of mud (buyut al-madar) because that is a place of residence. Translation: And similarly, when the Islamic army besieges the rebels in dar al-islam outside a city, or besieges them in the sea, because their condition invalidates their intention. And according to Imam Zufar, it is valid in both cases provided the Islamic army has strength, because apparently they have control over staying. And according to Abu Yusuf, it is valid when the Islamic army’s stay is in mud houses, because they are a place of residence.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a dispute within the Hanafi school. It addresses the situation of an Islamic army besieging rebels (ahl al-baghy) in dar al-islam, but not inside a city: either in open land or the sea. The Hanafi position (presumably Abu Hanifa's) is that the army cannot validly intend 15 days of residence because they are still in a state of uncertainty (like in dar al-harb). However, Imam Zufar disagrees: he says the intention is valid if the army has the upper hand (shawka), because then they have apparent stability. Abu Yusuf takes a middle ground: the intention is valid only if the army is staying in mud houses (permanent buildings) because that indicates a place of residence; if they are in tents, the intention is not valid.

Key Terms
اهل البغى (ahl al-baghy): Rebels; Muslims who revolt against the legitimate ruler without justification.
شوکت (shawka): Strength, power, military might that gives apparent stability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only if the army is in the sea
B) Only if the army stays in mud houses (permanent buildings)
C) Only if the army has the upper hand
D) Under no circumstances

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that a besieging army always prays qasr, regardless of its strength or dwelling, because its intention to settle is nullified by uncertainty.

The Bedouin's Intention to Stay: Becoming Muqimun
Ruling on Bedouin's intention to stay despite nomadic lifestyle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Bedouin nomads who intend 15 days of residence and explain the legal reasoning (talil) for their status as muqimun.

Core Idea
A Bedouin who intends 15 days becomes a resident because residence is the original state.

The status of Bedouin nomads (ahl al-kala/ahl al-akhbiya) in the laws of travel (qasr) raises a question: can a person whose livelihood depends on moving from pasture to pasture ever be considered a resident? The Hanafi school, based on a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf, rules that yes—if they intend to stay 15 days, they become muqimun. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the group
Understand who 'ahl al-kala' (people of grass) and 'ahl al-akhbiya' (tent-dwellers) are—Bedouin nomads who move for grazing.
They are not permanent settlers.
2
State the initial objection and correct view
Some said their intention of residence is invalid. The correct view (al-asahh) is that they become muqimun.
The text: 'قيل لا يصح والأصح أنهم مقيمون'.
3
Identify the proof source
The correct view is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf, a major Hanafi authority.
This gives the ruling weight from Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Analyze the legal reasoning (talil)
The reason is that residence (iqamah) is the original state for humans. Temporary movement for pasture does not nullify that original residence.
This is a principle of istishan.
5
Apply the ruling
If a Bedouin intends to stay 15 days in a location, he/she must pray full prayers (tamam) instead of qasr.
Practical consequence in salah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونية الاقامة من اهل الكلاء وهم اهل الاخبية قيل لانصح والاصح انهم مقيمون يروى ذلك عن ابي يوسف لان الاقامة اصل فلا تبطل بالانتقال من مرعى الى مرعى رجمہ اور اقامت کی نیت کرنا گھاس والوں کا درانحالیکہ وہ خیمہ بردار لوگ ہیں کہا گیا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اور اصبح یہ ہے کہ یہ یتیم رکعت کی طرح ہیں۔ امام ابو یوسف سے یوں ہی روایت کیا جاتا ہے کیونکہ اقامت اصل ہے لہذا ایک چراگاہ سے دوسری چراگاہ کی طرف منتقل ہونے سے باطل نہیں ہوگی۔
And the intention of residence from the people of grass (ahl al-kala) and they are the people of tents (ahl al-akhbiya): it was said it is not valid, and the correct view is that they are residents (muqimun). That is narrated from Abu Yusuf, because residence is the origin, so it is not invalidated by moving from one pasture to another. Translation: And the intention of residence from the grass-dwellers, while they are tent-dwelling people, it was said it is not valid. And the correct view is that these are like the muqimun. It is narrated thus from Abu Yusuf, because residence is the origin, so it will not be invalidated by moving from one pasture to another.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage addresses the status of Bedouin nomads (ahl al-kala, ahl al-akhbiya) who live in tents and move from place to place for pasture. The question is whether they can validly intend 15 days of residence in a given location and thus be considered residents (muqimun) who must pray full prayers. Some scholars said their intention is not valid because they do not have permanent settlement. However, the correct view (al-asahh) is that they are considered muqimun and their intention is valid. This is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf. The reasoning is that residence (iqamah) is the original state for humans, and merely moving from one pasture to another for livelihood does not nullify that original residence. Therefore, when they intend 15 days in a spot, they become muqimun.

Key Terms
اهل الكلاء (ahl al-kala): People who depend on grass/pasture for their livelihood, i.e., Bedouin nomads.
اهل الاخبية (ahl al-akhbiya): People of tents; those who live in tents rather than permanent buildings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) They must continue to pray qasr because they are nomads
D) They are considered travelers until they build permanent houses

Key Takeaway
Bedouin nomads who intend 15 days become muqimun; their nomadic lifestyle does not prevent them from being residents.

Intention of Residence for an Army Besieging Rebels
Intra-Hanafi dispute on niyyat al-iqamah for a besieging army.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on niyyat al-iqamah for an army besieging rebels and explain the intra-Hanafi differences among Abu Hanifa, Zufar, and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
An army's unsettled battle condition invalidates residence intention, unless strength or durable dwelling is present.

When Muslim soldiers besiege rebels outside cities, does their intention to stay make them residents? The Hanafi school examines the realities of war and dwelling to determine residency. In this passage, we explore the positions of Abu Hanifa, Zufar, and Abu Yusuf on this nuanced issue.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi ruling
Identify the default position: niyyat al-iqamah is invalid because the army's situation (battle, uncertainty) undermines the resolve to stay.
This is based on the phrase 'hāluhum mubṭil li-ʿazīmatihim'.
2
Identify Zufar's condition
Imam Zufar holds the intention valid if the army has military strength (shawkah), giving them apparent ability to settle.
He validates in both non-city and sea scenarios.
3
Identify Abu Yusuf's condition
Abu Yusuf restricts validity to when the army stays in mud houses (buyut al-madar), which are considered permanent dwellings.
He does not accept mere military strength as sufficient.
4
Understand the grassland people ruling
The passage discusses nomads (ahl al-kalā') who move between pastures. The correct view is that they are residents because residence is the default (asl), not invalidated by mobility within a region.
This is narrated from Abu Yusuf and is the preferred view (al-aṣaḥḥ).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
While the text does not explicitly settle the dispute for the army, the preference for the grassland people's residence suggests a lenient approach when stability is apparent. The general ruling remains that the intention is invalid without a stable dwelling or guaranteed control.
Practically, most soldiers remain travelers unless they have a fixed base.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا إذا حاصروا أهل البغي في دار الإسلام في غير مصر أو في البحر لأن حالهم مبطِّل لعزمتهم. وعند زفر يصح في الوجهين إذا كانت الشوكة لهم للتمكن من القرار ظاهرًا. وعند أبي يوسف يصح إذا كانوا في بيوت المدر لأنه موضع إقامة. ونية الإقامة من أهل الكلاء وهم أهل الأخبية قيل لا يصح والأصح أنهم مقيمون يروى ذلك عن أبي يوسف لأن الإقامة أصل فلا تبطل بالانتقال من مرعى إلى مرعى.
ترجمہ: اور یونہی جب لشکر اسلام نے دار الاسلام کے اندر شہر کے علاوہ میں باغیوں کا محاصرہ کیا یا سمندر میں ان کا محاصرہ کیا۔ کیونکہ ان کی حالت ان کے ارادہ کو باطل کرتی ہے۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں صحیح ہے بشرطیکہ شوکت لشکر اسلام کو حاصل ہو۔ کیونکہ بظاہر ان کو ٹھہرنے پر قابو حاصل ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس وقت صحیح ہے جبکہ اسلامی لشکر کا قیام مٹی کے گھروں میں ہو اس لئے کہ وہ ٹھہرنے کی جگہ ہیں۔ اور اقامت کی نیت کرنا گھاس والوں کا درآنحالیکہ وہ خیمہ بردار لوگ ہیں کہا گیا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اور اصح یہ ہے کہ یہ مقیم ہیں۔ امام ابو یوسف سے یوں ہی روایت کیا جاتا ہے کیونکہ اقامت اصل ہے لہذا ایک چراگاہ سے دوسری چراگاہ کی طرف منتقل ہونے سے باطل نہیں ہوگی۔
And likewise, when they besiege the people of rebellion in Dar al-Islam outside a city or at sea, because their situation invalidates their resolve. According to Zufar, it is valid in both cases if they have the upper hand, apparently having ability to settle. According to Abu Yusuf, it is valid if they are in mud houses because that is a place of residence. The intention of residence from the grassland people who are tent-dwellers, it is said it is not valid, but the most correct is that they are residents; that is narrated from Abu Yusuf because residence is the original state and is not invalidated by moving from one pasture to another.
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage contains an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of niyyat al-iqamah (intention to reside) for a Muslim army besieging rebels in non-urban areas. The general ruling is that the army's unsettled condition (being in a state of battle with possibility of victory or defeat) invalidates their intention to reside, so they remain travelers. Imam Zufar holds it valid if they have military strength (shawkah) giving them apparent ability to settle. Imam Abu Yusuf restricts validity to when they stay in mud houses (buyut al-madar), which are typical dwelling places. Regarding the grassland people (ahl al-kala') who live in tents, some say their intention to reside is invalid, but the correct view is that they are residents (muqimun) because residence is the original state and moving from one pasture to another does not break it. This shows Hanafi methodology: the principle (asl) is residence; travel is an incidental (arid) that must be proven. The ruling exemplifies consideration of 'urf and actual conditions.

Key Terms
الإقامة (al-iqāmah): Intention to stay in a place for 15 days or more, making one a muqim (resident) required to pray full prayers.
الشوكة (al-shawkah): Military strength and power that enables an army to settle securely.
الكلاء (al-kalā'): Grassland people, i.e., nomads who live in tents and move for pasture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is invalid because their situation is unsettled.
C) It is valid only if they stay in mud houses, according to Imam Abu Yusuf.
D) It is valid if they have military strength, according to Imam Zufar.

Key Takeaway
The validity of niyyat al-iqamah depends on the ability to settle securely, not merely on intention or duration.

Traveler Following Resident Imam Within Time
Ruling on traveler completing four rak'ahs when following resident imam within time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a traveler follows a resident imam within the prayer time, explain the proof (taba'iyyah and qiyas), and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Following a resident imam changes the traveler's obligation from two to four rak'ahs within the time.

This lesson examines a key scenario in congregational prayer: a traveler (musafir) joining a resident (muqim) imam for a four-rak'ah prayer within its time. The Hanafi school rules that the traveler must complete all four rak'ahs, contrary to the Shafi'i and Maliki schools. We will analyze the proof based on the principle of taba'iyyah (following) and the analogy with niyyat al-iqamah (intention to reside).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific act being ruled upon? The traveler (musafir) follows (iqtida') a resident (muqim) imam in a four-rak'ah fard prayer within its prescribed time. The ruling is that the traveler must complete four rak'ahs.
The act is defined by three conditions: traveler status, following a resident imam, and the prayer time still remaining.
2
Locate the dalil
The text states: 'because his obligation changes to four due to following (taba'iyyah)'. This is the proof. Additionally, an analogy (qiyas) is made with intention to reside (niyyat al-iqamah), where the obligation also becomes four. Both are cases where a changer (mugayyir) is connected to the cause (sabab), i.e., the time.
The dalil combines explicit statement and qiyas.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase is 'يتغير فرضه إلى أربع للتبعية' (his obligation changes to four due to following). The cause (illa) is the connection (ittisal) of the changer (the act of following) to the cause (the prayer time). Just as niyyat al-iqamah changes the obligation, so does iqtida' because in both cases the changer is time-connected.
The proof relies on the Hanafi principle that taba'iyyah can override the traveler's original concession.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i and Maliki schools hold that the traveler's original rukhsah (shortening) is not overridden by following a resident imam. The Hanbali school agrees with the Hanafi position. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in Shafi'i/Maliki, the traveler prays two rak'ahs even behind a resident.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; each school has its own usul principles.

Source Text

وإن اقتدى المسافر بالمقيم في الوقت أتم أربعا لأنه يتغير فرضه إلى أربع للتبعية كما يتغير بنية الإقامة لاتصال المغير بالسبب وهو الوقت.
ترجمہ: اور اگر وقت کے اندر مسافر نے مقیم کی اقتداء کی تو پوری چار رکعت پڑھے۔ کیونکہ تابع ہونے کی وجہ سے مسافر کا فریضہ چار رکعت کی طرف متغیر ہو جاتا ہے جیسے اقامت کی نیت سے متغیر ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ متغیر کرنے والا سبب یعنی وقت کے ساتھ متصل ہو گیا ہے۔
And if the traveler follows the resident imam within the time, he completes four rak'ahs because his obligation changes to four due to following, just as it changes by intention of residence, because the changer is connected to the cause, which is the time.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage states the ruling: when a traveler (musafir) prays behind a resident (muqim) imam in a four-rak'ah prayer within its prescribed time, he must complete all four rak'ahs. The proof is that following (taba'iyyah) changes his obligation from two to four, analogous to how the intention to reside (niyyat al-iqamah) changes it. The common factor (jami') is that the changer (mugayyir) – either the act of following or the intention – is connected to the cause (sabab), which is the time. Since the time is still present, the traveler's duty is to complete the prayer. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is universally accepted among Hanafis.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtidā'): Following an imam in congregational prayer.
التبعية (al-taba'iyyah): The principle that a follower's obligation adapts to the imam's by virtue of following.

B) The traveler must complete four rak'ahs.
C) The prayer becomes invalid.
D) The traveler may choose to complete or shorten.

Key Takeaway
Following a resident imam within the prayer time obligates the traveler to complete four rak'ahs, due to the principle of taba'iyyah.

Traveler Following Resident Imam for Missed Prayer
Ruling on traveler following resident for qada prayer being invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a traveler's following a resident imam for a missed (qada) prayer is invalid and apply the qiyas jaliy reasoning behind the ruling.

Core Idea
When the cause (time) is absent, the obligation does not change, making iqtida' invalid.

This lesson examines a specific scenario: a traveler praying a missed (qada) prayer behind a resident imam. The Hanafi school rules this iqtida' invalid because the time (sabab) for the obligation has expired. We will explore the qiyas jaliy that links this case to the rule that niyyat al-iqamah does not change a qada prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a traveler following a resident imam for a missed prayer after its time. The ruling: the iqtida' is invalid (lam tujizhu).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is a qiyas jaliy: analogy to the case where a traveler intends residence (niyyat al-iqamah) for a qada prayer, which does not change the prayer from two to four rak'ahs.
The analogy is drawn because both cases share the absence of the cause (time).
3
Analyze the illa (effective cause)
The illa is the absence of the cause (sabab) – time. Since the time for the prayer has passed, the traveler's obligation to pray two rak'ahs does not change to four.
The illa is jaliyyah (obvious): time is the operative cause.
4
Apply the analogy
Just as niyyat al-iqamah does not change the qada prayer, following the resident imam does not change the traveler's obligation. Therefore, the traveler remains obligated to pray two rak'ahs, but the imam prays four, creating a mismatch.
5
State the consequence
The mismatch results in a muftarid (obligated person) following a mutanaffil (supererogatory performer) in terms of sitting and recitation, which is invalid according to Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن دخل معه في فائتة لم تجزه لأنه لا يتغير بعد الوقت لانقضاء السبب كما لا تتغير بنية الإقامة فيكون اقتداء المفترض بالمتنقل في حق القعدة أو القراءة.
ترجمہ: اور اگر مسافر مقیم کے ساتھ کسی فائتہ نماز میں داخل ہوا تو جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وقت کے بعد مسافر کا فریضہ متغیر نہیں ہوگا اس لئے کہ سبب (وقت) تو گزر چکا۔ جیسے قضاء نماز میں نیت اقامت سے نہیں بدلتی، تو قعدہ یا قراءت میں مفترض کا متنفل کی اقتداء لازم آئے گا۔
And if he enters with him in a missed prayer, it is not valid for him because he does not change after the time has passed due to the expiration of the cause, just as it does not change by intention of residence. Then it would be the following of one who is obliged by one who is supererogatory in respect of sitting or recitation.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage explains the second scenario: if a traveler follows a resident imam for a missed (fā'itah) prayer after its time has expired, the iqtida' is invalid. The reason is that the cause (sabab) for the change in obligation – the time – has ended. Just as niyyat al-iqamah does not change the traveler's prayer from qada to ada (because the time is gone), similarly, following the imam does not change the traveler's obligation from two to four after the time has passed. Consequently, the traveler would be praying his two-rak'ah qada prayer behind an imam who prays four, resulting in a case where a person obligated (muftarid) follows one who is performing a supererogatory (mutanaffil) prayer in terms of actions like sitting and recitation, which is invalid according to Hanafi fiqh. This is a qiyas jaliy: the time is the effective cause for the change; when the time is absent, the change does not occur.

Key Terms
الفائتة (al-fā'itah): A missed prayer performed after its time (qada).
المتنفل (al-mutanaffil): One performing a supererogatory prayer; here, the imam's prayer is considered supererogatory for the traveler's obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the cause (time) has expired, so the obligation does not change.
C) Because the imam's prayer is invalid.
D) Because the traveler must pray alone.

Key Takeaway
The traveler's missed prayer after its time does not change obligation when following a resident imam, making iqtida' invalid.

Traveler Following Resident Imam in On-Time Prayer
Ruling with proof: traveler completing four rakats behind a resident imam in on-time prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a traveler follows a resident imam in an on-time four-rakat prayer, explain the proof using tabi'iyyah and qiyas, and distinguish the two cases of a traveler imam and resident imam following each other.

Core Idea
A traveler who follows a resident imam in on-time prayer must complete four rakats because his obligation changes to match the imam's through tabi'iyyah.

This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling established by al-Quduri in his matn and expanded in al-Hidayah. The key issue is whether a traveler who shortens prayers must pray two or four rakats when praying behind a resident imam. The ruling relies on the principle of tabi'iyyah (following) and uses a qiyas (analogy) to the case of a traveler who intends to reside. Understanding this reasoning clarifies how Hanafi school derives obligations in congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
The case is a traveler (musafir) who prays behind a resident imam (muqeem) in an on-time (ada) four-rakat prayer.
The prayer must be performed within its proper time, not as qada.
2
State the ruling
The traveler must complete four rakats; he cannot shorten to two.
This is despite the general concession for travelers to shorten four-rakat prayers.
3
Explain the proof: tabi'iyyah
The traveler's obligation changes to four because he has bound himself to follow an imam whose fard is four. The principle of tabi'iyyah (following) transforms the follower's fard to that of the imam.
This is a qiyas-based ruling, not from a direct text.
4
Analyze the qiyas
The analogy is to a traveler who intends residence (niyyat al-iqamah): in both cases, the traveler's prayer changes from two to four. The common 'illa is that a 'changer' (iqtida' or niyyah) is connected to the cause (time).
The qiyas is khafiyyah; the 'illa is extracted via tanqih al-manat.
5
Note the scope and second case
The ruling applies only within the prayer time. There is also a second case: a resident following a traveler, which is valid both within and after the time.
This distinction is important for muftis to apply correctly.

Source Text

مسافر کے لئے مقیم کی اقتداء کا حکم
وان اقتدى المسافر بالمقيم فى الوقت اتم اربعا لانه يتغير فرضه الى اربع للتبعية كما يتغير بنية الاقامة لاتصال المغير بالسبب وهو الوقت
ترجمہ اور اگر وقت کے اندر مسافر نے مقیم کی اقتداء کی تو پوری چار رکعت پڑھے۔ کیونکہ تابع ہونے کی وجہ سے مسافر کا فریضہ چار رکعت کی طرف متغیر ہو جاتا ہے جیسے اقامت کی نیت سے متغیر ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ متغیر کرنے والا سب یعنی وقت کے ساتھ متصل ہو گیا ہے۔ تشریح یہاں نے دو باتوں کا حکم بیان کیا گیا ہے ایک مسافر کا مقیم کی اقتداء کرنے کا حکم، دوم مقیم کا مسافر کی اقتداء کا حکم ۔ پہلی صورت وقت کے اندر تو جائز ہے لیکن وقت نکلنے کے بعد جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور دوسری صورت وقت کے اندر بھی جائز ہے اور وقت کے بعد بھی۔ صاحب قدوری نے پہلی صورت کو بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ اگر مسافر نے وقت کے اندر مقیم کی اقتداء کی یعنی رباعی ادا نماز میں مسافر نے مقیم کی اقتداء کی تو مسافر پوری چار رکعت پڑھے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسافر نے اس شخص کی متابعت کا التزام کیا ہے جس کی فرض نماز چار رکعت ہیں اور جو شخص اس کی متابعت کا التزام کرے جس کا فریضہ چار رکعت ہیں تو تابع ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کا فریضہ چار رکعت کی طرف متبدل ہو جائے گا۔ جس طرح اقامت کی نیت سے مسافر کا فریضہ چار رکعت کی طرف متبدل ہو جاتا ہے۔ لاتصال المغير سے علت جامعہ کا بیان ہے۔ یعنی یہاں جامع موجود ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ مغیر ( دورکعت کو چار میں تبدیل کرنے والا ) سبب کے ساتھ متصل ہے۔ چنانچہ مغیر ، اول میں اقتداء ہے جو سبب لینی وقت کے ساتھ متصل ہے جیسا کہ ثانی کے اندر مغیر یعنی نیست اقامت سبب یعنی وقت کے ساتھ متصل - ا ہے۔
The ruling of a traveler following a resident [imam]. And if the traveler follows the resident in time [i.e., on-time prayer], he completes four, because his obligatory duty changes to four due to following, just as it changes by the intention of residence, because the changer is connected to the cause, which is time. Translation: And if during the time the traveler follows the resident, he prays four complete rakats. Because due to being a follower, the traveler's obligation changes to four rakats, just as it changes with the intention of residence, because the changer has become connected to the cause, i.e., time. Explanation: Here the ruling of two things has been stated: one, the ruling of a traveler following a resident; two, the ruling of a resident following a traveler. The first case is permissible during the time, but not after the time expires. And the second case is permissible both during and after the time. Imam Quduri, stating the first case, said: If the traveler follows a resident during the time, i.e., in a four-rakat on-time prayer, then the traveler will pray four complete rakats. The proof is that the traveler has undertaken to follow a person whose obligatory prayer is four rakats, and whoever undertakes to follow the one whose obligation is four rakats, then due to being a follower his obligation changes to four rakats. Just as the traveler's obligation changes to four rakats by the intention of residence. 'Because of the connection of the changer to the cause' is a statement of the comprehensive cause. That is, here the comprehensive [cause] exists. It is that the changer (the one who changes two into four) is connected to the cause. Thus, in the first, the changer is the following, which is connected to the cause, i.e., time, just as in the second the changer, i.e., the intention of residence, is connected to the cause, i.e., time.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of al-Quduri, expanded by the commentator. The ruling states that if a traveler (musafir) prays behind a resident imam (muqeem) in an on-time four-rakat prayer, the traveler must complete four rakats. The reason (ta'lil) is the principle of tabi'iyyah (following): the traveler's obligation transforms to four rakats because he has bound himself to follow an imam whose obligation is four rakats. This change is analogous to the change that occurs when a traveler intends to reside (niyyat al-iqamah) at a place, which also converts a traveler's prayer from two to four rakats. The analogy is based on the common 'illa (effective cause): both the following (iqtida') and the intention of residence are 'changers' (mughtayyir) that are connected to the cause (sabab), which is the time of prayer. The commentator explains two aspects: the traveler following a resident (which is valid only within the prayer time) and the resident following a traveler (valid both within and after the time). This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may have different views on whether the traveler must complete four.

Key Terms
مقیم (muqeem): A person who is not a traveler, i.e., a resident who intends to stay in his homeland permanently or for more than a certain period (15 days in Hanafi law).
تابعیت (tabi'iyyah): The principle of following; here it means that the traveler's obligation follows that of the imam.
اقتداء (iqtida'): The act of following an imam in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the traveler must follow the imam's obligation due to tabi'iyyah, and the imam's fard is four rakats.
C) Because the prayer is a make-up (qada) prayer.
D) Because the traveler is actually a resident.

Key Takeaway
A traveler who prays behind a resident imam in an on-time four-rakat prayer must complete four rakats because the principle of tabi'iyyah changes his obligation to match the imam's.
