Traveler Following Resident Imam in Missed Prayer: Ruling and Reasoning
Ruling that traveler cannot follow resident imam in a missed (qada) prayer, with detailed reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a traveler following a resident imam in a missed (qada) prayer and explain the reasoning based on the expiry of cause and the resulting two corruptions.

Core Idea
After prayer time expires, the traveler's obligation is fixed; following a resident imam leads to impermissible fard-behind-nafl prayer.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific yet important scenario: a traveler who has missed a four-rakat prayer wishes to make it up (qada) by following a resident imam who is praying that same prayer on time. The Hanafi school rules that this following is invalid. The reasoning delves into the interplay of cause (sabab), time (waqt), and the changer (iqtida'), culminating in an explanation of two inevitable defects that corrupt the prayer. Let us walk through the legal logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act: a traveler enters prayer behind a resident imam in a missed (qada) four-rakat fard prayer. Ruling: This following is not permissible (haram) and invalidates the prayer.
2
Locate the cause and its expiry
The cause (sabab) that allows the traveler's obligation to change from two to four rakats is the prescribed time (waqt). In qada, the time has passed, so the cause is absent. Therefore, the changer (iqtida') cannot function.
The passage compares this to the intention of residence (niyyat al-iqamah), which also cannot change a qada prayer.
3
Apply the qiyas
Just as qada prayer does not change by intending residence (which normally changes a traveler's prayer), it does not change by following a resident imam. The analogy shows that after time, any changer is ineffective.
The dalil is a qiyas: the original case is on-time prayer where change is possible; the new case is qada where change does not occur.
4
Trace the two possible corruptions
If the traveler says salam after two rakats, he opposes the imam (invalidates). If he stays until four, two subcases arise: (a) he followed from start → his sitting after two is his final sitting (fard) but imam's first sitting (nafl), making fard follow nafl; (b) he joined in last two rakats → imam's recitation is nafl, his is fard, again fard follows nafl.
Both subcases yield the impermissible situation of a fard-performer following a nafl-performer.
5
Conclude the ruling
Since every possible outcome leads to corruption (either opposing imam or fard-behind-nafl), the iqtida' of a traveler behind a resident imam in qada prayer is categorically invalid.
This ruling is specific to the traveler; a resident making up a missed prayer behind another resident is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسافر کے لئے فوت شدہ نماز کی اقتداء کا حکم
وأن دخل معه في فائتة لم تجزه لانه لا يتغير بعد الوقت لانقضاء السبب كما لا تتغير بنية الاق فيكون اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل في حق القعدة او القراءة
ترجمہ اور اگر مسافر مقیم کے ساتھ کسی فائینہ نماز میں داخل ہوا تو جائز نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مسافر کا فریضہ وقت کے بعد متغیر نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ سبب تو گذر چکا۔ جیسے (قضاء نماز) نیت اقامت سے نہیں بدلتی تو قعدہ یا قرآت کے حق میں مفترض کا متحمل کی اقتدادہ کرنا لازم آئے گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مسافر نے اگر قضاء نماز کے اندر مقیم کی اقتداء کی تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ وقت گذرنے کے بعد مسافر کا در ہے متغیر پیش ہو گا اس لئے کہ فرض نماز کا سب تو وقت ہے اور اقتدا ، اجو تغیر دیتا ہے، وہ سبب سے متصل ہو کر کار آمد ہوتا ہے اور چونکہ قضاء نماز میں سبب یعنی وقت گذر جانے کی وجہ سے یہ اتصال نہیں پایا گیا۔ اس لئے مسافر کا فرض دو رکعت سے چار رکعت کی طرف متبدل بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ قضاء نماز نیت اقامت سے نہیں بدلتی حالانکہ نیت اقامت بھی دور کعت کو چار رکعت میں تبدیل کرنے والی ہے فیکون اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل الخ سے ماقبل کا نتیجہ مذکور ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ وقت نماز نکلنے کے بعد اگر مسافر نے رباعی قضاء نماز میں مقیم کی اقتداء کی تو دوخرابیوں میں سے ایک خرابی ضروری لازم آئے گی۔ یا تو اپنے امام کی مخالفت کرنا لازم آئے گا۔ یا اقتداء مفترض با مقفل لازم آئے گا اس لئے کہ مسافر نے اگر قضاء رباعی نماز میں مقیم کی اقتداء کی تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ مسافر مقتدی دورکعت پر سلام پھرے گا یا چار پڑا اگر مسافر نے دور کعت پر سلام پھیر دیا تو وہ اپنے امام کے مخالف ہوا۔ اور مخالفت امام مفسد نماز ہے۔ اور اگر مسافر آخر تک امام کے ساتھ شریک رہا تو اب اس کی بھی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ مسافر نے شروع ہی سے اقتداء کی ہے یا آخر کی دورکعتوں میں اگر اول صورت ہے تو دورکعت پر قعدہ مسافر کے حق میں فرض ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اس کے حق میں یہ قعدہ اخیرہ ہے۔ اور امام مقیم کے حق میں فرض نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کے حق میں یہ قعدہ اولیٰ ہے اور قعدہ اولیٰ فرض نہیں ہوتا۔ پس اس صورت میں قعدہ کے حق میں فرضی ادا کرنے والا نفل ادا کرنے والے کا مقتدی ہوگا اور اگر آخرکی دورکعتوں میں اقتداء کی گئی ہے تو آخر میں امام یعنی مقیم کی قرآت نفل ہے اور مقتدی یعنی مسافر کی فرض ہے۔ پس اس صورت میں قرآت کے حق میں فرض ادا کرنے والے کا نفل ادا کرنے والے کی اقتداء کرنا لازم آئے گا۔ اور یہ امر مسلم ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک اقتداء مفترض بالمتفل نا جائز ہے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ وقت نکل جانے کے بعد مسافر کو مقیم کا مقتدی بننے میں جب دونوں صورتوں میں فساد ہے تو وقت کے بعد یہ اقتداء ہی جائز نہ ہوگی۔
The ruling of following a missed prayer for the traveler. And if he enters with him in a missed prayer, it is not permissible for him, because he does not change after the time due to the expiry of the cause, just as it does not change by the intention of residence. Then it would be the following of an obligation-performer by a supererogatory-performer with respect to the sitting or the recitation. Translation: And if the traveler enters with the resident in a missed prayer, it is not permissible. Because the traveler's obligation will not change after the time, since the cause has passed. Just as (in qada prayer) it does not change by the intention of residence, then it becomes necessary for the obligation-performer to follow the supererogatory-performer regarding the sitting or recitation. Explanation: The issue is that if the traveler follows the resident in qada prayer, it is not permissible, because after the time passes, the traveler's obligation will not change, since the cause of the obligatory prayer is time, and the following, which causes change, works by being connected to the cause. And since in qada prayer the cause, i.e., time, has passed, this connection is not found. Therefore, the traveler's obligation will not change from two rakats to four. Just as qada prayer does not change with the intention of residence, even though the intention of residence also changes two to four. Then the consequence mentioned before is 'fa yakuunu iqtida' al-muftarid bi al-mutanafill' etc. The conclusion is that after the time of prayer expires, if a traveler follows a resident in a four-rakat qada prayer, one of two defects will necessarily occur: either opposition to his imam, which invalidates the prayer, or following of a supererogatory performer by an obligatory performer. If the traveler follower says salam after two rakats, he opposes his imam, which invalidates the prayer. If he stays with the imam to the end, then there are two subcases. If he followed from the beginning, then sitting after two rakats is obligatory for the traveler (as his final sitting) but not for the resident imam (as his first sitting), so a fard-performer follows a nafl-performer regarding sitting. If he started following in the last two rakats, then the imam's recitation is nafl while the follower's is fard, again leading to a fard-performer following a nafl-performer. Since this is not permissible in our school, such following is invalid.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage explains a second ruling: a traveler cannot validly follow a resident imam in a missed (qada) prayer after the prayer time has expired. The reason is that the change of obligation (from two to four rakats) depends on the changer (iqtida' or niyyat al-iqamah) being connected to the cause (the prescribed time). In qada prayer, the time has passed, so the connection is lost. The commentator elaborates that if the traveler tries to follow, two corruptions result: either he opposes the imam by ending prayer early, or he ends up in a situation where he (as fard-performer) follows the imam (as nafl-performer), which is impermissible in the Hanafi school. Thus, such iqtida' is invalid.

Key Terms
فائتہ (fa'itah): A missed prayer that is being made up (qada).
متنفل (mutanaffil): One performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid for a traveler to follow a resident imam in a missed (qada) prayer?
A) Because the traveler must pray qada alone.
B) Because the prayer time has passed, so the changer (iqtida') is not connected to the cause, leading to an impermissible following of a nafl performer.
C) Because the resident imam cannot lead a missed prayer.
D) Because the traveler must intend residence first.

Key Takeaway
A traveler cannot validly follow a resident imam in a missed prayer because the expired time severs the changer's effect, inevitably causing corruption.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Why a Traveler Cannot Follow a Resident in Qada Prayer: The Two-Corruption Proof
Ruling with rational proof on traveler following resident in qada prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain, step by step, why a traveler's iqtida of a resident in qada prayer after the time is invalid, and identify the two scenarios that lead to corruption.

Core Idea
Following a resident in qada prayer forces either opposition to the imam or a muftarid following a mutanafifil — both invalid.

This passage from Al-Hidayah unpacks a subtle rule about the traveler's prayer. After the time for a prayer has passed, the traveler's obligation remains two rak'ahs, but his imam (a resident) is praying four. The author shows how this mismatch creates an inevitable corruption, establishing that such iqtida is impermissible.

Guided Path
1
Understand the baseline
A traveler's fard is 2 rak'ahs; a resident's is 4. For qada, the traveler's prayer is not altered by intending residence later. This is the foundation.
The traveler's obligation is fixed at 2 rak'ahs even if he later becomes a resident, because the prayer is linked to the time it was due.
2
Identify the two possible outcomes
When a traveler follows a resident in a 4-rak'ah qada prayer, either the traveler says salam after 2 rak'ahs and opposes the imam, or he stays for all 4 rak'ahs, creating a mismatch in obligation levels.
There is no third option; this exhausts the possibilities.
3
Analyze the first outcome: opposition
If the traveler says salam after 2 rak'ahs, he has opposed his imam by ending early. Opposing the imam deliberately invalidates the prayer (mufsid).
This is a known rule: the muqtadi must follow the imam in actions; deliberate opposition breaks the congregation and the prayer.
4
Analyze the second outcome: muftarid following mutanafifil
If the traveler stays for all 4 rak'ahs, two subcases arise: (a) he followed from the start, then the sitting after 2 rak'ahs is fard for him (his final sitting) but nafl for the imam (first sitting); (b) he joined in the last two rak'ahs, then the imam's recitation is nafl for himself but fard for the traveler. In both subcases, a muftarid follows a mutanafifil, which is impermissible.
The Hanafi principle that a muftarid cannot follow a mutanafifil is a settled rule (mas'alah musallamah).
5
Conclude the ruling
Since both possible outcomes lead to corruption, the iqtida itself is invalid. Therefore, the traveler must pray his qada alone, as two rak'ahs.
This ruling applies specifically after the time has passed; during the time, the traveler's prayer is 2 rak'ahs and he can follow a resident? Actually, during the time, the traveler is performing ada (on-time) prayer, and his fard is 2, so following a resident would still have the same issue. But here the focus is on qada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة المسافر
نماز میں سبب یعنی وقت گذر جانے کی وجہ سے یہ اتصال نہیں پایا گیا۔ اس لئے مسافر کا فرض دو رکعت سے چار رکعت کی طرف متبدل بھی نہیں ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ قضاء نماز نیت اقامت سے نہیں بدلتی حالانکہ نیت اقامت بھی دور کعت کو چار رکعت میں تبدیل کرنے والی ہے فیکون اقتداء المفترض بالمتنفل الخ سے ماقبل کا نتیجہ مذکور ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ وقت نماز نکلنے کے بعد اگر مسافر نے رباعی قضاء نماز میں مقیم کی اقتداء کی تو دوخرابیوں میں سے ایک خرابی ضروری لازم آئے گی۔ یا تو اپنے امام کی مخالفت کرنا لازم آئے گا۔ یا اقتداء مفترض با مقفل لازم آئے گا اس لئے کہ مسافر نے اگر قضاء رباعی نماز میں مقیم کی اقتداء کی تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ مسافر مقتدی دورکعت پر سلام پھرے گا یا چار پڑا اگر مسافر نے دور کعت پر سلام پھیر دیا تو وہ اپنے امام کے مخالف ہوا۔ اور مخالفت امام مفسد نماز ہے۔ اور اگر مسافر آخر تک امام کے ساتھ شریک رہا تو اب اس کی بھی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ مسافر نے شروع ہی سے اقتداء کی ہے یا آخر کی دورکعتوں میں اگر اول صورت ہے تو دورکعت پر قعدہ مسافر کے حق میں فرض ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اس کے حق میں یہ قعدہ اخیرہ ہے۔ اور امام مقیم کے حق میں فرض نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کے حق میں یہ قعدہ اولیٰ ہے اور قعدہ اولیٰ فرض نہیں ہوتا۔ پس اس صورت میں قعدہ کے حق میں فرضی ادا کرنے والا نفل ادا کرنے والے کا مقتدی ہوگا اور اگر آخرکی دورکعتوں میں اقتداء کی گئی ہے تو آخر میں امام یعنی مقیم کی قرآت نفل ہے اور مقتدی یعنی مسافر کی فرض ہے۔ پس اس صورت میں قرآت کے حق میں فرض ادا کرنے والے کا نفل ادا کرنے والے کی اقتداء کرنا لازم آئے گا۔ اور یہ امر مسلم ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک اقتداء مفترض بالمتفل نا جائز ہے۔
حاصل یہ ہے کہ وقت نکل جانے کے بعد مسافر کو مقیم کا مقتدی بننے میں جب دونوں صورتوں میں فساد ہے تو وقت کے بعد یہ اقتداء ہی جائز نہ ہوگی۔
Chapter of the traveler's prayer. In prayer, due to the cause—that is, the passing of the time—this connection was not found. Therefore, the traveler's obligatory (prayer) will not change from two rak'ahs to four rak'ahs. Just as the qada prayer does not change by the intention of residence, even though the intention of residence also changes two rak'ahs into four. So the phrase 'fikun iqtida' al-muftarid bi al-mutanafifil' etc. is the conclusion of what came before. The gist is that after the time of prayer has passed, if a traveler follows a resident in a four-rak'ah qada prayer, then one of two corruptions will necessarily occur: either he must oppose his imam, or the iqtida of a muftarid (obligation-performer) by a mutanafifil (optional-performer) becomes necessary. This is because if the traveler follows a resident in a four-rak'ah qada prayer, there are two possibilities. The traveler muqtadi will say salam after two rak'ahs or pray four. If the traveler says salam after two rak'ahs, he opposed his imam, and opposing the imam invalidates the prayer. And if the traveler remains with the imam until the end, then there are two possibilities: the traveler followed from the beginning or followed in the last two rak'ahs. If the first case, then the sitting (qa'dah) after two rak'ahs is fard for the traveler because it is his final sitting, and it is not fard for the resident imam because it is his first sitting, and the first sitting is not fard. So in this case, in terms of sitting, one performing fard is following one performing nafl. And if the following occurred in the last two rak'ahs, then in the end, the recitation of the imam (the resident) is nafl and the recitation of the muqtadi (the traveler) is fard. So in this case, in terms of recitation, it becomes necessary for the one performing fard to follow one performing nafl. And it is a settled matter that, according to us, the iqtida of a muftarid by a mutanafifil is not permissible. The gist is that when both cases contain corruption after the time has passed, then this iqtida is not permissible at all after the time.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with reasoning (talil) explaining why a traveler (musafir) cannot validly follow a resident (muqim) in qada prayer after the time has expired. The author first notes that the traveler's obligatory prayer does not increase from two to four rak'ahs even if he intends residence, because the qada prayer is not altered by such intent. Then, he presents the core problem: if a traveler follows a resident in a qada four-rak'ah prayer, two cases arise, both leading to corruption. In the first case, the traveler says salam after two rak'ahs, thereby opposing his imam, which invalidates the prayer. In the second case, he stays with the imam for all four rak'ahs, but then either he follows the imam in a sitting that is fard for the traveler but nafl for the imam, or he follows the imam in recitation that is fard for the traveler but nafl for the imam. Both situations result in a follower performing fard following someone performing nafl, which is impermissible in the Hanafi school. The conclusion is that this iqtida is invalid after the time.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in prayer; the act of being a muqtadi.
مفترض (muftarid): One who is performing an obligatory prayer (fard).
متنفل (mutanafifil): One who is performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a traveler follows a resident in qada prayer from the beginning, which act becomes fard for the traveler but not for the imam?
A) Qira'ah (recitation)
B) Qa'dah (sitting after two rak'ahs)
C) Salam
D) Takbir al-tahrimah

Key Takeaway
A traveler cannot follow a resident in qada prayer after the time because it inevitably leads to either opposition to the imam or a muftarid following a mutanafifil — both corrupt the prayer.

A Traveler Leading Residents in Prayer and the Ruling on the Muqtadi
Ruling on a traveler as imam for residents and the muqtadi's obligation after salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a traveler leading residents in prayer and explain why the muqtadi (lahiq) does not recite in the remaining rak'ahs, distinguishing him from the masbuq.

Core Idea
A traveler can lead residents; the muqtadi (lahiq) does not recite in the remaining rak'ahs because his fard recitation is complete.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary establishes two key rulings: the permissibility of a traveler (musafir) acting as imam for residents (muqimin), and the specific obligation of the resident muqtadi after the imam's salam. The central point is the distinction between a lahiq and a masbuq, which determines whether the muqtadi must recite the Qur'an in the remaining rak'ahs. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and the proof from the Prophet's practice during the conquest of Makkah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a traveler leading residents in a two-rak'ah prayer. The ruling is that it is permissible, and after salam, residents complete their prayer individually.
The passage assumes the traveler is praying a shortened prayer (qasr) of two rak'ahs.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn about the Prophet in Makkah, who prayed two rak'ahs and told residents to complete their prayer.
This hadith is reported by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of praying two rak'ahs and his command 'Complete your prayer' prove the permissibility of the traveler leading and indicate the recommended statement after salam.
The statement 'We are travelers' becomes the basis for the mustahabb phrase.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion: the more correct view (asah) is that the muqtadi does not recite in the remaining rak'ahs, unlike a masbuq.
The opposing view, if any, is not detailed but is implied by the choice of 'asah'.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The preferred view is based on the distinction between lahiq and masbuq; the muqtadi's fard recitation is already fulfilled, so recitation is abandoned out of caution.
The lahiq is defined as one who is a follower in tahrima but not in action after salam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان صلى المسافر بالمقيمين ركعتين سلم واتم المقيمون صلاتهم لان المقتدى التزم الموافقة في الركعتين فينفرد في الباقي كالمسبوق الا انه لا يقرأ فى الاصح لانه مقتد تحريمة لا فعلا والفرض صار مؤدى فيتركها احتياطا بخلاف المسبوق لانه ادرك قراءة نافلة فلم يتأدى الفرض فكان الايتان اولى
ترجمہ اگر مسافر نے مقیموں کو دورکعت نماز پڑھائی تو امام مسافر سلام پھیر دے اور مقیم لوگ اپنی نماز پوری کرلیں۔ کیونکہ مقتدی نے دو رکعت میں موافقت کا التزام کیا ہے تو باقی دو رکعت میں وہ مسبوق کی مانند دے۔ اور مقیم لوگ اپنی نماز پوری کر لیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقیم مقتدی نے امام کو مسافر جان کر دو رکعت میں موافقت کا التزام کیا تھا۔ اور جس کا التزام کیا تھا وہ ادا کر چکا۔ حالانکہ مقیم مقتدی کی نماز ابھی پوری نہیں ہوئی ہے اس لئے مقیم مقتدی باقی دو رکعتوں میں منفرد ہوگا۔ جیسے امام کے سلام پھیرنے کے بعد مسبوق منفرد ہوتا ہے مگر ان دونوں میں اتنا فرق ہے کہ مقیم مقتدی اصح قول کی بناء پر ان رکعتوں میں قرآت متبدل بھی نہیں کرے گا۔ جو مسافر امام کے سلام پھیرنے کے بعد پڑھتا ہے اور مسبوق قرآت کرتا ہے۔ قول اصبح کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقیم آخر کی دو ہے فيكون رکعتوں میں تحریمہ کے اعتبار سے مقتدی ہے۔ لیکن فعل کے اعتبار سے مقتدی نہیں ہے۔ تحریمہ کے اعتبار سے تو مقتدی اس لئے ہے کہ اس نماز میں مقیم نے اول تحریمہ میں امام کے ساتھ ادا کرنے کا التزام کیا ہے۔ اور فعل کے اعتبار سے مقتدی اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ دورکعت پر سلام کے ذریعہ رض بالمتحفل امام مسافر کا فعل ختم ہو چکا ہے۔ اور جو شخص ایسا ہو یعنی تحریمہ کے اعتبار سے مقتدی اور فعل کے اعتبار سے غیر مقتدی تو وہ لاحق کہلاتا ہے۔ سلام پھرے اور لاحق پر قرآت نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ تحریمہ کے اعتبار سے اس کے مقتدی ہونے پر نظر کی جائے تو اس پر قرآت کر نا حرام ہوگا اور اگر فعل کے اعتبار سے غیر مقتدی ہونے پر نظر کی جائے تو اس کے لئے قرآت کرنا مستحب ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ جن پہلی دو رکعتوں میں قرآت فرض تھی وہ ادا ہو چکی ہے حاصل یہ کہ آخیر کی دورکعتوں میں مقیم مقتدی کے لئے قرآت کرنا حرام اور مستحب کے درمیان دائر ہے۔ پس حرام کو ترجیح تی نہیں ہے دیتے ہوئے احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ مقیم مقتدی آخر کی دورکعتوں میں قراۃ چھوڑ دے۔ برخلاف مسبوق کے۔ یہاں مسبوق سے مراد وہ والا نفل ادا مسبوق ہے جس کو بائی نماز میں پہلی دور کعتیں امام کے ساتھ نہیں مل سکیں بلکہ آخر کی دورکعتوں میں امام کے ساتھ شریک ہوا۔ بہر حال امام کے سلام پھیرنے کے بعد مسبوق جب اپنی قوت شدہ دور کعتیں پڑھے گا۔ تو اس پر ان میں قرآت کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ نہ اور یہ امر کیونکہ مسبوق نے آخر کی دورکعتوں میں امام کی جو قرآت پائی ہے دو نفل قرآت ہے اور پہلی دو رکعتوں میں جو مفروضہ قرآت تھی اس کو ابھی تک ادا نہیں کر سکا۔ اس لئے مسبوق پر قرآت کرنا واجب ہوگا ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
صورت ہے
یعنی مسافر
حدید اقتداء
مسافر امام کے لئے اتموا صلاتكم فانا قوم سطر کہنا مستحب ہے
قال ويستحب للامام اذا سلم ان يقول المواصلاتكم فانا قوم سفر لانه عليه السلام قاله حين صلى باهل
مكة وهو مساف
افقة في ترجمہ اور امام کے لئے مستحب یہ ہے کہ جب وہ سلام پھیر نے تو یوں کہے کہ تم لوگ اپنی نماز پوری کولو ہم تو مسافر قوم ہیں کیونکہ حضور ار مؤدی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جس وقت اہل مکہ کو نماز پڑھائی درانحالیکہ آپ مسافر تھے تو یہی فرمایا تھا۔ نان اولی تشریح امام اگر مسافر ہوتو دورکعت پر سلام پھیرنے کے بعد مقتدیوں سے یوں کہے آپ حضرات اپنی نماز پوری کر لیں میں تو مسافر مقتدی نے ہوں۔ دلیل ابو داؤد اور ترمذی کی روایت کردہ حدیث ہے عن عمران حصین رضی الله تعالى عنه قال غزوت مع رسول ۔ کیونکہ وہ اللہ صلی الله عليه وسلم وشهدت معه الفتح فاقام بمكة ثمان عشر ليلة لا يصلي الأركعتين يقول يا اهل مكه سبوق کے صلوا اربعاً فان اقول سفر عمران بن حصین کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم کے ساتھ غزوہ کیا آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ساتھ فتح مکہ میں شریک رہا۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اٹھارہ رات مکتہ المکرمہ میں قیام فرمایا۔ اس عرصہ میں آپ (رباعی نماز ) میں فقط دو رکعت
دے۔ اور پڑھتے اور فرمایا کرتے اے مکہ والو! تم چار رکعت ہی پڑھو میں تو مسافر ہوں ۔ کا التزام فائدہ قدوری کی عبارت سے ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ یہ شرط نہیں ہے کہ نماز شروع کرنے سے پہلے مقتدی کو امام کے مسافر یا مقیم ہونے کا علم ے امام کے ہو اس لئے کہ اگر مقتدیوں کو امام کے مسافر ہونے کا علم پہلے سے ہے تو سلام پھیرنے کے بعد امام مسافر کا قول اتــمـواصـلا تـكم بث اں قرآت ہے۔ اور اگر اس کے مقیم ہونے کا علم ہے تو مسافر اپنے قول انا قوم سفر میں کا ذب ہوگا۔
And if a traveler leads residents, he prays two rak'ahs and says salam, and the residents complete their prayer, because the muqtadi committed to following in the two rak'ahs, so he becomes alone in the remaining (rak'ahs) like a masbuq, except that according to the more correct view, he does not recite, because he is a muqtadi in terms of the tahrima (opening takbir) not in terms of action, and the obligatory (recitation) has been performed, so he leaves it out of caution, unlike the masbuq because he caught a nafl recitation and the fard recitation has not been performed, so recitation is better. Translation: If a traveler leads residents in a two-rak'ah prayer, then the traveler imam says salam and the residents complete their prayer. Because the muqtadi committed to following in the two rak'ahs, so in the remaining two rak'ahs he will be alone like a masbuq, but according to the more correct view, he should not recite, because he is a muqtadi in terms of tahrima, not in terms of action, and the fard has been performed, so he leaves recitation out of caution, unlike the masbuq because the masbuq caught a nafl recitation and has not yet performed the fard recitation, so recitation is preferable. Explanation: The situation is that if residents follow a traveler, the traveler prays two rak'ahs, sits for tashahhud, then says salam. The residents then complete their prayer. The proof is that the resident muqtadi committed to following only in two rak'ahs knowing the imam is a traveler, and that commitment has been fulfilled. So the resident muqtadi will be alone in the remaining two rak'ahs, like a masbuq after the imam's salam, but with the difference that the resident muqtadi, according to the more correct view, does not recite in those rak'ahs. The proof of the more correct view is that the resident in the last two rak'ahs is a muqtadi in terms of tahrima but not in terms of action. He is a muqtadi in terms of tahrima because he committed to following the imam in the opening takbir; he is not a muqtadi in terms of action because the imam's action (prayer) has ended with the salam. One who is a muqtadi in tahrima but not in action is called a lahiq. The lahiq does not recite because if we consider his status as muqtadi in tahrima, recitation would be haram for him, and if we consider his status as non-muqtadi in action, recitation would be mustahabb for him. Since the fard recitation in the first two rak'ahs has been performed, the matter is between haram and mustahabb, so caution is to leave recitation. Unlike the masbuq, who caught a nafl recitation and has not yet performed the fard recitation, so recitation is wajib for him. And Allah knows best. The picture is: the traveler imam. It is mustahabb for the traveler imam to say after salam: 'Complete your prayer, for we are a traveling people.' He (peace be upon him) said this when he prayed with the people of Makkah while he was a traveler. Translation: It is mustahabb for the imam, when he says salam, to say: 'Complete your prayer, for we are a traveling people,' because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said this when he prayed with the people of Makkah while he was a traveler. The benefit: It appears from the text of Quduri that it is not a condition that the muqtadi know before starting the prayer whether the imam is a traveler or resident, because if the muqtadis know beforehand that the imam is a traveler, then after salam the traveler imam's statement 'Complete your prayer' is recitation (of the ruling), and if they know he is a resident, then the traveler's statement 'We are traveling' would be a lie.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage contains two main rulings: first, it establishes that a traveler (musafir) can validly lead residents (muqimin) in prayer. The imam prays two rak'ahs and says salam. The residents then complete their prayer individually. The reasoning is that the muqtadi committed to following the imam only for the two rak'ahs, after which they become independent. Second, it details the difference between such a muqtadi and a masbuq (one who missed part of the prayer). The muqtadi here is called a lahiq: he is a follower by virtue of the opening takbir but not by action after the imam's salam. The ruling for the lahiq is that he should not recite in the remaining rak'ahs, unlike the masbuq, because the fard recitation has already been performed and recitation would be between haram and mustahabb, so it is left out of caution. The passage also mentions a mustahabb (recommended) action: after salam, the imam should say to the congregation, 'Complete your prayer, for we are travelers,' based on the Prophet's practice during the conquest of Makkah. Finally, it notes that it is not necessary for the muqtadis to know the imam's status beforehand, as this would cause contradiction.

Key Terms
لاحق (lahiq): A muqtadi who followed the imam in the opening takbir but whose prayer is not completed with the imam's salam, becoming separate in action.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who missed one or more rak'ahs with the imam and must make them up after the imam's salam.
تحریمہ (tahrima): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) which initiates the prayer and establishes the connection between imam and muqtadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should the resident muqtadi do after the traveler imam says salam following two rak'ahs?
A) He says salam as well and ends his prayer.
B) He completes two more rak'ahs with recitation.
C) He completes two more rak'ahs without recitation.
D) He waits for another imam.

Key Takeaway
A traveler can lead residents in prayer; after the imam's salam, the resident muqtadi completes his prayer without recitation because his fard recitation is already fulfilled.

Recitation for a Resident Muqtadi Behind a Traveling Imam
Ruling on recitation for a resident muqtadi behind a traveling imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qira'ah for a resident muqtadi in the last two rak'ahs behind a traveling imam, distinguish between lahiq and masbuq, and explain the rational proof based on tahrimah vs. action.

Core Idea
For a resident muqtadi, recitation in the last two rak'ahs is omitted out of caution between haram and mustahab.

When a resident follower prays behind a traveling imam who shortens the prayer, a nuanced situation arises regarding recitation in the final two rak'ahs. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, which distinguishes between two categories of followers: the lahiq (who started with the imam) and the masbuq (who joined late). The ruling is built on a careful analysis of the follower's connection to the imam through the opening takbir (tahrimah) versus separation in action after the imam's salam. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the correct ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the specific situation: a resident (muqim) is praying behind a traveling imam who prays only two rak'ahs. The question is whether the resident muqtadi should recite Qur'an in the last two rak'ahs (the imam's second two, which the follower performs after the imam's salam).
This is not the case of a masbuq joining late; the resident started with the imam.
2
Distinguish lahiq from masbuq
The text introduces two types of followers: lahiq (one who began with the imam but whose action is now separate because the imam finished) and masbuq (one who missed one or more rak'ahs and will make them up after the imam's salam). Understand their different rulings on recitation.
The lahiq is bound by the tahrimah but not by the imam's ongoing action.
3
Analyze the dual perspective
The proof is based on viewing the lahiq from two angles: (a) due to tahrimah, he is still a muqtadi, so recitation would be haram (since muqtadi must not recite behind the imam); (b) due to action, he is separate, so recitation would be mustahab (since he is now praying alone).
This conflict of perspectives drives the ruling.
4
Derive the ruling of caution
Because recitation is caught between haram and mustahab, the preferred course is caution (ihtiyat): omitting recitation. Hence it is makruh tanzih to recite in the last two rak'ahs for the lahiq. Contrast this with the masbuq, who must recite in his missed rak'ahs because the recitation he heard was supererogatory.
The masbuq's obligation is wajib, not optional.
5
Apply the distinction
Now practice: given a scenario of a resident behind a traveling imam, determine whether the follower is a lahiq or masbuq and state the correct ruling on recitation.
Check if the follower joined after the first rak'ah or from the beginning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلوة المسافر
متبدل بھی نہیں کرے گا۔ جو مسافر امام کے سلام پھیرنے کے بعد پڑھتا ہے اور مسبوق قرآت کرتا ہے۔ قول اصبح کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقیم آخر کی دو ہے فيكون ركعتوں میں تحریمہ کے اعتبار سے مقتدی ہے۔ لیکن فعل کے اعتبار سے مقتدی نہیں ہے۔ تحریمہ کے اعتبار سے تو مقتدی اس لئے ہے کہ اس نماز میں مقیم نے اول تحریمہ میں امام کے ساتھ ادا کرنے کا التزام کیا ہے۔ اور فعل کے اعتبار سے مقتدی اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ دورکعت پر سلام کے ذریعہ رض بالمتحفل امام مسافر کا فعل ختم ہو چکا ہے۔ اور جو شخص ایسا ہو یعنی تحریمہ کے اعتبار سے مقتدی اور فعل کے اعتبار سے غیر مقتدی تو وہ لاحق کہلاتا ہے۔ سلام پھرے اور لاحق پر قرآت نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ تحریمہ کے اعتبار سے اس کے مقتدی ہونے پر نظر کی جائے تو اس پر قرآت کر نا حرام ہوگا اور اگر فعل کے اعتبار سے غیر مقتدی ہونے پر نظر کی جائے تو اس کے لئے قرآت کرنا مستحب ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ جن پہلی دو رکعتوں میں قرآت فرض تھی وہ ادا ہو چکی ہے حاصل یہ کہ آخیر کی دورکعتوں میں مقیم مقتدی کے لئے قرآت کرنا حرام اور مستحب کے درمیان دائر ہے۔ پس حرام کو ترجیح تی نہیں ہے دیتے ہوئے احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ مقیم مقتدی آخر کی دورکعتوں میں قراۃ چھوڑ دے۔ برخلاف مسبوق کے۔ یہاں مسبوق سے مراد وہ والا نفل ادا مسبوق ہے جس کو بائی نماز میں پہلی دور کعتیں امام کے ساتھ نہیں مل سکیں بلکہ آخر کی دورکعتوں میں امام کے ساتھ شریک ہوا۔ بہر حال امام کے سلام پھیرنے کے بعد مسبوق جب اپنی قوت شدہ دور کعتیں پڑھے گا۔ تو اس پر ان میں قرآت کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ نہ اور یہ امر کیونکہ مسبوق نے آخر کی دورکعتوں میں امام کی جو قرآت پائی ہے دو نفل قرآت ہے اور پہلی دو رکعتوں میں جو مفروضہ قرآت تھی اس کو ابھی تک ادا نہیں کر سکا۔ اس لئے مسبوق پر قرآت کرنا واجب ہوگا ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Chapter of the traveler's prayer. He will not change [the prayer]. As for the one who prays after the traveling imam's salam, and the msubuq recites. The proof of the saying of our companions is that the resident in the last two rak'ahs is a muqtadi with respect to the tahrimah but not with respect to action. With respect to tahrimah he is muqtadi because in this prayer the resident undertook to perform the first tahrimah with the imam. And with respect to action he is not muqtadi because the imam's action has ended by salam after two rak'ahs. And a person who is such, i.e., muqtadi with respect to tahrimah and non-muqtadi with respect to action, is called lahiq. He [the imam] performs salam, and recitation is not [required] for the lahiq because if we consider his being muqtadi with respect to tahrimah, recitation for him would be haram, and if we consider his being non-muqtadi with respect to action, recitation for him would be mustahab. Because the recitation that was fard in the first two rak'ahs has already been performed. The conclusion is that recitation for the resident muqtadi in the last two rak'ahs is between haram and mustahab. So, giving precedence to caution, it is that the resident muqtadi should leave recitation in the last two rak'ahs, unlike the msubuq. Here msubuq refers to the one who missed the first two rak'ahs with the imam and joined in the last two rak'ahs. When after the imam's salam he completes his missed rak'ahs, recitation in them is wajib for him. This is because the recitation he heard from the imam in the last two rak'ahs is supererogatory recitation, while the obligatory recitation of the first two rak'ahs he has not yet performed. Therefore recitation is wajib for the msubuq. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil aqli/istihsan) regarding the recitation (qira'ah) of a resident muqtadi when praying behind a traveling imam who only performs two rak'ahs. The text first distinguishes between a lahiq and a msubuq. A lahiq is one who began the prayer with the imam (thus bound by the tahrimah) but whose action is separate because the imam finished before him. The ruling is that the lahiq should not recite in the last two rak'ahs because recitation would be haram from the perspective of being a muqtadi (as the imam's recitation suffices) but mustahab from the perspective of being separate (since he is performing the last two rak'ahs as if alone). To avoid the risk of haram, he should omit recitation; this is caution (ihtiyat). In contrast, a msubuq (one who joined late) must recite in his missed rak'ahs because the recitation he heard from the imam was supererogatory (nafl) and he still owes the obligatory (fard) recitation. The proof is rational: the conflicting considerations lead to preference for omission.

Key Terms
مقتدی (muqtadi): A follower in prayer who intends to pray behind an imam.
لاحق (lahiq): One who caught the prayer with the imam from the beginning but separated due to the imam finishing early or other reason.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joins the congregation after the imam has started and misses one or more rak'ahs.
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir which establishes the prayer and creates the connection with the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a resident muqtadi reciting in the last two rak'ahs when praying behind a traveling imam?
A) It is wajib to recite.
B) It is mustahab to recite.
C) It is better to omit recitation (makruh tanzih).
D) It is haram to recite.

Key Takeaway
The lahiq's dual connection (tahrimah vs. action) creates a conflict that leads to the preferred omission of recitation, while the masbuq's obligation to recite remains wajib.

Recommendation for Traveling Imam to Say 'Ammu Salatakum' After Salam
Ruling with proof: recommendation for traveling imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a traveling imam after salam and explain its proof from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
A traveling imam should recommend followers to complete their prayer after salam, based on the Prophet's practice.

In this lesson, we examine a specific sunnah for the traveling imam: after saying salam, he announces that the followers should pray four rak'ahs because he is a traveler. The passage provides the proof from the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn and clarifies when this announcement is needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended act
Determine what exactly the imam is recommended to do: after salam, say 'Ammu salatakum fainna qawmu safar'.
This is a verbal announcement, not an action.
2
Determine the ruling level
Classify the ruling: mustahab (recommended), which in Hanafi terminology is equivalent to sunnah muakkadah when done consistently by the Prophet.
The evidence shows the Prophet did it consistently, so it is highly recommended.
3
Locate the dalil
Find the proof: the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn where the Prophet stayed in Mecca during the Conquest and prayed two rak'ahs, telling the Meccans to pray four.
This is a hadith ahad (single-chain), so it establishes recommendation, not obligation.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling: the Prophet's consistent action and his explicit command 'pray four' show that this is a recommended practice; his statement 'I am a traveler' indicates the rationale.
The command 'pray four' is directed to the residents, not to the Prophet himself.
5
Consider the benefit from al-Quduri
Al-Quduri clarifies that it is not a condition for the followers to know the imam's travel status before starting the prayer. The imam's statement after salam is sufficient, and if they knew, it confirms; if they thought he was a resident, his statement would be truthful.
This addresses potential confusion about timing and honesty.

Source Text

وقال رحمه الله: ويستحب للامام اذا سلم ان يقول اتموا صلاتكم فانا قوم سفر لانه عليه السلام قاله حين صلى باهل مكة وهو مسافر. ودليله حديث عمران بن حصين رضي الله عنهما قال: غزوت مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وشهدت معه الفتح فاقام بمكة ثمان عشر ليلة لا يصلي الا ركعتين يقول يا اهل مكة صلوا اربعا فانا قوم سفر. فائدة: من عبارة القدوري يظهر انه ليس شرطا ان يعلم المقتدى قبل شروع الصلاة كون الامام مسافرا او مقيما. لانه لو علم المقتدون ان الامام مسافر فقوله اتموا صلاتكم بعد السلام كاف. ولو علموا انه مقيم فقوله انا قوم سفر يكون كذبا.
And he (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: It is recommended for the imam, when he says salam, to say 'Complete your prayer, for we are a traveling group' because the Prophet, peace be upon him, said it when he prayed with the people of Mecca while he was a traveler. Its proof is the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn, may Allah be pleased with them both, who said: 'I went on an expedition with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and witnessed the Conquest with him. He stayed in Mecca for eighteen nights, not praying except two rak'ahs, and he would say: O people of Mecca, pray four, for I am a traveler.' Benefit: From the statement of al-Quduri, it appears that it is not a condition that the followers know before starting the prayer whether the imam is a traveler or a resident. Because if the followers know that the imam is a traveler, his saying 'Complete your prayer' after salam is sufficient. And if they know he is a resident, then his saying 'I am a traveler' would be a lie.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil naqli) stating the recommendation (istihbab) for a traveling imam to announce after the salam that the followers should complete their prayer. The proof is the practice of the Prophet during the Conquest of Mecca: he prayed two rak'ahs and told the Meccans to pray four. The benefit (fa'idah) clarifies that it is not required for the followers to know the imam's travel status beforehand; the imam's statement after salam clarifies it. If they already know, the statement confirms. If they thought he was a resident, the statement would be truthful, as he is actually traveling.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahab): Recommended; an act that if done brings reward, if left is not sinful.
اتباع (ittiba'): Following the Prophet's practice.

Entering Watan Asli and the Types of Homeland
Rulings on watan and its nullification hierarchy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for completing prayer when entering watan asli, classify the three types of watan, and apply the nullification hierarchy.

Core Idea
Entering watan asli ends travel status; watan asli nullifies only its equal—tawtan rules are about strength.

This passage clarifies when a traveler becomes a resident upon entering a city. It presents a key ruling: entering one's original homeland (watan asli) immediately requires completing prayer, even without intending to stay. The text then introduces the three categories of homeland—watan asli, watan iqama, and watan sukna—and explains how each nullifies others based on relative strength.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Focus on the first sentence: when a traveler enters his city, he must complete the prayer. Determine the hukm level: it is fard (obligatory) because residence is established.
The ruling applies immediately upon entry; no intention of stay required for watan asli.
2
Examine the Dalil
The proof is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions. They would travel and return to their homelands as residents without a new resolve. This shows the default ruling for watan asli.
The dalil is an established Sunnah (mutawatir in practice).
3
Define the Three Types of Watan
The text describes watan asli (original), watan iqama (15+ days intention), and watan sukna (<15 days). Understand each definition and note that later scholars (al-Haqiq) only accept two types.
Watan sukna does not change travel status; you remain a traveler.
4
Apply the Nullification Rule
Watan asli is only nullified by another watan asli. Watan iqama is nullified by another iqama, by travel, or by watan asli. This determines whether you shorten or complete prayer when revisiting a former homeland.
The principle: a weaker entity is nullified by an equal or stronger one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و اذا دخل المسافر فى مصره اتم الصلواة وان لم ينو المقام فيه لانه عليه السلام و اصحابه رضوان الله عليهم كانوا يسافرون و يعودون الى اوطانهم مقيمين من غير عزم جديد. و من كان له وطن فانتقل منه واستوطن غيره ثم سافر فدخل وطنه الأول قصر لانه لم يبق وطنا له الا يرى انه عليه السلام بعد الهجرة عد نفسه بمكة من المسافرين وهذا لان الاصل ان الوطن الاصلى تبطل بمثله دون السفرو وطن الاقامة تبطل بمثله و بالسفر و بالاصلي. تشريح: عامة المشايخ نے وطن کی تین قسمیں بیان کی ہیں: وطن اصلی، وطن اقامت، وطن سکنی. وطن اصلی انسان کی اپنی جائے پیدائش ہے یا وہ شہر جس میں اس کے اہل وعیال رہتے ہوں اور اس سے منتقل ہونے کا ارادہ نہ ہو۔ وطن اقامت وہ شہر یا گاؤں ہے جس میں مسافر نے پندرہ دن قیام کا ارادہ کر لیا ہو۔ وطن سکنی وہ شہر ہے جس میں مسافر نے پندرہ دن سے کم قیام کا ارادہ کیا ہو۔ حقین نے وطن کو دو قسموں پر منقسم کیا ہے: وطن اصلی اور وطن اقامت۔ ان حضرات نے وطن سکنی کا اعتبار نہیں کیا ہے اس لئے کہ وطن سکنی میں اقامت ثابت نہیں ہوتی بلکہ سفر کا حکم باقی رہ جاتا ہے۔ ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ وطن اصلی وطن اصلی سے باطل ہوتا ہے نہ وطن اقامت سے اور نہ سفر سے۔ وطن اقامت وطن اقامت سے بھی باطل ہو جاتا ہے سفر سے بھی اور وطن اصلی سے بھی۔ دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ شے اپنے سے بڑی چیز سے باطل ہوتی ہے یا مساوی درجہ کی چیز ہے۔ اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ وطن اصلی سے اوپر کوئی چیز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا وطن اصلی اپنے مساوی یعنی وطن اصلی سے باطل ہو جائے گا۔ صورت اس کی یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص کا ایک وطن ہے وہ اس سے منتقل ہو گیا اور دوسری جگہ کو اپنا وطن بنالیا تو پہلا وطن اصلی باطل ہو گیا۔ چنانچہ اگر شرعی سفر کے بعد وہ اپنے پہلے وطن میں داخل ہوا تو قصر کرے گا۔
And when a traveler enters his city, he completes the prayer even if he did not intend residence therein, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, and his companions, may Allah be pleased with them, used to travel and return to their homelands as residents without a new resolve. And whoever had a homeland and moved from it and settled elsewhere, then traveled and entered his first homeland, he shortens because it is no longer his homeland. Do you not see that the Prophet, peace be upon him, after the hijrah counted himself among the travelers in Mecca? And this is because the principle is that the original homeland is nullified by its like, not by travel; and the homeland of residence is nullified by its like, by travel, and by the original. Explanation: The general mashayikh have mentioned three types of watan: original watan (watan asli), watan of residence (watan iqama), and watan of sojourn (watan sukna). Watan asli is one's birthplace or the city where his family resides and he has no intention to move. Watan iqama is a city or village where a traveler intends to stay for fifteen days. Watan sukna is a city where a traveler intends to stay for less than fifteen days. The later scholars divided watan into two types: original and residence; they did not consider watan sukna because residence is not proven in it; rather the ruling of travel remains. The rule is: original watan is nullified only by another original watan, not by [intending] residence or travel. Watan iqama is nullified by another watan iqama, by travel, and by the original watan. The proof is that a thing is nullified by something greater than it or equal. It is agreed that nothing is above original watan. So original watan is nullified by its equal, i.e., another original watan. The case: a person had a homeland, moved from it, and made another place his homeland; then the first original watan is nullified. So if after a valid travel he enters his first homeland, he shortens.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings: (1) When a traveler enters his original hometown (watan asli), he becomes a resident and must complete (four rak'ahs) even without intention of staying, based on the Prophet's practice. (2) A person who moves to a new homeland loses his previous watan asli; if he later visits it, he is considered a traveler and should shorten. The text then explains the three categories of watan according to the general mashayikh: watan asli (original), watan iqama (where one intends 15+ days), and watan sukna (where one intends less than 15 days). However, later scholars (like al-Haqiq) consider only two: asli and iqama, as sukna does not change the travel ruling. The rule of nullification: watan asli is only annulled by another watan asli; watan iqama is annulled by another watan iqama, by travel, or by watan asli. The reasoning is that a stronger or equal entity nullifies a weaker one; watan asli is the strongest.

Key Terms
وطن اصلی (watan asli): Original homeland: birthplace or where family resides permanently.
وطن اقامت (watan iqama): Place where one intends to stay for 15 days or more.
وطن سکنی (watan sukna): Place where one intends to stay less than 15 days.
قصر (qasr): Shortening prayer from four to two rak'ahs during travel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is nullified by travel alone.
D) It is never nullified.

Key Takeaway
Entering watan asli immediately ends travel status; watan asli is the strongest category, nullified only by its equal.

Traveler Completes Prayer Upon Entering Original Home
Statement of ruling when traveler enters home city without intention to reside

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a traveler completes prayer upon entering his original home and explain the proof from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Entering your original home makes you a resident — no new intention needed.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a key question for travelers: when does the concession of qasr end? The matn gives a clear answer based on the Prophet's own practice. We will analyse the ruling, its proof, and the concept of waṭan aṣlī.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is the hukm level (fard/wajib/etc.)?
The act is the traveler's prayer; the ruling is wajib (to pray four rak'ahs).
2
Understand the scenario
The traveler has completed a journey of three days and enters his original home (miṣr).
No new intention to reside is required.
3
Identify the proof
What dalil does the author cite? It is the practice of the Prophet and his Companions.
The proof is a Sunnah ahad, but its wajh al-dalalah is the consistent practice.
4
Recognise the concept of waṭan aṣlī
The original home is defined as one's birthplace or permanent residence. Entering it establishes residency automatically.
This is distinct from waṭan iqāma, which requires intention.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario, determine if the traveler must pray full or shortened.
Check if the place entered is waṭan aṣlī.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم

مسافر شہر میں داخل ہو جائے تو مکمل نماز پڑھے گا اگر چہ اقامت کی نیت نہ کی ہو

و اذا دخل المسافر فى مصره اتم الصلواة وان لم ينو المقام فيه لانه عليه السلام و اصحابه رضوان الله عليهم کانوا يسافرون و يعودون الى اوطانهم مقیمین من غير عزم جديد ترجمہ اور جب مسافر اپنے وطن میں داخل ہوا تو نماز پوری پڑھے اگر چہ اس میں قیام کی نیت نہ کی ہو۔ اس لئے کہ حضور اور آپ کے صحابہ شفر کیا کرتے اور اپنے وطنوں کی جانب واپس آتے ہی بغیر کسی عزم جدید کے مقیم ہو جاتے ۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب مسافر نے تین دن کی مسافت طے کر کے سفر مکمل کر لیا، پھر وہ اپنے وطن اصلی میں داخل ہواتو آبادی میں داخل ہوتے ہی مقیم ہو گیا اگر چہ اقامت کی نیت نہ کی ہو ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم اور آپ کے صحابہ رضی اللہ تعالی ہم سفر کیا کرتے تھے اور تکمیل سفر کے بعد جب وطن لوٹ کر آتے تو بغیر اقامت کی نیت کے مقیم ہو جاتے۔ وطن اقامت وطن اقامت سے باطل ہو جاتا ہے
Chapter on the Traveler's Prayer. When a traveler enters his city (the place of his origin), he completes the prayer even if he did not intend residence, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions would travel and return to their homelands as residents without a new resolve. Commentary: And when the traveler entered his homeland, he prays fully even if he did not intend to stay there, because the Prophet and his companions would travel and return to their homelands as residents without a new resolve. Explanation: The scenario is that when a traveler has completed a journey of three days' distance, then he enters his original homeland, he becomes a resident upon entering the populated area even if he did not intend residence. The proof is that the Messenger of God and his companions would travel, and upon completing the journey, when they returned to the homeland, they would become residents without the intention of residence. The residence home is nullified by the residence home.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on a traveler entering his original home (waṭan aṣlī). The Hidayah states that if a traveler enters his home city (miṣr), he must perform the prayer in full (tamam) even without a new intention to reside. The proof is the practice of the Prophet and his Companions, who would return from travel and automatically be considered residents. The Urdu commentary clarifies: once a traveler completes a journey of three days (the minimum travel distance) and enters his original homeland (waṭan aṣlī), residency is immediately established upon entering the built-up area, regardless of intent. The passage ends with a brief principle: 'Waṭan iqāma is nullified by (another) waṭan iqāma', hinting at the rules of nullification of different types of homes.

Key Terms
المِصر (al-miṣr): The city or town that is a person's original home (waṭan aṣlī).
وطن اصلی (waṭan aṣlī): A person's original home, e.g., birthplace or permanent residence with no intent to leave.
وطن اقامت (waṭan iqāma): A place where a traveler intends to stay for fifteen days or more; it is a temporary residence.

Nullification of Original Home and Residence Home
Explanation of nullification rules for waṭan types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when a former original home is nullified and apply it to determine whether a traveler must shorten prayer.

Core Idea
A former original home is nullified only by another original home; a residence home is nullified by travel, its like, or an original home.

The Hidayah clarifies a critical fiqh rule for Muslims who relocate. The legal status of 'home' (waṭan) directly affects whether one shortens or completes prayer. This lesson explains how an original home is nullified by acquiring a new permanent home, and how a temporary residence home is more easily invalidated. We anchor the ruling in the Prophet’s own practice after the Hijra.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The central act is entering a former original home after moving to a new one. The ruling is that the traveler must shorten prayer (qasr) because the old home no longer holds the status of 'original home'.
Act: entry into former home. Ruling: qasr is wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's (ﷺ) own conduct after the Hijra. When he entered Mecca for the conquest or pilgrimage, he counted himself among the travelers and shortened prayer.
Dalil: Sunnah of the Prophet.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action demonstrates that Mecca, his original home before Hijra, ceased to be his home after he settled in Medina. If it were still his home, he would not have shortened prayer. This shows that moving to a new home nullifies the old one.
Wajh: the Prophet's shortening implies nullification.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some later scholars argue that maintaining property or family ties in the former home could preserve its status. The Hanafi school, however, insists on complete abandonment—only taking a new original home nullifies the old one.
Ikhtilaf: existence of property/family does not preserve status per Hanafis.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Hidayah: the original home is nullified only by another original home, not by travel or temporary presence. This is the authoritative view in the school.
Tarjih: based on the Prophet's practice and the principle of nullification by equal or greater.

باب صلوة المسافر
نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ قصر پڑھے گا یہی وجہ ہے کہ صاحب شریعت علیہ السلام کا وطن اصلی مکہ المکرمہ تھا لیکن آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم جب ہجرت فرما کر مدینہ منورہ تشریف لے گئے ۔ اور مدینہ کو اپنا وطن بنالیا تو مکہ وطن اصلی نہیں رہا چنانچہ ہجرت کے بعد جب آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم مکہ مکرمہ تشریف لائے تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے خود کو مسافر شمار کیا۔ اور فرمایا اتموا صلاتكم فانا قوم سفر -

اور چونکہ وطن اصلی وطن اقامت سے مافوق ہے اس لئے وطن اقامت وطن اصلی سے باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اور وطن اقامت طول قامت اور کا مساوی ہے اس لئے وطن اقامت وطن اقامت سے بھی باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اور وطن اقامت سفر سے اس لئے باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کہ سفر ان اقامت کی ضد ہے۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ شئے اپنی ضد سے باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور اگر سوال کیا جائے کہ سفر تو وطن اصلی کی بھی ضد ہے لہذا
ہوا تو ان اصلی بھی سفر سے باطل ہونا چاہئے ۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔ انم جواب وطن اصلی کا سفر کی وجہ سے عدم بطلان اثر کی وجہ سے ہے کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم غزوات کے لئے مدینہ منورہ سے نکل کر دور دراز تشریف لے جاتے۔ لیکن اس کے باوجود مدینہ منورہ آپ کا وطن اصلی رہا، چنانچہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم جب سفر سے واپس تشریف لاتے تو
انه
اقامت کی نیت نہ فرماتے ۔ اگر وطن اصلی سفر سے باطل ہو جاتا تو واپسی پر آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم اقامت کی نیت ضرور فرماتے ۔
And whoever has a home, then moves from it and settles elsewhere, then travels and enters his first home, he should shorten the prayer because it is no longer his home. Do you not see that the Prophet (peace be upon him) after the hijra counted himself among the travelers in Mecca? And this is because the principle is that the original home is nullified by its like (original home), not by travel; and the residence home is nullified by its like, by travel, and by the original home. ... Explanation: General scholars have mentioned three types of home: original home, residence home, and dwelling home (waṭan suknā). Original home is a person's birthplace or the city where his family lives without intent to leave. Residence home is a city or village where a traveler intends to stay fifteen days; its other name is 'travel home' (waṭan safar). Dwelling home is a city where a traveler intends to stay less than fifteen days. Some scholars divided home into only two: original and residence, not considering dwelling home because residency is not established in it. ... The proof for this is that a thing is nullified by something greater or equal. It is well-known that nothing is above original home, so it is only nullified by its equal, i.e., another original home. For example, a person has one home, then moves from that place and makes another place his home; the first original home is nullified. So if after a legal journey he enters his first home, he will not become a resident but will shorten the prayer. This is why the Lawgiver's original home was Mecca, but when he emigrated to Medina and made it his home, Mecca was no longer his original home. Consequently, after hijra, when he came to Mecca, he counted himself a traveler and said: 'Complete your prayer, for we are a traveling people.' And because the original home is superior to residence home, the residence home is nullified by the original home. And the residence home is equal to another residence home, so it is nullified by its like. And the residence home is nullified by travel because travel is its opposite, and rule is that a thing is nullified by its opposite. If it is asked: Travel is also opposite to original home, so why is it not nullified? The answer is that the original home is not nullified by travel due to effect (athar), for it is narrated that the Prophet would go out from Medina for expeditions far away, yet Medina remained his original home. So when he returned from travel, he would not intend residence. If original home were nullified by travel, he would have needed to intend residence upon return.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This section provides the rules for nullification of different types of home (waṭan). The Hidayah's matn states that if a person moves from his original home to another and makes that his home, then later travels back to the first home, he must shorten prayer because it is no longer his home. Evidence: the Prophet after hijra counted himself a traveler in Mecca. The principle is that the original home is nullified only by another original home, not by travel. The residence home (waṭan iqāma) is nullified by its like (another residence home), by travel, and by the original home. The Urdu commentary expands: scholars mention three types: original (waṭan aṣlī), residence (waṭan iqāma), and dwelling (waṭan suknā). Some only recognize two. The dwelling home does not change the ruling of travel. The reasoning for nullification: a thing is nullified by what is greater or equal. Original home is the highest level, so only another original home can nullify it. Residence home is lower, so it can be nullified by original home (superior), by its equal, and by travel (its opposite). A potential objection: if travel nullifies its opposite (residence), why doesn't it nullify original home? The answer: because original home has permanence (athar) proven by the Prophet's practice; after traveling from Medina, he never needed to re-intend residence, showing Medina remained his original home.

Key Terms
وطن أصلي (waṭan aṣlī): Permanent home (birthplace or family residence with no intent to emigrate) that is not nullified by travel.
وطن إقامة (waṭan iqāma): Place where a traveler intends to stay fifteen days; it nullifies the status of traveler.
وطن سكنى (waṭan suknā): Place where a traveler intends to stay less than fifteen days; does not affect travel status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what nullifies an original home (waṭan aṣlī)?
A) Travel
B) Another original home
C) A residence home
D) Dwelling home

Key Takeaway
An original home is nullified only by acquiring another original home, not by travel or temporary moves.

Intention to Stay in Two Places Does Not Make One Resident
Ruling when traveler intends fifteen days in two separate locations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a traveler's intention to stay fifteen days in two separate places makes him a resident, and apply the criterion of overnight stay (mabīt) to determine residency.

Core Idea
Intending fifteen days in two places keeps you a traveler; only intending overnight in one makes you resident.

This lesson explores a subtle but important ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding the definition of residency for the traveler. When a traveler intends to stay fifteen days but splits that intention between two locations, the school provides a clear criterion based on the place of overnight stay. Understanding this distinction prevents errors in shortening prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize the scenario: a traveler intends to stay fifteen days total, but in two separate places (e.g., Mecca and Mina).
The two places must be distinct, even if nearby.
2
State the default ruling
The traveler does not become a resident; he remains a traveler and must shorten his prayers. This is because considering intention in two places would logically require considering it in many places, which is impossible given that travel always involves multiple stops.
The ruling is based on rational proof (dalil aqli).
3
Understand the rational proof
The proof: if intention in two places were valid, it would necessitate intention in many places (since travel always includes multiple stops). That would eliminate the category of travel altogether. Therefore, such an intention cannot be valid.
This is a sad al-dhara'i' (blocking means) argument.
4
Identify the exception
If the traveler intends to stay overnight (al-mabīt) in one specific place, then upon entering that place he becomes a resident. Residency is tied to the overnight stay.
Daytime stays in the other place do not affect this residency.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario with specific intentions, determine whether the traveler becomes a resident or remains a traveler, and state the prayer ruling.
Practice applying the criterion of overnight stay.

And when the traveler intends to stay in Mecca and Mina for fifteen days, he does not complete the prayer because the consideration of intention in two places necessitates its consideration in many places, which is impossible because travel is never free from it. But if he intends to stay overnight in one of them, then he becomes a resident immediately upon entering, because a person's residence is attributed to his place of staying overnight. Commentary: When a traveler intends fifteen days in Mecca and Mina, he does not become a resident; he remains a traveler and shortens prayer. Because requiring intention in two places would logically require intention in many places, leading to no preference without justification. And it is forbidden for a traveler to intend to stay in many places because travel necessarily involves stopping at many places. If intention in multiple places were considered, one would never be a traveler. However, if he intends to spend the night in one of the two specific places, then that intention is valid: upon entering that place, he becomes a resident. Then if he goes to the other place (where he intended daytime stays), he does not lose residency because a person's residence is attributed to his overnight stay.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a traveler intends to spend fifteen days in two distinct locations (e.g., Mecca and Mina). The Hanafi ruling: this does not make him a resident; he must still shorten prayer. The reason provided is that accepting intention in two places would logically require accepting intention in many places (since travel always involves multiple stops), which would eliminate the very concept of travel. The exception: if the traveler intends to spend the night (al-mabīt) in one of the two places specifically, then upon entering that place he becomes a resident. The ruling on the other place: if he later goes there, he remains a resident because residency is tied to the place of overnight stay. The Urdu commentary elaborates: if one intends fifteen days in two places like Mecca and Mina, he is still a traveler because such intention, if valid, would lead to an infinite regress. Only when the intention includes overnight stay in one specific location does residency begin there.

Key Terms
مبيت (mabīt): Overnight stay; the place where one spends the night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) He becomes a resident in the place where he intends to stay overnight.
D) He remains a traveler in both.

Key Takeaway
A traveler does not become a resident by intending fifteen days in two places unless he specifies overnight stay in one location.

The Original Homeland Is Not Nullified by Travel
Ruling on immunity of watan asli from travel with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the immunity of watan asli from travel and explain the proof from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The original homeland remains intact regardless of travel; only the homeland of residence is nullified.

In this lesson, we examine a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: the original homeland (watan asli) is never nullified by travel, even prolonged absence. The passage uses the Prophet's own example to establish this ruling, clarifying the hierarchy between watan asli and watan iqamah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the legal status: watan asli is not nullified by travel. The passage opens by affirming that a person with watan asli still prays qasr when away.
2
Examine the proof
Consider the Prophet's migration: after settling in Madinah, Makkah lost its status as his watan asli. When he visited Makkah, he considered himself a traveller and said, 'Complete your prayer, for we are a travelling people.'
The hadith 'أتموا صلاتكم فإنا قوم سفر' is used as evidence.
3
Understand the hierarchy
Watan asli overrides watan iqamah, and watan iqamah is nullified by travel because travel is its opposite. But watan asli is immune to nullification by travel.
The rule 'a thing is nullified by its opposite' applies only to watan iqamah.
4
Answer the objection
If travel nullifies its opposite (watan iqamah), why not watan asli? The answer is based on the Prophet's ongoing practice: he left Madinah for battles but never needed to intend residence upon return, proving watan asli remained intact.
This is a dalil naqli based on athar (Prophetic practice).
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that watan asli is never nullified by travel, as supported by the Prophet's example and the Hanafi legal hierarchy.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is universally applied in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ قصر پڑھے گا یہی وجہ ہے کہ صاحب شریعت علیہ السلام کا وطن اصلی مکہ المکرمہ تھا لیکن آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم جب ہجرت فرما کر مدینہ منورہ تشریف لے گئے ۔ اور مدینہ کو اپنا وطن بنالیا تو مکہ وطن اصلی نہیں رہا چنانچہ ہجرت کے بعد جب آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم مکہ مکرمہ تشریف لائے تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے خود کو مسافر شمار کیا۔ اور فرمایا اتمموا صلاتكم فانا قوم سفر - اور چونکہ وطن اصلی وطن اقامت سے مافوق ہے اس لئے وطن اقامت وطن اصلی سے باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اور وطن اقامت طول قامت اور کا مساوی ہے اس لئے وطن اقامت وطن اقامت سے بھی باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اور وطن اقامت سفر سے اس لئے باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کہ سفر ان اقامت کی ضد ہے۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ شئے اپنی ضد سے باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور اگر سوال کیا جائے کہ سفر تو وطن اصلی کی بھی ضد ہے لہذا ہوا تو ان اصلی بھی سفر سے باطل ہونا چاہئے ۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔ انم جواب وطن اصلی کا سفر کی وجہ سے عدم بطلان اثر کی وجہ سے ہے کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم غزوات کے لئے مدینہ منورہ سے نکل کر دور دراز تشریف لے جاتے۔ لیکن اس کے باوجود مدینہ منورہ آپ کا وطن اصلی رہا، چنانچہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم جب سفر سے واپس تشریف لاتے تو اقامت کی نیت نہ فرماتے ۔ اگر وطن اصلی سفر سے باطل ہو جاتا تو واپسی پر آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم اقامت کی نیت ضرور فرماتے ۔
It will not be. Rather, he will pray qasr. For this reason, the original homeland of the Master of the Law (peace be upon him) was Makkah al-Mukarramah, but when he migrated and went to Madinah Munawwarah, and made Madinah his homeland, Makkah did not remain his original homeland. Accordingly, after the migration, when he (peace be upon him) came to Makkah Mukarramah, he considered himself a traveller and said, 'Complete your prayer, for we are a travelling people.' And since the original homeland is superior to the homeland of residence, therefore the homeland of residence becomes nullified by the original homeland. And the homeland of residence is equal to [؟], therefore the homeland of residence becomes nullified by the homeland of residence as well. And the homeland of residence becomes nullified by travel because travel is the opposite of residence. And the rule is that a thing becomes nullified by its opposite. And if it is asked that travel is also the opposite of the original homeland, therefore the original homeland should also become nullified by travel, but this is not the case. Their answer is that the non-nullification of the original homeland by travel is due to effect (athar), because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would leave Madinah for distant places for battles, but despite that, Madinah remained his original homeland. Thus, when he would return from travel, he would not intend residence. If the original homeland were nullified by travel, then upon return, the Prophet (peace be upon him) would have certainly intended residence.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the status of the original homeland (watan asli) in relation to travel. The passage begins by stating the ruling that the original homeland is not nullified by travel, using the example of the Prophet Muhammad (SAW). After the Hijrah, Madinah became his watan asli, and when he later visited Makkah, he considered himself a traveller and shortened his prayers, as narrated in the hadith 'Complete your prayer, for we are a travelling people.' The text then explains the hierarchy: watan asli overrides watan iqamah, watan iqamah overrides another watan iqamah, and watan iqamah is nullified by travel because travel is its opposite. An objection is raised: if travel nullifies its opposite (watan iqamah), why does it not nullify watan asli, which is also opposite? The answer is based on the Prophet's practice (athar): he repeatedly left Madinah for battles without intending residence upon return, proving that his watan asli remained intact despite prolonged travel. This demonstrates that watan asli is immune to nullification by travel.

Key Terms
وطن اصلی (watan asli): The original homeland, which a person has permanent ties to and is not nullified by travel.
وطن اقامت (watan iqamah): A place where one intends to stay for at least fifteen days, considered a residence but subordinate to watan asli.
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'ah prayers to two rak'ahs while travelling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) It is nullified only if the travel exceeds 15 days.

Key Takeaway
The original homeland is never nullified by travel, as established by the Prophet's practice and Hanafi legal hierarchy.
