Dual Intention for Residency: The General Ruling
Ruling on dual-locality intention for residency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a traveller who intends to stay in two separate places for fifteen days does not become a resident, and explain the rationale based on the impossibility of recognizing multiple intentions.

Core Idea
Intent to stay in two places cannot establish residency; only a single unified intention for fifteen days qualifies.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi fiqh: a traveller who intends to stay in two different localities for fifteen days remains a traveller. The reason is that if we allowed multiple intentions, it would lead to recognizing residency in every place a traveller stops, which would negate the very concept of travel. This precision is crucial for determining salah rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the Arabic sentence: a traveller intends to stay in Makkah and Mina for fifteen days. The ruling is that he does not complete his prayer, i.e., he remains a musafir.
The act of 'not completing' means he prays qasr (shortened prayers).
2
Analyze the rationale
The text says 'because considering intention in two places necessitates considering it in multiple places, and that is impossible since travel is not free from it.' Explain this reasoning in your own words.
Travel inherently involves multiple stops; if any stop with intention for 15 days made one muqeem, no journey would be travel.
3
Contrast with single-locality intention
If the traveller intended fifteen days in a single city, he would become muqeem. Compare with the dual intention case.
The key is the unity of the place, not the total duration.
4
Note the exception
The passage introduces an exception involving overnight stay, which will be covered in the next lesson.
This exception shows the importance of night-time stay in determining residency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسافر کے لئے دو شہروں میں اقامت کی نیت کا اعتبار نہیں 
راذا نوى المسافر ان يقيم بمكة و منى خمسة عشر يوما لم يتم الصلوة لان اعتبار النية في موضعين يقتضى اعتبارها في مواضع وهو ممتنع لان السفر لا يعرى عنه الا اذا نوى ان يقيم بالليل في احدهما فيصير مقيما بدخوله لان اقامة المرء مضافة الى مبيته 
ترجمہ اور جب مسافر نے مکہ اورمنی میں پندرہ دن کی اقامت کی نیت کی تو وہ نماز پوری نہ پڑھے کیونکہ دو مقام میں نیت کا معتبر ہونا مقتضی ہے کہ چند جگہوں میں نیت معتبر ہو اور یہ متنع ہے کیونکہ سفر اس سے خالی نہیں ہوتا۔ ہاں اگر ان دونوں میں سے ایک میں رات میں قیام کی نیت کرے تو اس مقام میں داخل ہونے کے ساتھ ہی مقیم ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ آدمی کا مقیم ہونا اس کی شب باشی کے مقام کی جانب منسوب ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مسافر نے ایسے مقام میں پندرہ دن ٹھہرنے کی نیت کی جن میں سے ایک مستقل نہیں ہے۔ مثلا یہ کہ مکہ اور منی میں اقامت کی نیت کی تو یہ مقیم نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ مسافر ہی رہے گا۔ اور نماز قصر پڑھے گا۔ کیونکہ دو مقام میں اقامت کی نیت کا معتبر ہونا اس بات کی مقتضی ہے کہ دو سے زائد مقامات میں بھی نیت معتبر ہو ورنہ ترجیح بلا مرج لازم آئے گا۔ اور مسافر کا بہت سے مقامات پر قیام کی نیت کرنا منع ہے کیونکہ سفر متعدد مقامات پر قیام کرنے سے خالی نہیں ہوتا بلکہ بہت سے مقامات پر قیام کرنا ضروری ہوتا ہے پس اگر متعدد مقامات میں اقامت کی نیت کا اعتبار کر لیا جائے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہو گا کہ آدمی کبھی مسافر ہی نہ ہو۔ ہاں اگر صورت یہ ہے کہ دو مقام میں پندرہ یوم اقامت کی نیت کی اور ان دونوں میں سے ایک متعینہ مقام میں رات گزارنے کی نیت کی تو یہ نیت معتبر ہوگی اب اگر یہ شخص پہلے اس جگہ گیا جہاں دن گزارنے کی نیت کی ہے تو یہ مقیم نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر پہلے اس جگہ گیا جہاں رات گزارنے کا ارادہ کیا ہے تو اس بستی میں داخل ہوتے ہی مقیم ہو جائے گا۔ پھر اس بستی کی طرف نکلنے سے مسافر نہ ہو گا جہاں دن گزارنے کی نیت کی ہے کیونکہ آدمی کی اقامت اس کی شب باشی کی طرف منسوب کی جاتی ہے۔ چنانچہ آپ دیکھئے جو شخص بازار میں کاروبار کرتا ہے اس سے اگر دریافت کیا جائے کہ اس وقت تم کہاں رہتے ہو تو وہ اس محلہ کا پتہ بتلائے گا جہاں وہ رات گزارتا ہے۔
For a traveller, intending to stay in two cities is not considered.
If a traveller intends to stay in Makkah and Mina for fifteen days, he does not complete his prayer, because considering intention in two places necessitates considering it in multiple places, and that is impossible, since travel is not free from it. Except if he intends to stay at night in one of them, then he becomes a resident upon entering it, because a person's residency is attributed to his overnight stay.
Translation: And when a traveller intended to stay in Makkah and Mina for fifteen days, he will not pray completely, because the validity of intention in two places requires that intention be valid in several places, and this is prevented because travel is not free from it. Yes, if he intends to stay at night in one of them, then upon entering that place he will become a resident, because a person's residency is attributed to the place of his overnight stay. Explanation: The gist of the issue is that a traveller intended to stay for fifteen days in a place where one is not permanent. For example, if he intends to stay in Makkah and Mina, he will not become a resident; rather he will remain a traveller and pray qasr. Because the validity of intention in two places necessitates that intention be valid in more than two places, otherwise preference without a preponderant would be necessary. And it is prohibited for a traveller to intend to stay in many places because travel is not free from halting at multiple places; rather halting at many places is necessary. So if the intention of stay in multiple places were considered valid, it would mean that a person would never be a traveller. Yes, if the case is that he intended to stay in two places for fifteen days, and in one of those specific places he intended to spend the night, then this intention will be valid. Now if this person first goes to the place where he intended to spend the day, he will not become a resident. And if he first goes to the place where he intended to spend the night, upon entering that town he will become a resident. Then he will not become a traveller by going to the place where he intended to spend the day because a person's residency is attributed to his overnight stay. So you see, a person who does business in the market, if asked where he lives, he will give the location of the place where he spends the night.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school regarding the effect of intending to stay in two separate localities. The matn states that if a traveller intends to stay in two places (e.g., Makkah and Mina) for fifteen days, he does not become a resident (muqeem) and must continue to shorten prayers. The reasoning is that recognizing intention in two places would logically require recognizing it in many places, which is impossible because travel necessarily involves stopping at various locations. However, if he specifically intends to spend the night in one of them, he becomes a resident upon entering that place, as residency is attached to one's night-time stay. The commentary elaborates with examples: intending to stay in two places without specifying overnight stay does not change the traveler's status. But if he designates one for sleeping, that place becomes his residence. This aligns with the common practice that a person's home is where he sleeps at night.

Key Terms
اقامت (iqamah): Residency, legally defined as intending to stay for fifteen days or more in one place.
نیت (niyyah): Intention, which is a condition for becoming a resident (muqeem) when staying fifteen days.
شب باشی (shab bashi): Overnight stay; the place where one spends the night is the determinant of residency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if a traveller intends to stay in Makkah for 10 days and Medina for 10 days, with no overnight intention specified, what is his legal status?
A) He is a muqeem in both places.
B) He remains a traveller.
C) He becomes a muqeem of his first destination.
D) He becomes a muqeem after 15 total days.

Key Takeaway
Intent to stay in two places for fifteen days does not make one a resident; residency requires a single, unified intention for fifteen days in one locality.

The Exception: Overnight Stay Determines Residency
Exception to dual-intention rule based on overnight stay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the exception that a traveller who intends to spend the night in one of two places becomes a resident upon entering that place.

Core Idea
The place where one spends the night determines residency, even if one intends to spend the day elsewhere.

This lesson builds on the previous one by examining the exception: if the traveller specifies that he will stay overnight in one of the two locations, he becomes a resident of that location upon entering it. This is because 'a person's residency is attributed to his overnight stay' (shab bashi). This principle is grounded in common practice: a person's home is where he sleeps.

Guided Path
1
Read the exception sentence
Read: 'Except if he intends to stay at night in one of them, then he becomes a resident upon entering it.' Identify the trigger: intention to stay at night.
The Arabic term 'shab bashi' is used in the Urdu commentary.
2
Understand the basis
The text says 'because a person's residency is attributed to his overnight stay.' This is a legal presumption based on custom.
Think of common practice: a person is asked 'where do you live?' and answers with the place he sleeps.
3
Apply the ruling
If he first goes to the place where he intends to sleep, he becomes muqeem immediately upon arrival. If he first goes to the day-stay place, he remains a traveller until he enters the night-stay place.
This shows the order of entry matters.
4
Consider the consequence
Once muqeem in the night-stay place, he does not become a traveller again by going to the day-stay place during the day.
Residency persists while he remains connected to the night-stay locality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Determining the Number of Rak'ahs for Qada Prayers When State Changes
Ruling on number of rak'ahs for qada of prayers missed in different states

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that qada follows the obligation at the end of the original prayer time to determine the number of rak'ahs for a makeup prayer when the state has changed.

Core Idea
The number of rak'ahs in qada depends on the state at the end of the missed prayer's time, not at makeup.

This lesson explains a key Hanafi ruling: the makeup (qada) of a missed prayer is performed according to the state (resident or traveller) at the end of the original prayer time, not the state at the time of makeup. This principle is derived from the maxim 'qada follows ada' and the consideration of the end of the time as the cause of obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the missed prayer and the two states
Determine which prayer was missed (is it a 4-rak'ah prayer? Zuhr, Asr, Isha? Or 2/3? The rule applies to the 4-rak'ah prayers that are shortened during travel). Identify the state (resident/traveller) at the end of the original prayer time and the state at the time of makeup.
Fajr and Maghrib are never shortened, so their qada is always the same.
2
Recall the general shortening rule
During travel, a 4-rak'ah fard prayer is shortened to 2 rak'ahs. During residence, it is performed as 4 rak'ahs.
3
Apply the principle 'qada follows ada'
The number of rak'ahs in qada is determined by the obligation that existed at the end of the original time. This is because the end of the time is considered the cause of obligation when the prayer was not performed in time.
The source states: لان القضاء بحسب الاداء والمعتبر في ذلك آخر الوقت
4
Address the counter-argument
Some may argue that the entire time is the cause, not just the end. The Hanafi response is that in the case of a missed prayer, the last part of the time (miqdar al-tahrimah) is the cause, as adopted by the author of Hidayah.
This is an internal Hanafi discussion; the mufta bihi is the end-of-time view.
5
Conclude the ruling
If the prayer was missed while resident, make up 4 rak'ahs even if now travelling. If missed while travelling, make up 2 rak'ahs even if now resident.
The state at the moment of makeup does not matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سفر کی نماز حضر میں قصر پڑھی جائے گی اور حضر کی نماز سفر میں مکمل پڑھی جائے گی 
و من فاتته صلواة فى السفر قضاءها في الحضر ركعتين ومن فاتته فى الحضر قضاها في السفر اربعا لان القضاء بحسب الاداء والمعتبر في ذلك آخر الوقت لانه المعتبر في السبية عند عدم الاداء في الوقت 
ترجمہ اور جس شخص کی کوئی نماز سفر میں فوت ہو گئی تو حضر میں اس کو دو رکعت قضاء کرے اور جس کی نماز حضر میں فوت ہوگئی تو اس کو سند میں چار رکعت قضاء کرے کیونکہ قضاء ادا کے موافق ہوتی ہے اور اس میں معتبر آخر وقت ہے کیونکہ آخری وقت ہی سبب ہونے میں معتبر ہوتا ہے جبکہ وقت کے اندر ادا نہ کیا ہو۔ 
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ سفر کی حالت میں اگر رباعی نماز فوت ہوگئی اور حضر میں اس کو قضاء کرنا چاہا تو دو رکعت قضاء کرے اور حضر کے زمانے میں کوئی رباعی نماز فوت ہو گئی پھر سفر کی حالت میں اس کو قضاء کرنا چاہا تو چار رکعت قضاء کرے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ قضاء ادا کے موافق واجب ہوتی ہے یعنی جس شخص پر ادا چار رکعت واجب ہوئی تو وہ قضاء بھی چار رکعت کرے گا۔ اور جس پر دو رکعت ادا کرنا واجب ہوا ۔ اس پر قضاء بھی دورکعت کی واجب ہو گی۔ اور ادا کے اندر وقت کا آخر معتبر ہے آخر وقت سے مراد مقدار تحریمہ ہے مثلا اگر ظہیر کے اول وقت میں مقیم تھا کچھ وقت ختم ہونے سے پہلے سفر کے لئے نکالا اور آبادی سے باہر اس وقت ہوا جب کہ وقت صرف ایک رکعت کا یا کم باقی ہے تو اس پر دو ہی رکعت کی قضا واجب ہوگی کیونکہ آخر وقت میں وہ مسافر ہو چکا۔ اور یہی معتبر ہے۔ اور ادا کے اندر وقت کا آخر اس لئے معتبر ہے کہ وقت کے اندرادا کرنے کی صورت میں وجوب کا سبب ہونے میں آخر وقت معتبر ہے۔ اس موقع پر پاک اعتراض ہوسکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ ہمارا کلام قضاء نماز میں ہے۔ اور نماز جب اپنے وقت سے فوت ہوگئی تو اصل فقہ کے بیان کے مطابق پورا وقت نماز کا سبب ہوتا ہے نہ کہ آخری جز : جواب بعض مشائخ کے نزدیک نماز فوت ہونے کی صورت میں وقت کا آخری جز سبب ہوتا ہے۔ بہت ممکن ہی کہ مصنف ہدایہ نے اس کو اختیار کیا ہو۔
The prayer of travel will be shortened in residence, and the prayer of residence will be completed in travel.
Whoever misses a prayer during travel, its makeup in residence is two rak'ahs; and whoever misses a prayer during residence, its makeup in travel is four rak'ahs, because qada is in accordance with ada, and the consideration in that is the end of the time, because it is considered in causation when ada did not occur in time.
Translation: And whoever's prayer was missed during travel, he should make it up in residence as two rak'ahs; and whoever's prayer was missed during residence, he should make it up in travel as four rak'ahs, because qada corresponds to ada, and in that the end of the time is considered, because the end of the time is considered in causation when the prayer was not performed within the time.
Explanation: The gist of the issue is that if a four-rak'ah prayer was missed during travel and he wants to make it up in residence, he makes it up as two rak'ahs. And if a four-rak'ah prayer was missed during residence and he wants to make it up during travel, he makes it up as four rak'ahs. The proof is that qada is wajib according to ada: the person upon whom ada of four rak'ahs was obligatory will also make up four rak'ahs, and the person upon whom ada of two rak'ahs was obligatory will make up two rak'ahs. And in ada, the end of the time is considered; by 'end of the time' is meant the amount of time sufficient for the takbirat al-ihram (miqdar al-tahrimah). For example, if he was a resident at the beginning of Zuhr time, but before the time ended he left for travel and reached outside the settlement when only the time for one rak'ah or less remained, then only two rak'ahs of qada are obligatory because at the end of the time he had become a traveller. And that is what is considered. And the end of the time is considered in ada because in the case of performing the prayer within the time, the end of the time is considered as the cause of obligation. Here an objection may arise: we are discussing qada prayer, and when a prayer is missed from its time, according to the principles of fiqh, the entire time is the cause for the prayer, not just the last part. The answer is that according to some mashayikh, in the case of a missed prayer, the last part of the time is the cause. It is very possible that the author of Hidayah adopted this view.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof regarding the number of rak'ahs for qada (make-up) prayers when the prayer was missed in a different state. The matn states: if a prayer is missed while travelling, it is made up as 2 rak'ahs even if the person is now a resident; conversely, if a prayer is missed while resident, it is made up as 4 rak'ahs even if now travelling. The reason is that qada follows the obligation of ada at the time it became due, and the consideration for that obligation is the end of the prayer time. The commentary explains that the end of the time (the last portion sufficient for at least the takbirat al-ihram) determines whether the person was a traveller or resident at that moment. An objection is raised: the entire time is the cause for the prayer, not just the end. The response is that some mashayikh hold that in case of a missed prayer, the last part of the time is the cause, and the author of Hidayah likely adopted that view.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a prayer that was missed within its prescribed time.
اداء (ada): Performing a prayer within its prescribed time.
آخر وقت (akhir al-waqt): The end of the prayer time, specifically the amount sufficient for the takbirat al-ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person misses a Zuhr prayer while a resident, and later makes it up while travelling, how many rak'ahs does he pray?
A) 2 rak'ahs
B) 4 rak'ahs
C) 3 rak'ahs
D) It depends on his intention

Key Takeaway
The number of rak'ahs for a makeup prayer is determined by the state (resident or traveller) at the end of the original prayer time, not at the time of makeup.

Travel Concessions for the Sinful Traveller: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on travel concession for sinful vs obedient traveller

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on travel concessions for sinful travellers, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and apply the ikhtilaf to a concrete scenario.

Core Idea
Travel concessions apply to all travellers; sin does not nullify the concession because travel itself is not sinful.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a classic inter-madhhab dispute: does a person who travels for a sinful purpose (e.g., robbery) still benefit from the travel concessions such as shortening prayers? The Hanafi school holds that all travellers are equal in this regard, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts concessions to permissible travel. Let us examine the proofs and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the passage: the sinful and obedient traveller are equal in accessing travel concessions.
The passage uses the term 'sawa' (equal).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees and his reasoning: concessions are lightenings, so they should not attach to what necessitates severity (sin).
Shafi'i's argument is based on the nature of concessions (rukhsah) as lightenings.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand Shafi'i's dalil: 'Concessions are lightenings, and they should not be attached to that which necessitates severity (sinful travel).'
This is a rational proof (istidlal bi al-ma'qul) rather than a direct textual proof.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds with two points: (1) the texts are general (itlaq al-nusus) and (2) travel itself is not sinful; sin is separate.
The Hanafi proof relies on the generality of Quranic and hadith texts not specifying the purpose of travel.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a robber travelling to steal would be required to pray full prayers according to Shafi'i, but can shorten according to Hanafi.
This difference affects actual practice for those engaged in sinful travel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سفر کی رخصت مطیع اور عاصی دونوں کے لئے ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء 
والعاصي والمطيع في سفره في الرخصة سواء وقال الشافعى سفر المعصية لا يفيد الرخصة لانها تثبت تخفيفا فلا تتعلق بما يوجب التغليظ ولنا اطلاق النصوص ولان نفس السفر ليس بمعصية وانما المعصية ـایــــــــون بــــــــده اویجاوره فصلح متـعــلــق الـــرخــصـة والله اعلم 
ترجمہ اور جو شخص اپنے سفر میں نافرمان ہے اور جو شخص اپنے سفر میں فرمانبردار ہے۔ دونوں رخصت میں برابر ہیں۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ معصیت کا سفر رخصت کا فائدہ نہیں دیتا کیونکہ رخصت تو تخفیف ثابت کرتی ہے پس رخصت ایسی چیز ہے سے متعلق نہ ہوگی جس تختی کو واجب کرتی ہے۔ ہماری دلیل نصوص کا اطلاق ہے اور ابن لئے کہ نفس سفر گناہ نہیں ہے اور رہی معصیب تو وہ چیز ہے جو نہ
Are the travel concessions for the obedient and the sinful traveller or not? Statements of the jurists.
The sinful and the obedient in his travel are equal in the concession. And al-Shafi'i said: Travel for sin does not benefit the concession because it is established as a lightening, so it does not attach to that which necessitates severity. Our proof is the generality of the texts, and because travel itself is not sin; rather sin is [garbled] so it is suitable to attach the concession. And Allah knows best.
Translation: And the person who is disobedient in his travel and the person who is obedient in his travel, both are equal in the concession. And Imam Shafi'i said: The travel of sin does not give the benefit of the concession because the concession is established as a lightening, so it will not be attached to that which necessitates severity. Our proof is the generality of the texts, and because travel itself is not sin, and as for sin, it is that which [incomplete].
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi position is that the travel concessions (such as shortening prayers and breaking fast) apply equally to all travellers, whether the purpose of the travel is obedient or sinful. Imam Shafi'i holds that a sinful travel does not entitle one to the concessions because concessions are lightenings, and they should not be attached to matters that require severity. The Hanafi response is that the texts of the Quran and Sunnah are general (mutlaq) and do not differentiate between righteous and sinful travel. Moreover, travel itself is not a sin; the sin lies in the intention or action accompanying the travel. Therefore, the concession attaches to the travel itself, not the sin. The text ends abruptly but the Hanafi stance is clear.

Key Terms
رخصت (rukhsah): Concession or dispensation, e.g., shortening prayers or breaking fast during travel.
عاصی (asi): Disobedient; one whose travel involves sin (e.g., robbery, fleeing from justice).
اطلاق نصوص (itlaq al-nusus): The general, unqualified nature of the textual proofs (Quran and Sunnah) that do not impose conditions on travel for concessions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person travels for robbery, does he still get the concession to shorten his prayer?
A) No, because the travel is sinful.
B) Yes, because travel itself is not sin and the texts are general.
C) Yes, only if he repents first.
D) No, because the sin negates the lightening.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants travel concessions to all travellers, regardless of the purpose of travel, because the texts are general and travel itself is not sinful.

Ruling on Qadā' According to the End of Time
Ruling with proof on qadā' according to the end of time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of rak'ahs in qadā' for prayers missed in travel and residence and explain why the end of the time is the determining factor.

Core Idea
Make-up prayer mirrors the obligation at the end of the prayer's time, not its beginning.

In this passage from Al-Hidāyah, the author explains a key Hanafi principle: when missing a prayer, the way to make it up depends on the obligation at the very end of the prayer's time, not when it was missed. This determines whether you pray two or four rak'ahs when your travel status changes. Let's unpack the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
State the two cases: prayer missed in travel made up in residence = 2 rak'ahs; prayer missed in residence made up in travel = 4 rak'ahs.
2
State the general principle
The author says qadā' follows adā' (performance). Understand that the obligation in qadā' mirrors what was obligatory in adā'.
3
Determine the operative time
The end of the time (ākhir al-waqt) is what determines whether the obligation is 2 or 4 rak'ahs. 'End of time' means the amount needed for takbīr taḥrīmah.
4
Apply the principle to an example
If resident at start but traveler at end, qadā' is 2 rak'ahs. This is because the end of the time is the cause when performance did not occur.
5
Address the objection
Some argue the entire time is the cause, but the Hanafi position adopts the end of the time as the cause for missed prayers. This ensures consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من فاتته صلاة في السفر قضاءها في الحضر ركعتين ومن فاتته في الحضر قضاها في السفر اربعا لان القضاء بحسب الاداء والمعتبر في ذلك آخر الوقت لانه المعتبر في السبية عند عدم الاداء في الوقت ترجمہ اور جس شخص کی کوئی نماز سفر میں فوت ہو گئی تو حضر میں اس کو دو رکعت قضاء کرے اور جس کی نماز حضر میں فوت ہوگئی تو اس کو سفر میں چار رکعت قضاء کرے کیونکہ قضاء ادا کے موافق ہوتی ہے اور اس میں معتبر آخر وقت ہے کیونکہ آخری وقت ہی سبب ہونے میں معتبر ہوتا ہے جبکہ وقت کے اند ادا نہ کیا ہو۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ سفر کی حالت میں اگر رباعی نماز فوت ہوگئی اور حضر میں اس کو قضاء کرنا چاہا تو دو رکعت قضاء کرے اور حضر کے زمانے میں کوئی نماز فوت ہو گئی پھر سفر کی حالت میں اس کو قضاء کرنا چاہا تو چار رکعت قضاء کرے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ قضاء ادا کے موافق واجب ہوتی ہے یعنی جس شخص پر ادا چار رکعت واجب ہوئی تو وہ قضاء بھی چار رکعت کرے گا۔ اور جس پر دو رکعت ادا کرنا واجب ہوا اس پر قضاء بھی دو رکعت کی واجب ہو گی۔ اور ادا کے اندر وقت کا آخر معتبر ہے آخر وقت سے مراد مقدار تحریمہ ہے مثلا اگر ظہر کے اول وقت میں مقیم تھا کچھ وقت ختم ہونے سے پہلے سفر کے لئے نکالا اور آبادی سے باہر اس وقت ہوا جب کہ وقت صرف ایک رکعت کا یا کم باقی ہے تو اس پر دو ہی رکعت کی قضا واجب ہوگی کیونکہ آخر وقت میں وہ مسافر ہو چکا۔ اور یہی معتبر ہے۔ اور ادا کے اندر وقت کا آخر اس لئے معتبر ہے کہ وقت کے اندر ادا کرنے کی صورت میں وجوب نماز کا سبب ہونے میں آخر وقت معتبر ہے۔ اس موقع پر ایک اعتراض ہوسکتا ہے وہ یہ کہ ہمارا کلام قضاء نماز میں ہے۔ اور نماز جب اپنے وقت سے فوت ہوگئی تو اصل فقہ کے بیان کے مطابق پورا وقت نماز کا سبب ہوتا ہے نہ کہ آخری جز : جواب بعض مشائخ کے نزدیک نماز فوت ہونے کی صورت میں وقت کا آخری جز سبب ہوتا ہے۔ بہت ممکن ہے کہ مصنف ہدایہ نے اس کو اختیار کیا ہو۔
Whoever misses a prayer in travel, its make-up in residence is two rak'ahs; and whoever misses a prayer in residence, its make-up in travel is four rak'ahs, because make-up is according to performance, and the consideration in that is the end of the time, because it is the consideration in causation when performance did not occur in the time. Urdu: And if a person's prayer was missed in travel, then in residence he should make it up as two rak'ahs; and if his prayer was missed in residence, then in travel he should make it up as four rak'ahs, because make-up corresponds to performance, and in this the end of the time is considered, because the end of the time is considered in being the cause when performance did not occur within the time. Explanation: The case is that if a four-rak'ah prayer was missed during travel and he wishes to make it up in residence, he should make it up as two rak'ahs; and if a prayer was missed in residence and then he wishes to make it up in travel, he should make it up as four rak'ahs. The proof is that make-up is obligatory according to performance: that is, the person upon whom four rak'ahs were obligatory in performance will also perform four rak'ahs in make-up, and the one upon whom two rak'ahs were obligatory in performance will perform two rak'ahs in make-up. In performance, the end of the time is considered; 'end of the time' means the amount of takbīr taḥrīmah. For example, if at the beginning of Zuhr time he was a resident, then he departed for travel before the time ended, and he came out of the inhabited area at a time when only the time of one rak'ah or less remained, then upon him is the obligation of two rak'ahs of make-up, because at the end of the time he had become a traveler, and this is what is considered. The end of the time is considered in performance because in the case of performance within the time, the end of the time is considered in the causation of the obligation. Here a possible objection arises: our discussion is about make-up of prayer, and when a prayer is missed from its time, according to the principles of fiqh, the entire time is the cause of the prayer, not the last part. The answer: according to some mashāyikh, in the case of a missed prayer, the last part of the time is the cause. It is very possible that the author of al-Hidāyah adopted this view.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling regarding how to make up missed prayers when the situation changes between travel and residence. The ruling states that the make-up prayer (qadā') is performed according to the obligation at the time of actual performance (adā'), and the critical moment for determining that obligation is the end of the prescribed time for the prayer. The author explains that if a four-rak'ah prayer is missed during travel and made up in residence, it is performed as two rak'ahs; conversely, if missed in residence and made up in travel, it is performed as four rak'ahs. The reasoning is that make-up follows performance, and in performance, the end of the time is what determines the obligation. For example, if a person was a resident at the start of Zuhr time but travels before the end such that at the end of the time he is a traveler, his make-up will be two rak'ahs because at the end of the time he was a traveler. The passage then addresses a potential objection: some argue that the entire time is the cause for the obligation, not just the end. The response, attributed to some mashāyikh and possibly adopted by the author of al-Hidāyah, is that for a missed prayer, the last part of the time is indeed the cause. This ensures consistency in the ruling.

Key Terms
قضاء (qadā'): The compensatory performance of an obligation after its prescribed time has elapsed.
آخر الوقت (ākhir al-waqt): The final portion of the prayer time, specifically the amount needed to perform at least the tahrīmah, which determines the obligation when the prayer is missed or when the traveler's status changes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person misses the Zuhr prayer while traveling, and later makes it up in residence (hazar), how many rak'ahs should he pray?
A) 2 rak'ahs
B) 4 rak'ahs
C) 3 rak'ahs
D) It depends on whether he was traveling at the end of the time

Key Takeaway
The number of rak'ahs in qadā' is determined by the obligation at the end of the original prayer time, not at the time the prayer was missed.

Rukhsah for the Disobedient Traveler: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute over rukhsah for sinful travel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on rukhsah for the disobedient traveler and explain the opposing Shafi'i view, citing the core proof for each.

Core Idea
Rukhsah is for the traveler, not for the sin; Hanafis grant it generally; Shafi'is withhold it.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute about whether a person traveling to commit a sin is entitled to the same legal concessions as an obedient traveler. The Hanafi school holds that all travelers, regardless of intention, may shorten prayers, break fast, and wipe over socks. The Shafi'i school restricts these concessions to permissible journeys. Understanding this dispute reveals how each school weighs general texts versus the purpose of the concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the point of disagreement
Recognize that both schools agree rukhsah is a concession (takhfif). The dispute is whether it applies to a journey whose purpose is sinful.
The sin is in the purpose or accompanying act, not in the act of traveling itself.
2
State the Hanafi position and its basis
Hanafis argue from the generality of Quranic verses (e.g., 2:185) and hadiths (e.g., 'The obligatory prayer of the traveler is two rak'ahs') that mention 'traveler' without qualification. Travel itself is neutral; sin is incidental.
The generality of the texts is the primary Hanafi proof.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its basis
Shafi'is argue that rukhsah, being a concession (takhfif), cannot attach to something that deserves severity (taghliz), i.e., sin. Thus, a sinful journey is not eligible for rukhsah.
This reasoning is based on the purpose and nature of the concession.
4
Compare the usul principles underlying each
Hanafis prioritize the apparent meaning (zahir) of the texts and consider travel an objective fact. Shafi'is consider the rationale (illah) of rukhsah and restrict it to situations that are compatible with mercy.
This reflects a difference in how each school uses textual generality vs. teleological reasoning.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, Hanafis allow a disobedient traveler (e.g., a robber or runaway) to shorten salah, while Shafi'is require full prayers. The same difference applies to other rukhas like breaking fast in Ramadan.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school is the permissive position.

والعاصي والمطيع في سفره في الرخصة سواء وقال الشافعي سفر المعصية لا يفيد الرخصة لانها تثبت تخفيفا فلا تتعلق بما يوجب التغليظ ولنا اطلاق النصوص ولان نفس السفر ليس بمعصية وانما المعصية تكون بعد او معه ارادہ سے سفر کرنا یا عورت کا بغیر محرم کے حج کے لئے سفر کرنا۔ اول کی دو قسمیں بالاتفاق رخصت کا سبب ہیں اور تیسری قسم کے نزدیک تو رخصت کا سبب ہے لیکن امام شافعی کے نزدیک سبب نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یعنی معصیت اور نافرمانی تو سختی اور عذاب واجب کرتی ہے اس کے ساتھ رخصت اور تخفیف متعلق نہیں ہوسکتی۔ آپ اس کو اس طرح بھی کہہ سکتے ہیں کہ رخصت تو رحمت و انعام ہے وہ عذاب کے مستحق کو نہیں ملے گی۔ ہماری دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نفس سفر معصیت نہیں ہے کیونکہ سفر نام ہے قطع مسافت کا، اور اس معنی میں کوئی معصیت نہیں معصیت تو وہ ہے جو قطع مسافت کے بعد ہوگی مثلاً ڈاکہ زنی یا چوری یا معصیت سفر کے ساتھ ساتھ ہوتی ہے جیسے غلام کا بھاگ جانا۔ پس جب ذات سفر معصیت نہیں ہے تو اس کے ساتھ رخصت متعلق ہو سکتی ہے۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد القاسمی
The disobedient and the obedient in their travel are equal in terms of rukhsah. Al-Shāfiʿī said: The travel of disobedience does not confer rukhsah, because rukhsah is established as a concession, so it cannot be related to something that necessitates harshness. Our proof is the generality of texts, and because travel itself is not a sin; rather, sin occurs after or with it, so travel is suitable for rukhsah to be attached to it. And Allah knows best. Urdu: The person who is disobedient in his travel and the person who is obedient in his travel are equal in rukhsah. Imam Shāfiʿī said: The travel of disobedience does not benefit rukhsah, because rukhsah establishes a concession, so it will not be related to something that necessitates harshness. Our proof is the generality of texts, and because travel itself is not a sin; as for sin, it is something that either arises afterward or accompanies the travel. Therefore, travel is worthy for rukhsah to be attached to it. Explanation: According to the fuqahā, there are three types of travel: travel of obedience (e.g., Hajj and Jihad), travel that is permissible (e.g., trade), and travel of disobedience (e.g., traveling with the intention of highway robbery, or a woman traveling for Hajj without a mahram). The first two types are causes for rukhsah by consensus. As for the third type, in our view it is a cause for rukhsah, but Imam Shāfiʿī does not consider it a cause. Imam Shāfiʿī's proof is that rukhsah alleviates the burden on the legally responsible person, and something that alleviates cannot be attached to something that necessitates severity; so rukhsah cannot be attached to something that necessitates severity, meaning disobedience and sin necessitate hardship and punishment. Rukhsah, being mercy and favor, cannot be granted to one deserving of punishment. Our proof is that the texts granting rukhsah are absolute and include every traveler without distinction. For example, Allah said: 'Whoever is ill or on a journey, then a number of other days' (al-Baqarah 2:185). The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'The obligatory prayer of the traveler is two rak'ahs.' In another place he said: 'The resident wipes for one day and night, and the traveler for three days and nights.' These texts do not differentiate between obedient and disobedient; rather, they include the traveler whether he is obedient or disobedient. Our second proof is that travel itself is not a sin, because travel is merely covering distance, and in that sense there is no sin. Sin is something that occurs after covering distance (e.g., robbery, theft) or accompanies travel (e.g., a runaway slave). Since the essence of travel is not sin, rukhsah can be attached to it. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad al-Qasimi.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage addresses an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shāfiʿīs regarding whether a person traveling for a sinful purpose (safar al-maʿṣiyah) is entitled to the same concessions (rukhas) as an obedient traveler. The Hanafi position, attributed to Imām Abū Ḥanīfah and his school, is that both the disobedient and obedient traveler are equal in receiving rukhsah. The Shāfiʿī position, as stated by Imām al-Shāfiʿī, is that a sinful journey does not confer rukhsah. The text then provides the Hanafi reasoning: (1) the general texts (Quran and Sunnah) that mention rukhsah for the traveler are absolute and do not distinguish between obedient and disobedient journeys; (2) travel itself (qatʿ al-masāfah) is not inherently a sin; sin is an external factor that either occurs after or alongside travel, so the act of travel remains suitable for the attachment of rukhsah. The passage also categorizes travel into three types: obedience (e.g., Hajj, Jihad), permissible (e.g., trade), and disobedience (e.g., robbery). The first two are agreed upon as causes for rukhsah, while the third is contested. The Shāfiʿī proof is that rukhsah, being a concession, cannot apply to something that deserves severity (i.e., sin). The Hanafi response reiterates the generality of the texts and the neutrality of travel itself. This highlights a key difference in the legal principles: Hanafis give greater weight to the literal and general application of texts, while Shāfiʿīs consider the purpose and context of the concession.

Key Terms
رخصة (rukhsah): A legal concession granted by the Lawgiver that permits something otherwise prohibited or modifies an original ruling due to a valid excuse (e.g., travel, illness).
معصية (maʿṣiyah): Sin or disobedience to Allah; in this context, the sin is the purpose or accompanying action of the journey, not the journey itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No, because his travel is sinful.
B) Yes, because travel itself is not sin and the texts are general.
C) Yes, but only if he repents during the journey.
D) No, because shortening salah is only for those traveling for obedience.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants rukhsah to all travelers based on general texts, distinguishing between the act of travel (neutral) and the motive (sinful or not).

Friday Prayer: Definition and Obligation
Definition and proofs of obligation for Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the Hanafi school classifies Friday prayer as fard 'ayn and explain the Quranic proof from Surah al-Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is fard 'ayn, proven by the Quranic command to hasten to the khutbah.

This lesson introduces the Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) and establishes its obligation. The author explains why the chapter on Friday follows the traveler's prayer—both involve a reduction in rak'ahs. Then the term 'Jumu'ah' is defined, and the obligation is proven using the Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and rational evidence. The key proof is the verse from Surah al-Jumu'ah, where the imperative 'hasten' indicates obligation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the chapter placement
Note why the Friday prayer chapter follows the traveler's prayer: both involve reduction (tansif). Travel reduces all four-rak'ah prayers, while the Friday khutbah only reduces Zuhr. Since the specific follows the general, Friday prayer is discussed after the traveler's prayer.
This is a structural insight for memorization.
2
Define Jumu'ah linguistically and legally
Jumu'ah derives from 'ijtimā' (gathering). It is the Friday congregational prayer of two rak'ahs preceded by two khutbahs, replacing Zuhr.
Variations in vowel points (ḍammah, sukūn, fatḥah) are noted.
3
Identify the sources of obligation
The text states four sources: Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and rational proof. Focus on the Quranic proof.
The Quranic verse is the primary evidence.
4
Analyze the Quranic argument
Verse 62:9 commands: 'When the call is made... hasten to the remembrance of Allah.' 'Remembrance' is interpreted as the khutbah. The imperative 'is'aw' indicates obligation (wujūb) in Hanafi usul.
From the obligation of hastening to the khutbah, the obligation of the prayer itself follows by first priority (awlawiyyat).
5
Summarize the ruling
Friday prayer is fard 'ayn for every free, adult, male resident. This is established by definitive evidence (qat'i thubut but zanni dalala regarding interpretation).
The obligation is unanimous across schools.

Source Text

باب صلوة الجمعة ترجمہ ( یہ ) باب جمعہ کی نماز (کے بیان میں) ہے شرح یہ باب پہلے باب کے مناسب ہے اس لئے دونوں میں تنصیف ہے البتہ قصر کے اندر سفر کے واسطہ سے تنصیف کی گئی ہے اور جمعہ کے اندر خطبہ کے واسطے سے مگر چونکہ سفر ہر رباعی نماز کے لئے تنصیف کر دیتا ہے۔ اور خطبہ جمعہ فقط ظہر کی نماز کی تنصیف کرتا ہے اس لئے سفر ہر رباعی نماز کی تنصیف کو عام ہوا اور خطبہ فقط ظہر کی نماز کی تنصیف کو خاص ہے۔ اور خاص کا ذکر چونکہ عام کے بعد ہوتا ہے اس لئے صلوٰۃ سفر کے بعد صلوۃ جمعہ کا بیان ہوا۔ جمعہ اجتماع سے ہے جیسے فرقت افتراق سے ہے لفظ جمعہ میم کے ضمہ کے ساتھ ہے اور سکون کے ساتھ بھی پڑھا گیا ہے بعض حضرات میم کے فتحہ کے ساتھ بھی نقل کیا ہے جمعہ کو جمعہ اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ لوگ اس دن میں اکٹھا ہوتے ہیں۔ نماز جمعہ کی فرضیت کتاب سنت اجماع اور دلیل عقلی چاروں سے ثابت ہے۔ کتاب اللہ سے تو اس لئے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا نُودِيَ لِلصَّلَاةِ مِن يَوْمِ الجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ وَذَرُوا البَيْعَ مشہور قول کے مطابق ذکر اللہ سے مراد خطبہ ہے۔ اور اسعوا امر کا صیغہ سب کے لئے ہے۔ پس آیت سے خطبہ کی طرف سعی کا واجب ہونا ثابت ہوا اور سعی الی الخطبة جمعہ کی نماز کے شرائط میں سے ہے پس جب جمعہ کی شرط یعنی سعی الی الخطبة کا واجب ہونا ثابت ہوا تو نماز جمعہ جو مقصود ہے بدرجہ اولی واجب (فرض) ہوگی اس وجوب کو مؤکد کرنے کے
Chapter of Friday Prayer. Translation: (This) is the chapter concerning the prayer of Friday. Explanation: This chapter is appropriate after the previous chapter, because both involve reduction (tansīf). However, in the case of qaṣr, reduction is due to travel, and in the case of Jumuʿah, reduction is due to the khutbah. But because travel reduces every four-rakʿah prayer, and the khutbah of Jumuʿah reduces only the Ẓuhr prayer, therefore travel's reduction is general, and the khutbah's reduction is specific. And since the specific is mentioned after the general, the chapter on Friday prayer comes after the chapter on the traveler's prayer. Jumuʿah is derived from ijtimāʿ (gathering), just as furqah (separation) is from iftirāq. The word 'Jumuʿah' is read with ḍammah on the mīm and also with sukūn; some have also reported it with fatḥah on the mīm. It is called Jumuʿah because people gather on this day. The obligation of Friday prayer is established by the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and rational proof. From the Book: because Allah said: 'O you who believe! When the call is made for prayer on the day of Jumuʿah, then hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off trade' (al-Jumuʿah 62:9). According to the well-known interpretation, 'remembrance of Allah' refers to the khutbah. And 'hasten' (isʿaw) is a command addressed to all. Thus the verse proves the obligation of hastening to the khutbah. And hastening to the khutbah is a condition for Friday prayer. So when the condition (saʿy ilā al-khuṭbah) is proven obligatory, then Friday prayer itself, which is the objective, is even more so obligatory (farḍ). To emphasize this obligation...
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Friday prayer (Ṣalāt al-Jumuʿah). The author first explains the placement of this chapter after the chapter on the traveler's prayer: both involve a reduction (tansīf) in the number of rakʿahs, but travel reduces all four-rakʿah prayers while the Friday khutbah only reduces the Ẓuhr prayer. Since the specific (khutbah) comes after the general (travel), the chapter on Friday follows that on travel. Then the term 'Jumuʿah' is defined linguistically as 'gathering' (ijtimāʿ), with variations in vowel points. The core of the passage is the establishment of the obligation (farḍiyyah) of Friday prayer through four sources: the Quran, the Sunnah, consensus (ijmāʿ), and rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī). The primary Quranic evidence is Sūrat al-Jumuʿah, verse 9, where 'remembrance of Allah' (dhikr Allāh) is interpreted by many as the khutbah. The imperative 'hasten' (isʿaw) indicates obligation. From this, the obligation of attending the khutbah is derived, and since the khutbah is a condition for the prayer, the prayer itself is even more clearly obligatory. This establishes the farḍiyyah of Jumuʿah.

Key Terms
جمعہ (jumuʿah): The Friday congregational prayer that replaces the Ẓuhr prayer, consisting of two rakʿahs preceded by two khutbahs.
فرضیت (farḍiyyah): The quality of being an obligation (farḍ) established by definitive evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 'Establish prayer and give zakah.'
C) 'And when the prayer is concluded, disperse through the land.'
D) 'Indeed, the prayer is prescribed for the believers at fixed times.'

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is a fard ʿayn established by the Quranic command to hasten to the khutbah, making it a binding obligation on every eligible Muslim male.

Does Rukhsah Apply to Sinful Travel? Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on rukhsah for sinful travel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on rukhsah for sinful travel, explain the Hanafi proof from textual umum, and apply the ruling to a woman traveling without mahram.

Core Idea
Rukhsah attaches to the act of travel itself, not to the traveler's intention.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: does a traveler who is engaged in a sinful journey (e.g., robbery) still qualify for the legal concessions (rukhsah) of travel, such as shortening prayer and breaking fast? The Hanafi school says yes; Imam al-Shafi'i says no. Let's examine the reasoning on both sides and see how the Hanafi school defends its position using the generality of primary texts and the nature of travel.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the disagreement
State the three categories of travel (obedience, permissible, sinful). Note that the dispute is only about the third category: does rukhsah apply to sinful travel?
2
2. State the Shafi'i position and proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that rukhsah is a mercy/lightening, and sin deserves punishment, so they cannot combine. Articulate this as a qiyas: asl = sin warrants punishment, far' = rukhsah granting lightening, illa = incompatibility.
Shafi'i proof is based on the nature of rukhsah as a favor.
3
3. State the Hanafi position and proofs
Hanafi relies on two proofs: (a) the absolute wording of Quran 2:184 and hadiths – they say 'traveler' without qualification; (b) the essence of travel (covering distance) is not sinful – sin is either after or accompanying, not inherent.
The second proof is a ta'lil that separates sin from the act of travel.
4
4. Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply the difference to a concrete scenario: a woman traveling for Hajj without a mahram. Under Hanafi, she shortens and breaks fast; under Shafi'i, she prays full and fasts.
This practical consequence shows the importance of the dispute.
5
5. Conclude with the mufta bihi
The Hanafi school adopts the position that rukhsah applies to all travelers, as stated in the text. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

جد پیدا ہوگی یا سفر کے ساتھ ساتھ ہوگی۔ پس سفر اس کو لائق ہوا کہ رخصت اس سے متعلق ہو۔ شریح فقہاء کے بیان کے مطابق سفر کی تین قسمیں ہیں۔ سفر طاعت جیسے حج اور جہاد، سفر مباح جیسے تجارت، سفر معصیت جیسے ڈاکہ زنی کے ارادہ سے سفر کرنا یا عورت کا بغیر محرم کے حج کے لئے سفر کرنا۔ اول کی دو قسمیں بالاتفاق رخصت کا سبب ہیں اور تیسری قسم ہمارے نزدیک تو رخصت کا سبب ہے لیکن امام شافعی کے نزدیک سبب نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رخصت مکلف پر تخفیف کر دیتی ہے اور جو چیز مکلف پر تخفیف کرتی ہے وہ ایسی چیز کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہوتی جو مکلف کو واجب کرتی ہے اس لئے رخصت ایسی چیز کے ساتھ تعلق نہیں ہوگی جو مکلف کو واجب کرتی ہے یعنی معصیت اور نافرمانی تو سختی اور عذاب واجب کرتی ہے اس کے ساتھ رخصت اور تخفیف متعلق نہیں ہو سکتی۔ آپ اس کو اس طرح بھی کہہ سکتے ہیں کہ رخصت تو رحمت و انعام ہے وہ عذاب کے مستحق کو نہیں ملے گی۔ ہماری دلیل نصوص کا مطلق ہونا ہے یعنی جن نصوص میں رخصت ملی ہے وہ علی الاطلاق ہر مسافر کو شامل ہے مثلا اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے {مَنْ كَانَ مَرِيضًا أَوْ عَلَى سَفَرٍ فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ} حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے فرض المسافر ركعتان دوسری جگہ روایت ہے يمسح المقيم يوماً و ليلته و المسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليهن ان نصوص میں مطیع اور عاصی کی کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے بلکہ سفر کو شامل ہے خواہ اپنے سفر میں مطیع ہو یا عاصی ہو۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ نفس سفر معصیت نہیں ہے کیونکہ سفر نام ہے قطع مسافت کا، اور اس معنی میں کوئی معصیت نہیں معصیت تو وہ ہے جو قطع مسافت کے بعد ہوگی مثلاً ڈاکہ زنی یا چوری یا معصیت سفر کے ساتھ ساتھ ہوتی ہے جیسے غلام کا بھاگ جانا۔ پس جب ذات سفر معصیت نہیں ہے تو اس کے ساتھ رخصت متعلق ہو سکتی ہے۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد القاسمی
When travel occurs or accompanies, the travel becomes deserving that the concession relates to it. Explanation: According to the jurists, travel is of three types: travel of obedience like Hajj and Jihad, permissible travel like trade, and sinful travel like traveling with the intention of robbery or a woman traveling for Hajj without a mahram. The first two types are unanimously a cause for concession, and the third type is a cause in our view, but in the view of Imam Shafi'i it is not a cause. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that concession lessens the burden on the legally responsible person, and that which lessens his burden does not relate to that which makes punishment obligatory. Therefore concession cannot relate to that which makes punishment obligatory, i.e., sin and disobedience necessitate severity and punishment, and concession and alleviation cannot relate to them. You can also express it this way: concession is mercy and favor; it will not be given to one deserving punishment. Our proof is the absoluteness of the texts: the texts that give concession absolutely include every traveler. For example, Allah Almighty said: {Whoever is ill or on a journey, then a number of other days} and the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'The prayer of a traveler is two rak'ahs.' In another narration: 'A resident wipes for one day and one night, and a traveler for three days and their nights.' These texts make no distinction between obedient and disobedient; they include the traveler, whether he is obedient in his travel or disobedient. The second proof is that the essence of travel is not sin, because travel is merely covering distance, and there is no sin in that meaning. Sin occurs after covering the distance, like robbery or theft, or accompanies the travel, like a slave fleeing. Since the essence of travel is not sin, concession can relate to it. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad al-Qasimi.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether rukhsah (legal concession) applies to a traveler who is engaged in sinful travel. The Hanafi position is that rukhsah applies to all travelers unconditionally, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it to those traveling for obedience. The text first categorizes travel into three types: travel for obedience (e.g., Hajj and Jihad), permissible travel (e.g., trade), and sinful travel (e.g., robbery or a woman traveling without a mahram for Hajj, which is sinful in her case). The Hanafi and Shafi'i agree that the first two types are causes for concession. The disagreement is on the third. Imam al-Shafi'i's argument is that concession lightens the burden on the mukallaf, and since sin warrants punishment, concession cannot be granted alongside sin. The Hanafi response is twofold. First, the primary texts (Quran 2:184 and hadith on wiping over khuffain and shortening prayer) are absolute and apply to all travelers without distinction. Second, the essence of travel itself is not sinful; sin may accompany the travel but is not inherent to the act of traveling itself. Therefore, concession can validly attach to it. The author concludes with 'And Allah knows best' and the name Jamil Ahmad al-Qasimi, likely the commentator.

Key Terms
رخصت (rukhsah): A legal concession that lightens or replaces an original ruling due to a valid excuse, such as travel.
سفر (safar): Journey covering a distance that makes qasr and other concessions permissible. It is defined as covering approximately 48 miles (3 marhalas).
عاصی (aasi): One who commits sin. In this context, a traveler whose purpose is sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the Hanafi position on rukhsah for a traveler who is traveling to commit robbery?
A) He is not entitled to any rukhsah because his journey is sinful.
B) He is entitled to rukhsah because the texts are absolute and include all travelers.
C) He is entitled to rukhsah only if he repents before traveling.
D) The ruling depends on the distance of the journey.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the concessions of travel (qasr, iftar, etc.) apply to every traveler regardless of the purpose of the journey, because the texts are general and the act of travel itself is not sinful.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Proofs for the Obligation of Friday Prayer
Presentation of proofs from Quran, Hadith, Ijma, and reason for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four proofs for the obligation of Jumu'ah prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain how each proof establishes fard 'ain.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is fard 'ain — proven by Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and the principle that an obligation can only be replaced by an obligation.

The obligation of Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) is a consensus among all Muslims, but its proof structure in the Hanafi school is meticulously layered. In this passage, the author of Al-Hidayah presents a comprehensive case: from the clear command in Surah al-Jumu'ah to the severe warnings in the hadith, the unanimous agreement of the Ummah, and a rational demonstration that Jumu'ah must be fard because it replaces the certain obligation of Zuhr. By the end, you will be able to articulate each proof and understand why every Hanafi authority agrees on this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Jumu'ah prayer is ruled fard 'ain (individual obligation) on every qualified Muslim.
Qualified means free, male, adult, healthy, resident, not traveling, with no valid excuse.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof
The verse (Surah al-Jumu'ah 62:9) commands hastening to 'the remembrance of Allah' and prohibiting trade. Interpretations: either the khutbah (well-known) or the prayer itself (Ibn al-Humam). Both lead to obligation.
The prohibition of trade indicates that even permissible acts must be left for Jumu'ah.
3
Examine the hadith proofs
Four hadith are cited: one declaring Allah's prescription, one calling it a 'right obligatory' with exemptions, and two with severe warnings for abandonment.
Severe warnings (e.g., being written as a hypocrite) are characteristic of leaving a fard.
4
Acknowledge the Ijma'
The entire ummah has agreed upon the obligation of Jumu'ah, so it is established by consensus.
Ijma' is an independent proof that reinforces the textual evidence.
5
Understand the rational proof
Jumu'ah replaces Zuhr, which is definitely fard. An obligation can only be replaced by another obligation, so Jumu'ah must also be fard.
This is a logical argument (qiyas) based on the priority of obligations.

باب صلوة الجمعة
ترجمہ ( یہ ) باب جمعہ کی نماز (کے بیان میں) ہے
شریح یہ باب پہلے باب کے مناسب ہے اس لئے دونوں میں تنصیف ہے البتہ قصر کے اندر سفر کے واسطہ سے تنصیف کی گئی ہے اور جمعہ کے اندر خطبہ کے واسطے سے مگر چونکہ سفر ہر رباعی نماز کے لئے تنصیف کر دیتا ہے۔ اور خطبہ جمعہ فقط ظہر کی نماز کی تنصیف کرتا ہے اس لئے سفر ہر رباعی نماز کی تنصیف کو عام ہوا اور خطبہ فقط ظہر کی نماز کی تنصیف کو خاص ہے۔ اور خاص کا ذکر چونکہ عام کے بعد ہوتا ہے اس لئے صلوٰۃ سفر کے بعد صلوۃ جمعہ کا بیان ہوا۔
جمعہ اجتماع سے ہے جیسے فرقت افتراق سے ہے لفظ جمعہ میم کے ضمہ کے ساتھ ہے اور سکون کے ساتھ بھی پڑھا گیا ہے بعض حضرات میم کے فتحہ کے ساتھ بھی نقل کیا ہے جمعہ کو جمعہ اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ لوگ اس دن میں اکٹھا ہوتے ہیں۔ نماز جمعہ کی فرضیت کتاب سنت اجماع اور دلیل عقلی چاروں سے ثابت ہے۔ کتاب اللہ سے تو اس لئے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے {يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا نُودِيَ لِلصَّلَاةِ مِنْ يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ وَذَرُوا الْبَيْعَ} مشہور قول کے مطابق ذکر اللہ سے مراد خطبہ ہے۔ اور اسعوا امر کا صیغہ سب کے لئے ہے۔ پس آیت سے خطبہ کی طرف سعی کا واجب ہونا ثابت ہوا اور سعی الی الخطبہ جمعہ کی نماز کے شرائط میں سے ہے پس جب جمعہ کی شرط یعنی سعی الی الخطبہ کا واجب ہونا ثابت ہوا تو نماز جمعہ جو مقصود ہے بدرجہ اولیٰ واجب (فرض) ہوگی اس وجوب کو مؤکد کرنے کے لئے فرمایا وذروا البیع یعنی اذان جمعہ کے بعد خرید وفروخت کو حرام کیا گیا حالانکہ خرید وفروخت مباح ہے اور یہ اصول ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ مباح کو کسی امر واجب کی وجہ سے ہی حرام کرتے ہیں پس ثابت ہوا کہ جمعہ جس کی وجہ سے اذان کے بعد بیع کو حرام کیا گیا واجب (فرض) ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے فرمایا کہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ ذکر اللہ سے نماز مراد ہو اس صورت میں براہ راست نماز جمعہ کا فرض ہونا ثابت ہوگا۔ مفسرین نے ذکر اللہ کی تفسیر نماز اور خطبہ دونوں سے کی ہے علامہ ابن الہمام نے کہا ہے کہ یہ زیادہ مناسب ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں آیت نماز اور خطبہ دونوں پر صادق آئے گا۔
حدیث جس سے نماز جمعہ کی فرضیت ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ یہ ہے اعلموا ان الله كتب عليكم الجمعة في يومي هذا في شهري هذا في مقامي هذا جان لو کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہارے اوپر جمعہ فرض کیا ہے میرے اس دن میں میرے اس مہینہ میں میرے اس مقام میں۔ دوسری حدیث الجمعة حق واجب على كل مسلم في جماعة الا اربعة مملوك او امرأة او صبي او مريض رواه ابو داود جمعہ کی نماز ہر مسلمان پر جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھنا حق واجب یعنی فرض ہے مگر چار آدمیوں پر غلام عورت نابالغ بچہ اور بیمار پر تیسری حدیث قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من ترك ثلاث جمعات من غير عذر كتب من المنافقين رسول اللہ صلى اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس شخص نے تین جمعہ بغیر عذر کے چھوڑے اس کا شمار منافقین میں ہوگا۔ چوتھی حدیث من ترك الجمع ثلاث جمع متواليات فقد نبذ الاسلام وراء ظهره جس نے مسلسل تین جمعوں کو ترک کر دیا اس نے اسلام پس پشت ڈال دیا۔ ان دونوں حدیثوں میں ترک جمعہ پر سخت وعید بیان کی گئی ہے۔ اور ظاہر ہے کہ وعید فرض چھوڑنے پر آتی ہے۔ پس ان دونوں حدیثوں سے بھی جمعہ کا فرض ہونا ثابت ہوا۔ چونکہ پوری امت مسلمہ جمعہ کے فرض ہونے پر متفق ہو گئی اس لئے اجماع سے بھی جمعہ کی نماز کا فرض ہونا ثابت ہوا۔ جمعہ کی فرضیت پر عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہم کو جمعہ قائم کرنے کے لئے ظہر کی نماز چھوڑنے کا امر کیا گیا ہے اور ظہر کی نماز بالیقین فرض ہے۔ اور یہ بات بھی مسلمات میں سے ہے کہ فرض کو فرض ہی کی وجہ سے چھوڑا جا سکتا ہے نفل کی وجہ سے نہیں پس اس سے بھی جمعہ کا فرض ہونا ثابت ہوا۔
Chapter of Friday Prayer. Translation: This chapter is about the prayer of Friday. Explanation: This chapter is appropriate after the previous chapter because both involve reduction (tansif). In qasr, reduction is due to travel; in Jumu'ah, reduction is due to the khutbah. However, travel reduces every four-rak'ah prayer, while the khutbah reduces only the Zuhr prayer, so travel reduction is general and khutbah reduction is specific. Since specific is mentioned after general, the chapter on travel prayer is followed by the chapter on Jumu'ah. Jumu'ah is from 'ijtima' (gathering), just as 'furqat' is from 'iftiraq'. The word Jumu'ah is read with dammah on the meem, and also with sukoon; some have even narrated with fatha. It is called Jumu'ah because people gather on this day. The obligation of Friday prayer is established from four sources: the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and rational proof. From the Book: Allah Almighty said: {O you who believe, when the call is made for prayer on the day of Jumu'ah, hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off trade}. According to the well-known opinion, 'remembrance of Allah' means the khutbah. The word 'fas'aw' (hasten) is a command for everyone. Thus the verse establishes the obligation of hastening to the khutbah, and hastening to the khutbah is among the conditions of Jumu'ah. Since the condition (hastening to khutbah) is obligatory, then the Jumu'ah prayer itself is even more obligatory (fard). To emphasize this obligation, He said 'and leave off trade', meaning that after the adhan, buying and selling is prohibited, although trade is normally permissible. It is a principle that Allah only prohibits a permissible thing for the sake of something obligatory. Thus it is established that Jumu'ah, for which trade is prohibited after the adhan, is obligatory (fard). Allamah Ibn al-Humam said: The apparent meaning is that 'remembrance of Allah' refers to the prayer itself; in that case the obligation of Jumu'ah prayer itself would be directly established. The commentators have interpreted 'remembrance of Allah' as both prayer and khutbah; Allamah Ibn al-Humam said this is more appropriate because then the verse would apply to both prayer and khutbah. From the Hadith: The first hadith: 'Know that Allah has prescribed Jumu'ah upon you on this day, in this month, in this place of mine.' The second hadith: 'Jumu'ah is a right obligatory upon every Muslim in congregation except four: a slave, a woman, a minor, and a sick person' (narrated by Abu Dawud). The third hadith: The Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'Whoever leaves three Jumu'ahs without an excuse is written among the hypocrites.' The fourth hadith: 'Whoever leaves Jumu'ah for three consecutive Fridays has cast Islam behind his back.' Both these hadiths contain severe warnings for leaving Jumu'ah, and it is clear that warnings come for leaving an obligation. So from these two hadiths too, the obligation of Jumu'ah is established. Since the entire Muslim nation has agreed upon the obligation of Jumu'ah, it is established by consensus. The rational proof: We are commanded to leave the Zuhr prayer in order to establish Jumu'ah, and Zuhr is certainly obligatory. It is among accepted principles that an obligation can only be left for another obligation, not for a supererogatory act. Hence this also proves Jumu'ah is obligatory.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, demonstrating that Friday (Jumu'ah) prayer is obligatory (fard 'ain) based on four sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and 'aql. It begins with the chapter heading and a brief explanation of why this chapter comes after the chapter on travel prayer: both involve reduction (tansif), but travel reduction is general for all four-rak'ah prayers while Jumu'ah reduction is specific to Zuhr due to the khutbah. Linguistic definition: Jumu'ah is derived from 'ijtima' (gathering). The obligation is then proven from the Quran (Surah al-Jumu'ah, verse 9) with two interpretations: 'dhikr Allah' means khutbah (well-known view) or prayer itself (Ibn al-Humam). The command to hasten and the prohibition of trade after the adhan indicate the importance of Jumu'ah. Four hadith are cited: one declaring Allah's prescription, another listing exemptions (slave, woman, child, sick), and two with severe warnings against leaving Jumu'ah, which indicate obligation. Consensus (ijma') is then mentioned as the entire ummah agreed. Finally, a rational argument: since Zuhr, a definite obligation, is replaced by Jumu'ah, Jumu'ah must also be obligatory (an obligation can only be replaced by another obligation).

Key Terms
جمعہ (Jumu'ah): The Friday congregational prayer that replaces Zuhr prayer. Derived from 'ijtima' (gathering).
فرضیت (fardiyyah): The quality of being obligatory (fard). In Hanafi usul, fard is established by qat'i evidence.
خطبہ (khutbah): The sermon delivered before the Jumu'ah prayer, considered a condition for its validity.
تنصیف (tansif): Reduction; here meaning the reduction of rak'ahs in travel (qasr) and the reduction of Zuhr to Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT among the four exceptions listed in the hadith to the obligation of Jumu'ah?
A) Slave
B) Woman
C) Traveler
D) Sick person

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah prayer is fard 'ain on qualified Muslims, proven by Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and rational necessity.

Salah — Prayer

Conditions for Jumu'ah and the Definition of Misr Jami'
Lists conditions for Jumu'ah obligation and validity, with intra-Hanafi definition of misr jami'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for obligation and validity of Jumu'ah, and distinguish between the intra-Hanafi positions on the definition of misr jami'.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only valid in a major city with a governor and judge—this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

This passage from al-Hidayah enumerates twelve conditions for Jumu'ah, but the core Hanafi debate centers on what qualifies as a 'misr jami''. We will examine the hadith evidence, the differing definitions of the early imams, and why Imam al-Karkhi's choice of Abu Yusuf's first narration became the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sets of conditions
Distinguish between conditions for obligation (six personal, six external) and conditions for validity (misr jami').
OCR corruption affects the personal conditions here.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith 'There is no Jumu'ah except in a misr jami'' is the primary textual proof (dalil naqli).
The hadith is narrated by several companions.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's definition
Abu Hanifa: misr jami' requires streets, markets, a ruler, and a scholar for fatwa.
This definition is broader in terms of authority.
4
Compare Abu Yusuf's three narrations
First narration: amir and qadi who enforce judgments and execute hadd punishments. Second: largest mosque capacity. Third: population of 1000 men.
The first is chosen by al-Karkhi and is the apparent madhhab.
5
Understand the tarjih
Imam al-Karkhi preferred the first narration because it ensures the presence of authority necessary for implementing Islamic punishments, which is the rationale behind the condition.
This is the mufta bihi position.

باب صلوة الجمعة

شرائط صحت جمعہ
مح الجمعة الا في مصر جامع اوفى مصلى المصر ولاتجوز فى القرى لقوله عليه السلام لاجمعة الشريق ولا فطر ولا اضحى الا فى مصر جامع والمصر الجامع كل موضع له امير وقاض ينفذ الاحكام يم الحدود وهذا عن ابى يوسف وعنه انهم اذا اجتمعو افى اكبر مساجد هم لم يسعهم والاول اختیار برخى وهو الظاهر والثانى اختيار الثلجى والحكم غير مقصور على المصلى بل يجوز في جميع افنية ب عر لانها بمنزلته في حوائج اهله
جمعہ صحیح نہیں ہوتا مگر شہر جامع میں یا شہر کی فناء میں اور جمعہ گاؤں میں جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا جمعہ تشریق نماز عید اور نماز بقر عید جائز نہیں مگر شہر جامع میں۔ اور شہر جامع ہر وہ موضع کہ اس کا ایک امیر ہو اور قاضی ہو جو حکام کو نافذ ہو اور حدود کو قائم کرتا ہو۔ اور یہ ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف سے یہ بھی مروی ہے کہ جب لوگ وہاں کی سب سے بڑی میں جمع ہوں تو سب لوگوں کی اس میں سائی نہ ہو۔ قول اول کو امام کرختی نے اختیار کیا ہے اور یہی ظاہر مذہب ہے۔ اور قول ثانی کو امام نے اختیار کیا ہے۔ اور جواز کا حکم مسجد فناء پر مخصر نہیں ہے بلکہ شہر کے تمام فناؤں میں جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اہل شہر کی ضروریات کے سلسلہ شر کی فتاء کی تمام جوانب بمنزلہ مصلی کے نہیں ہے۔ متن میں دولفظ مصر جامع اور مصلی المصر قابل تشریح ہیں۔ مصر جامع کی تعریف: مصر جامع کی تعریف میں اختلاف ہے امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک مصر جامع وہ ہے جہاں سٹرکیں ہوں بازار ہوں حاکم ہو جو ظالم اور مظلوم کے درمیان انصاف کرے اور عالم ہو م آمده حوادث میں فتوی دے۔ حضرت امام ابو یوسف سے اس بارے میں تین روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ مصر جامع ہر وہ موضع ہے جس میر اور قاضی ہو جو احکام جاری کرنے اور شرعی سزاؤں کو قائم کرنے پر قادر ہو ۔ ينفذ الاحکام کے بعد یقیم الحدود کی قید لگا کر محکم کو حکم اور فیصل بنایا گیا ہے ) اور عورت قاضیہ سے احتراز کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ عورت کی قضاء جائز ہے مگر اس کو حدود قصاص قائم کرنے کی شرعیہ نہیں ہوتی ۔ مصر جامع کے سلسلہ میں یہی ظاہر مذہب ہے اور اسی کو امام کرخی نے اختیار کیا ہے دوسری روایت یہی کہ مر جامع وہ تا ہے کہ اس موضع کی سب سے بڑی مسجد میں اگر اس موضع کے وہ لوگ جمع ہو جائیں جن پر جمعہ فرض ہے تو اس میں لوگ سمامہ نہیں بلکہ کے لئے دوسری مسجد بنانے کی ضرورت محسوس ہو ۔ اس روایت کو ابوعبداللہ بچی نے اختیار کیا ہے۔ تیسری روایت یہ ہے کہ ایک ہزار کی ان کا موضع میصر جامع ہے سفیان ثوری کہتے ہیں کہ مصر جامع وہ ہے جس کو لوگ شہروں کے تذکرہ کے وقت شہر سمجھیں۔ سر الفظ مصلی ہے۔ شہر کا مصلی عید گاہ ہوتا ہے لیکن یہاں مصلی سے فنا شہر مراد ہے۔ فناء شہر شہر کے اس ماحول ( اردگرد ) کو کہتے ہیں جو
There are twelve conditions for Jumu'ah to be obligatory. Six conditions are necessary to be present in the person himself: (1) free, so it is not obligatory on a slave; (2) male [؟] and traveler? (4) healthy, i.e., not so ill that attending Jumu'ah would be burdensome; (6) eyesight sound and foot sound? ... It is not obligatory on a blind person. Six conditions that are not related to the person himself: being in a city, authority [sultan], congregation, time, sermon, general permission. Conditions of validity of Jumu'ah: Jumu'ah is not gathered except in a major city (misr jami') or in the musalla of the city, and it is not valid in villages due to his statement: 'There is no Jumu'ah, no Eid al-Fitr, no Eid al-Adha except in a major city.' And a major city is every place that has a governor and a judge who executes judgements and establishes penalties. This is from Abu Yusuf. And from him: if they gather in their largest mosque and it does not accommodate them [they may use another]. The first is the choice of al-Karkhi and it is the apparent [madhhab], and the second is the choice of al-Balkhi. The ruling is not restricted to the musalla but is permissible in all open areas (afniyah) of the city because they are like the musalla for the needs of its people. Definition of misr jami' differs: Imam Abu Hanifa said it is where there are streets, markets, a ruler who judges between oppressor and oppressed, and a scholar who gives fatwas in incidents. Three narrations from Imam Abu Yusuf: (1) a place with a governor and judge who can enforce judgements and establish hadd punishments (this is the apparent madhhab, chosen by al-Karkhi); (2) the largest mosque can accommodate all those obliged; (3) a place with one thousand men. Sufyan al-Thawri said it is what people consider a city. The word musalla literally means prayer ground, but here it refers to the fina' (surroundings) of the city.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute. It first enumerates twelve conditions (shurut) for the obligation of Jumu'ah: six relating to the person (freedom, male, residency, health, sound eyesight, sound foot) though the OCR is corrupt; and six external (city, sultan, congregation, time, sermon, general permission). Then it shifts to conditions of validity (sihha): Jumu'ah is only valid in a major city (misr jami') or its musalla area, based on the hadith narrated. The main fiqh discussion is the definition of misr jami'. Abu Hanifa defined it pragmatically: streets, markets, a ruler, and a scholar. Abu Yusuf has three narrations: (1) presence of an amir and qadi who can execute judgements and hadd penalties (this is the relied-upon position, chosen by Imam al-Karkhi and considered the apparent madhhab); (2) the largest mosque can accommodate all those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory; (3) population of one thousand men. The text also clarifies that 'musalla' here means the fina' (outskirts) of the city, not the Eid prayer ground, and that Jumu'ah is permissible in any open area that serves the city's needs.

Key Terms
مصر جامع (misr jami'): A major city where Jumu'ah and Eid prayers are valid; defined variously by Hanafi imams.
فناء (fina'): The open surroundings or outskirts of a city; treated like the musalla for Jumu'ah validity.
شرائط صحت (shurut al-sihha): Conditions for the validity of the prayer; here specifically the requirement of misr jami'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, what is the minimum requirement for a place to be considered a 'misr jami' where Jumu'ah is valid?
A) Population of one thousand men
B) Presence of streets and markets
C) An amir and a qadi who can execute judgements and punishments
D) The largest mosque can accommodate all obligants

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah validity in the Hanafi school depends on the presence of an amir and qadi who can enforce judgments and hadd punishments.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Conditions for Jumu'ah: The Requirement of a Major City (Misr Jami')
Ruling with proof and intra-madhhab elaboration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for Jumu'ah validity regarding the place, identify the proof, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi opinions on what constitutes a misr jami'.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only valid in a major city (misr jami') or its environs (fina'), not in villages.

This passage from the Hidayah clarifies a key Hanafi condition for Friday prayer: it must be performed in a major city or its outskirts. While the proof is a prophetic narration, the definition of 'major city' generated significant debate among the early Hanafi masters. Understanding this condition helps you see how the school prioritises scholarly consensus and practical authority in communal worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its object
State the ruling: Jumu'ah is not valid except in a misr jami' or its fina'. Note where it is invalid: in villages.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited: 'La jumu'ata wa la tashriqa wa la fitra wa la adha illa fi misr jami''. Identify its source and transmission chain.
The text attributes it to the Prophet but it is from Ali (ra) according to some scholars.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the word 'illa' (except) restricts the permissibility of Jumu'ah to a misr jami', thereby excluding villages.
The exclusion (takhsis) is a condition of place.
4
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Outline the definitions of misr jami' by Abu Hanifa (market, ruler, scholar), Abu Yusuf (three narrations: ruler+qadi executing hudud; largest mosque insufficient; 1000 men), and Muhammad (fina size).
The preferred view is Abu Yusuf's first narration as chosen by Karkhi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the operative fatwa requires an amir and qadi who execute hudud, and that fina is determined by custom.
This is the zahir al-madhhab.
