شہر سے متصل اہل شہر کی مصالح کے لئے بنایا گیا ہو جیسے قبرستان، گھوڑ دوڑ کا میدان، چراگاہ، عیدگاہ ، نذریج اور ہمارے زمانہ میں پارک وغیرہ۔ فناء شہر کی تحدید: فناء شہر کی تقدیر اور تحدید کے بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ امام محمد نے ایک غلوۃ کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے اور غلو کا اطلاق تین سو ذراع سے چار سو ذراع تک ہوتا ہے یعنی آبادی سے باہر چار سو ذراع تک فنا شہر کہلائے گا۔ امام ابو یوسف نے ایک میل با دو میل کی تحدید بیان کی ہے چنانچہ ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ اگر امام کی ضرورت کے پیش نظر اہل شہر کے ساتھ شہر سے نکل کر دو میل باہر تک چلا گیا، یہاں تک کہ جمعہ کا وقت ہو گیا تو اس کو جائز ہے کہ اسی جگہ جمعہ کی نماز ادا کر دے۔ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر کوئی میر شہر میں کھڑا ہو کر چیخ مارے یا مؤذن اذان دے تو جہاں تک آواز پہنچے گی وہاں تک فنا شہر کہلائے گا۔ صورت مسئلہ: اس تفصیل کے بعد ملاحظہ ہو کر صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نماز جمعہ شہر اور فناء شہر دونوں جگہ جائز ہے۔ البتہ گاؤں میں جائز نہیں ہے۔
Jumu'ah is not valid except in a major city (misr jami') or in its praying area (musalla), and it is not permissible in villages, because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'There is no Jumu'ah, nor on the day of Tashreeq (Eid), nor Eid al-Fitr, nor Eid al-Adha, except in a major city.' And a major city is every place that has a ruler (amir) and a judge (qadi) who executes rulings and establishes legal punishments. This is from Abu Yusuf. And from him (Abu Yusuf) also: when people gather in the largest mosque and they do not fit, the first opinion is chosen by some and it is the apparent (zahir) position, and the second opinion is chosen by Thalji. And the ruling is not limited to the musalla, but it is permitted in all the open spaces (fina) of the city because they are like the musalla for the needs of its people.
Jumu'ah is not valid except in a major city or its fina, and Jumu'ah is not permissible in a village, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Jumu'ah, the takbirat of Tashreeq, Eid al-Fitr, and Eid al-Adha are not permissible except in a major city.' A major city is every place that has an amir and a qadi who enforce rulings and establish punishments. This is narrated from Abu Yusuf. And from Abu Yusuf it is also narrated that when people gather in the largest mosque and they do not fit, the first opinion is chosen by Imam Karkhi and this is the apparent madhhab, and the second opinion is chosen by Imam Thalji. And the ruling of permissibility is not limited to the musalla of the city's fina, but it is permitted in all the fina of the city, because in the series of needs of the city's people, all aspects of the fina are like the musalla. In the matn, the two words 'misr jami'' and 'musalla al-misr' require explanation. Definition of misr jami': There is difference regarding the definition of misr jami'. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, misr jami' is where there are streets, markets, a ruler who judges between the oppressor and the oppressed, and a scholar who gives fatwa for new incidents. From Imam Abu Yusuf there are three narrations in this regard. One: misr jami' is every place that has a ruler and a judge who are able to execute rulings and establish legal punishments; after 'executes rulings', the condition 'establishes hudud' is added to make it a decisive ruling, and a female judge is avoided because a woman's judiciary is permissible but she does not have the legal authority to establish hudud and qisas. This is the apparent madhhab regarding misr jami', and it is the one chosen by Imam Karkhi. Second narration: misr jami' is that its largest mosque, if the people upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory gather, they do not fit, so there is need to build another mosque. This narration is chosen by Abu Abdullah al-Baji. Third narration: a place with one thousand men is a misr jami'; Sufyan al-Thawri says misr jami' is what people consider a city when listing cities. The word 'musalla' is key. The musalla of a city is the Eidgah, but here musalla refers to the fina of the city. Fina of the city is the surroundings attached to the city used for the needs of the people, such as graveyard, horse racing track, pasture, Eidgah, hitching post, and in our time parks, etc. Determination of fina: There is difference in the measure and determination of fina. Imam Muhammad restricted it to one 'ghalwa' (a bowshot), and ghalwa ranges from 300 to 400 cubits, meaning up to 400 cubits outside the inhabited area is called fina. Imam Abu Yusuf stated a measure of one or two miles; it is narrated from him that if the imam goes out with the people of the city up to two miles due to need, and the time of Jumu'ah enters, he may perform Jumu'ah there. Some said that if a mir (ruler) stands in the city and shouts, or the mu'adhdhin gives adhan, wherever the sound reaches is fina. Summary: After this detail, the ruling is that Jumu'ah prayer is valid in the city and its fina, but not in a village.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the condition that Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) is only valid in a major city (misr jami') or its environs (fina'), not in villages. The proof cited is a narration attributed to the Prophet (peace be upon him) but actually from Ali (ra). The text first states the ruling from the matn, then elaborates on the definition of 'misr jami'. There are multiple opinions within the Hanafi school. Imam Abu Hanifa defined it as a place with streets, markets, a ruler, and a scholar. Imam Abu Yusuf has three narrations: the first (preferred by Imam Karkhi and stated as the apparent madhhab) requires a ruler and judge who execute punishments; the second says a misr is where if the people gather in the largest mosque they do not fit; the third (from Sufyan al-Thawri) says a place with a thousand men. The passage then clarifies that the term 'musalla' in the matn actually refers to 'fina' (outskirts) of the city, not just a prayer ground. The fina includes attached areas used for public needs like graveyards, parks, Eidgahs, etc. The limit of fina is disputed: Imam Muhammad says 300-400 cubits; Imam Abu Yusuf says one or two miles; some say to the extent that a person's shout or the adhan can be heard. The conclusion is that Jumu'ah is valid in the city and its fina, but not in a village.

Key Terms
مصر جامع (misr jami'): A major city with a ruler, judge, and other facilities enabling the establishment of Friday prayer and public order.
فناء (fina'): The environs or outskirts of a city, attached to it and used for public needs like Eidgah, graveyards, etc.
قريه (qaryah): A village, which is not considered a valid place for Jumu'ah according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where is Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) valid?
A) In any village with a mosque
B) Only in a major city (misr jami') or its fina'
C) Anywhere with a congregation of forty men
D) Only in the city but not its outskirts

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is not valid in a village according to the Hanafi school; it requires a major city (misr jami') or its environs, as defined by the presence of an executive and judicial authority.

The Hanafi Refutation of Jumu'ah in Villages
Inter-madhhab dispute with refutation of proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of Jumu'ah in villages, identify the three proofs of the opponents, and explain the Hanafi rebuttal for each.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only valid in a major city (misr jami'), not in a village.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi response to the Maliki and Shafi'i schools, who permit Jumu'ah in villages under certain conditions. We will analyze each of their three proofs—the Quranic verse, the hadith of Jawatha, and qiyas—and see how the Hanafis rebut them, relying on the statement of Ali (ra) and linguistic analysis. Understanding this dispute clarifies a key difference in the conditions of Jumu'ah across madhahib.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: Jumu'ah is only valid in a misr jami' (major city) or its built-up area (fina'). In villages, it is not valid, and one must pray Zuhr instead.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i permit Jumu'ah in large villages with forty permanent residents who do not migrate with the seasons.
Shafi'i specifically requires forty resident males.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
They cite three proofs: (1) The Quranic command 'Fas'aw ila dhikr Allah' (62:9) which they take as general; (2) The hadith that the first Jumu'ah after Medina was at Jawatha, a village in Bahrain; (3) Qiyas – Jumu'ah is a prayer, so like other prayers it should be valid everywhere.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis rebut each: (1) The Quranic verse is not general even for the opponents, as they exclude deserts and migratory settlements; the verse refers to a specific place, and the Hanafis specify it as a city, supported by Ali's statement. (2) 'Qaryah' in the hadith means 'city' in early Arabic usage, as in Quran 43:31 where 'al-qaryatayn' refers to Mecca and Ta'if; also Jawatha was a fortress with a ruler, making it a city. (3) Qiyas is invalid because the condition of city is established by the proof from Ali (ra), which takes precedence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: According to Hanafis, a person in a village must pray Zuhr on Friday; according to Malik and Shafi'i, they may pray Jumu'ah if the village meets their conditions (e.g., forty residents). Following the wrong opinion could lead to an invalid prayer.

Source Text

امام مالک اور امام شافعی گاؤں کے اندر بھی جو از جمعہ کے قائل ہیں۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ جس گاؤں میں چالیں آزاد مقیم لوگ آباد ہوں خانہ بدوش کی طرح گرمی اور سردی کے موسم میں وچ نہ کرتے ہوں تو ان پر جمعہ فرض ہو گا۔ کہ جب جمعہ کے دن جمعہ کی اذان ہو تو لوگ فورا حاضر ہوں ۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ جمعہ کے لئے کسی خاص قسم کی بستی ہونے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ ہرجگہ جمعہ پڑھنا جائز ہے خواہ شہ ہو یا کاؤں خواہ بڑا گاؤں ہو یا چھوٹا گاؤں۔ دوسری دلیل ابن عباس سے مروی ہے ان اول جمعة جمعت في الاسلام بعد المدينة ما جمعت بجواثا وهى قرية فى البحرين يعنى اسلام میں مدینہ منورہ کے بعد سب سے پہلا جمعہ جوانا میں پڑھا گیا اور جواثا بحرین کا ایک قریہ (گاؤں) ہے۔
تیسری دلیل قیاس ہے وہ یہ کہ جمعہ ایک نماز ہے پس دوسری نمازوں کی طرح اس کا بھی ہر جگہ پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ ہماری دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول لا جمعة ولا تشریق الحدیث ہے۔ یعی جمعہ کی نماز تکبیرات تشریف' عید الفطر اور عید النخی مصرف شہر میں جائز ہے۔ اس قول کو صاحب ہدایہ نے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول قرار دیا ہے مگر صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ یہ آنحضرت کا قول نہیں بلکہ حضرت علی کا قول ہے جیسا کہ صاحب فتح القدیر نے تحریر کیا ہے کہ ابن ابی شیبہ نے اس قول کو حضرت علی پر موقوف کیا ہے۔ امام مالک اور امام شافعی کی پہلی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آیت فاسعوا الى ذکر اللہ آپ کے نزدیک بھی اپنے اطلاق پ نہیں ہے کیونکہ آیت کا اطلاق تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ جمعہ ہر جگہ جائز ہو آبادی میں بھی اور جنگل میں بھی حالانکہ خود آپ کے نزدیک جعد نہ جنگل میں جائز ہے۔ اور نہ ایسی بستی میں جس کے باشندے گرمی یا سردی کے زمانے میں کوچ کر جاتے ہوں۔ پس آیت میں بالاتفاق مخصوص جگہ مراد ہے آپ نے مخصوص جگہ سے گاؤں مراد لیا اور ہم نے شہر مراد لیا ہے۔ شہر مراد لینا انسب ہے۔ کیونکہ حضرت علی کا قول اس کا مؤید ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یعنی حدیث ابن عباس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں قریہ سے مراد شہر ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ابتداء زمانہ میں قریہ کا اطلاق ہر پر کیا جاتا تھا جیسا کہ خود قرآن حکیم میں ہے وَقَالُوا لَوْلَا نُزِلَ هَذَا الْقُرْآنُ عَلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنَ الْقَرْيَتَيْنِ عَظِيمٍ. قریتین سے مراد کہ اور طائف ہیں اور مکہ بالیقین شہر ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ حدیث کے اندر قریہ سے مراد شہر ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ جواثا بحرین کے ایک قلعہ کا نام ہے۔ اور قلعہ کے لئے حاکم اور عالم کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ پس اس سے بھی اس کا شہر ہونا ثابت ہوا۔ اسی وجہ سے مبسوط میں کہا ہے کہ جو اتنا بحرین کے شہر کا نام ہے۔
Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i are of the opinion that Jumu'ah is permissible in villages. Imam Shafi'i said that in a village where forty free resident people live, who do not migrate like Bedouins in summer and winter, then Jumu'ah is obligatory upon them, so that when the adhan for Jumu'ah is given on Friday, the people immediately attend. From this it is understood that there is no need for a specific type of settlement for Jumu'ah; rather, it is permissible to pray Jumu'ah anywhere, whether city or village, large or small. Second proof: Narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'The first Jumu'ah gathered in Islam after Medina was gathered at Jawatha, which is a village in Bahrain.' Third proof: Qiyas: Jumu'ah is a prayer, so like other prayers it should be permissible everywhere. Our proof is the Prophet's statement: 'There is no Jumu'ah nor Tashreeq...' i.e., Jumu'ah prayer, the takbirat of Tashreeq, Eid al-Fitr, and Eid al-Adha are only valid in a major city. The author of Hidayah attributed this statement to the Prophet, but the correct view is that it is not the Prophet's statement but rather the statement of Ali, as the author of Fath al-Qadir wrote that Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated it as a statement of Ali (mawquf). Response to Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i's first proof: The verse 'Fas'aw ila dhikr Allah' is not taken in its absolute generality even according to you, because the general application of the verse would require that Jumu'ah be valid everywhere, including desert, whereas according to you it is not valid in the desert, nor in a settlement whose inhabitants migrate in summer or winter. So the verse definitely refers to a specific place; you have taken it to mean a village, and we take it to mean a city. Taking it to mean a city is more appropriate because the statement of Ali supports it. Response to the second proof, the hadith of Ibn Abbas: The word 'qaryah' (village) in the hadith means a city, because in early times the word 'qaryah' was applied to cities, as in the Quran: 'And they said: Why was this Quran not sent down upon a great man of the two towns (qaryatayn)?' (43:31). 'Qaryatayn' refers to Mecca and Ta'if, and Mecca is definitely a city. So it is established that 'qaryah' in the hadith refers to a city. Second response: Jawatha is the name of a fortress in Bahrain, and a fortress necessarily has a ruler and a scholar, so that also proves it was a city. For this reason, in al-Mabsut it is said that Jawatha is the name of a city in Bahrain.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute, presenting the arguments of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i for permitting Jumu'ah in villages, followed by the Hanafi refutation. The opponents (Maliki and Shafi'i) present three proofs: (1) Quranic verse 'Fas'aw ila dhikr Allah' which commands rushing to the remembrance of Allah on Friday, which they interpret as general, applying to any settlement; (2) The hadith of Ibn Abbas that the first Jumu'ah after Medina was at Jawatha, which was a village in Bahrain; (3) Qiyas: Jumu'ah is a prayer like others, so it should be valid everywhere. The Hanafi response: (1) The Quranic verse is not taken generally even by the opponents, as they exclude deserts and migratory settlements. So the verse refers to a specific place; the Hanafis specify it as a major city, supported by the statement of Ali (ra). (2) The word 'qaryah' in the hadith of Ibn Abbas means 'city' in the early Islamic usage, as shown by the Quran using 'al-qaryatayn' for Mecca and Ta'if. Additionally, Jawatha was a fortress, which implies a ruler and scholar, making it a city. Thus the proof does not support Jumu'ah in ordinary villages. The passage also notes that the hadith cited by the Hidayah as proof from the Prophet is actually from Ali (ra), as clarified in Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
قريه (qaryah): In this passage, a village as opposed to a city; the Hanafis argue that in early Islamic usage it could also refer to a city.
تشريق (tashreeq): The days of Tashreeq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah) and the takbirat recited during them; here it is mentioned along with Jumu'ah as subject to the same condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) They deny the authenticity of the hadith
D) They say the hadith is abrogated

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is only valid in a major city (misr jami') according to the Hanafi school, a position supported by the statement of Ali (ra) and linguistic evidence.

The City Condition for Jumu'ah: Definition of Shahr and Fina'
Definition of fina' and Hanafi condition for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition that Jumu'ah is only valid in a city (shahr) or its environs (fina') and define the key terms shahr and fina' al-shahr.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only valid in a city or its immediate surroundings; a village or desert does not suffice.

The passage begins by defining the fina' (environs) of a city, explaining that Jumu'ah is valid both in the city and its fina', but not in a village. This lesson focuses on understanding these fundamental Hanafi conditions and the scholarly disagreement over the exact extent of fina'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the hukm is. Here, Jumu'ah is wajib, but its validity hinges on location.
2
Identify the location condition
Locate the explicit condition: Jumu'ah is valid only in a city (shahr) or its environs (fina').
The text states: 'Jumu'ah prayer is valid both in the city and in the fina al-shahr. However, it is not valid in a village.'
3
Define shahr and fina'
Understand the definition of shahr (a city with a ruler, market, and permanent population) and fina' (the adjoining area for city needs like cemeteries, parks).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on fina' extent
Imam Muhammad restricts fina' to 300-400 cubits (one arrow-shot); Imam Abu Yusuf extends it to one or two miles. A third view ties it to the range of a shout or adhan.
This difference does not affect the core condition; both agree Jumu'ah is valid in fina'.
5
Recognize the practical implication
The consequence: Jumu'ah is not valid in villages or open country. A Hanafi must pray Zuhr instead if Jumu'ah is attempted in a village.

قریہ کا اطلاق ہر پر کیا جاتا تھا جیسا کہ خود قرآن حکیم میں ہے وَقَالُوا لَوْلَا نُزِلَ هَذَا الْقُرْآنُ عَلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنَ الْقَرْيَتَيْنِ عَظِيمٍ. قریتین سے مراد کہ اور طائف ہیں اور مکہ بالیقین شہر ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ حدیث کے اندر قریہ سے مراد شہر ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ جواثا بحرین کے ایک قلعہ کا نام ہے۔ اور قلعہ کے لئے حاکم اور عالم کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ پس اس سے بھی اس کا شہر ہونا ثابت ہوا۔ اسی وجہ سے مبسوط میں کہا ہے کہ جو اتنا بحرین کے شہر کا نام ہے۔ تیسری دلیل یعنی قیاس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آیت ہر جگہ جمعہ کے جائز ہونے پر دلالت کرتی ہے۔ لیکن اس کے باوجود حضرت علیؓ نے بعض جگہوں پر جمعہ کے جواز کی نفی کی ہے مثلاً گاؤں میں اور جنگل میں حضرت علی مکا بعض جگہوں پر جمعہ کو جائز کہنا اور بعض جگہوں پر جواز کی نفی کرنا یہ حضور صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم سے سن کر ہی ہو سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ خلاف قیاس ہے۔ پس جب شہر کے اندر جمعہ کا جواز اور گاؤں میں عدم جو از خلاف قیاس ہو تو اس کو دوسری نمازوں پر قیاس کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ والحكم غير مقصور على المصلی الخ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جمعہ کی نماز جس طرح عید گاہ میں جائز ہے کیونکہ وہ فتا شہر ہے۔ اسی طرح شہر کے چاروں طرف جہاں جہاں تک فنا شہر کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے نماز جمعہ جائز ہے کیونکہ اہل شہر کی ضروریات پوری کرنے کے سلسلہ میں فناء شہر شہر کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔
Chapter of Friday Prayer. What is built adjoining the city for the needs of the city dwellers, such as cemetery, racecourse, pasture, Eidgah, sacrificial site, and in our time parks etc. Definition of fina al-shahr: There is disagreement about the measure and definition of fina al-shahr. Imam Muhammad restricted it to one arrow-shot, and arrow-shot applies from 300 to 400 cubits – so up to 400 cubits outside the inhabited area is called fina al-shahr. Imam Abu Yusuf defined it as one or two miles. Thus it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that if due to the imam's need he goes out with the city dwellers up to two miles until the time of Jumu'ah comes, then it is permissible for him to pray Jumu'ah there. Some scholars said that if a person stands in the city and shouts, or the mu'adhdhin gives the adhan, then wherever the sound reaches is called fina al-shahr. The issue: After this detail, the issue is that Jumu'ah prayer is valid both in the city and in the fina al-shahr. However, it is not valid in a village. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i hold that Jumu'ah is valid even in a village. Imam Shafi'i said: In any village where forty free resident people live, who do not migrate like nomads in summer and winter, then Jumu'ah is obligatory upon them. Because on Friday when the adhan for Jumu'ah is given, they immediately attend. From this it is understood that no specific type of settlement is required for Jumu'ah; rather it is permissible to pray Jumu'ah everywhere, whether city or village, large or small. Their second proof: Narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'The first Jumu'ah gathered in Islam after Medina was gathered at Ju'atha, which is a village in Bahrain.' Meaning after Medina, the first Jumu'ah was prayed at Ju'atha, and Ju'atha is a village in Bahrain. Third proof is qiyas: Jumu'ah is a prayer, so like other prayers it is permissible to pray it everywhere. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no Jumu'ah nor Tashriq' – the hadith. Meaning Jumu'ah prayer and the takbirs of tashriq of Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha are only valid in the city. The author of Hidayah considered this as the Prophet's statement, but the correct view is that it is not the Prophet's statement but rather the saying of Ali (RA), as authored in Fath al-Qadir: Ibn Abi Shaybah recorded it as Mawquf on Ali. The answer to the first proof of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i: The verse 'Fas'aw ila dhikr Allah' is not unrestricted even in your view, because its unrestricted application would require Jumu'ah to be valid everywhere – in populated areas and in the wilderness – while you yourselves do not consider it valid in the wilderness nor in a settlement whose inhabitants migrate in summer or winter. So the verse unanimously refers to a specific place. You took that specific place as village, and we took it as city. Taking it as city is more appropriate because the saying of Ali supports it. The answer to the second proof, the hadith of Ibn Abbas: The word qaryah in the hadith means city. Because in early times qaryah was used for every settlement, as in the Quran itself: 'And they said: Why was this Quran not sent down upon a great man from the two towns (al-qaryatayn)?' The two qaryatayn refer to Mecca and Ta'if, and Mecca is certainly a city. So it is proven that in the hadith qaryah means city. Second answer: Ju'atha is the name of a fortress in Bahrain, and a fortress necessarily has a ruler and a scholar. So this also proves it is a city. For this reason al-Mabsut says Ju'atha is the name of a city in Bahrain. The answer to the third proof (qiyas): The verse indicates the permissibility of Jumu'ah everywhere, but despite that, Ali (RA) negated its permissibility in some places, e.g., village and wilderness. Ali's (RA) affirming it in some places and negating it in others can only be from hearing the Prophet (peace be upon him), because it is contrary to qiyas. So when the permissibility of Jumu'ah within the city and its impermissibility in the village is contrary to qiyas, then analogizing it to other prayers is incorrect. The meaning of 'And the ruling is not restricted to the musalla' etc. is that just as Jumu'ah is valid in the Eidgah because it is in the fina of the city, similarly wherever the fina applies around the city, Jumu'ah is valid because fina al-shahr has the status of the city in fulfilling the needs of the city dwellers.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of Jumu'ah in villages. The Hanafi position is that Jumu'ah is only valid in a city (shahr) or its immediate environs (fina al-shahr), not in a village or open country. The author begins by defining fina al-shahr – the area adjoining a city used for its needs – noting a difference between Imam Muhammad (300-400 cubits) and Imam Abu Yusuf (one or two miles). A third view ties it to the range of a shout or adhan. The ruling: Jumu'ah is valid in the city and its fina, but not in a village. The opponents (Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i) argue it is valid anywhere, offering three proofs: (1) the Quranic command 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' is general; (2) the first Jumu'ah after Medina was at Ju'atha, described as a village; (3) qiyas to other prayers which are valid everywhere. The Hanafi response: (1) The verse is not unrestricted; even the opponents restrict it to settlements that are permanently inhabited, not nomadic; the dispute narrows to what constitutes a 'specific place' – they say village, Hanafis say city, supported by Ali's statement. (2) The word qaryah in the hadith historically meant any settlement, including cities (cf. Quran 43:31 where 'al-qaryatayn' refers to Mecca and Ta'if). Also, Ju'atha is a fortress, which requires a ruler, indicating a city. (3) Qiyas is invalid because the ruling is established contrary to qiyas based on transmitted authority (Ali's statement). Thus the Hanafi school insists on the condition of a city for Jumu'ah validity.

Key Terms
شہر (shahr): A city or large town where Jumu'ah is valid; defined by having a ruler, market, and permanent population.
فناء شہر (fina' al-shahr): The area adjoining a city used for its needs, such as cemeteries, parks, etc. Its extent is debated: 300-400 cubits (Muhammad) or one to two miles (Abu Yusuf).
قریہ (qaryah): A village or rural settlement; in this context, a settlement that does not meet the criteria of a city.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the maximum extent of fina al-shahr from the built-up area?
A) 100 cubits
B) 300-400 cubits
C) 1 mile
D) 2 miles

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is only valid in a city or its defined environs; villages do not qualify under Hanafi law.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
12 min
Inter-Madhhab Dispute: Jumu'ah in Villages
Inter-madhhab dispute over Jumu'ah in villages with proofs and refutations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi proof for restricting Jumu'ah to cities and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-arguments based on the text.

Core Idea
The Hanafi restriction is based on the saying of Ali (RA) and the interpretation of 'qaryah' as a city, not a village.

This lesson examines the inter-madhhab dispute over Jumu'ah in villages. The Hanafi school insists on a city or its fina', while the Shafi'i/Maliki schools permit Jumu'ah in villages with 40 permanent residents. The passage presents their proofs and the Hanafi responses, culminating in the key evidence from Ali (RA) and linguistic analysis of the Ju'atha hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate that the Hanafi school holds Jumu'ah is valid only in a city (shahr) or its environs (fina'), not in a village (qaryah).
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i allow Jumu'ah in villages if there are 40 free, resident males who do not migrate seasonally.
3
Examine the first opposing proof and the Hanafi response
Opponents cite Quran 62:9 'Fas'aw ila dhikr Allah' as general. Hanafi response: the verse is not unrestricted; even opponents restrict it to permanent settlements. The dispute reduces to defining 'specific place': they say village, Hanafis say city, supported by Ali's statement.
This is tafsir-based argument.
4
Examine the second opposing proof and the Hanafi response
Opponents cite the hadith of Ju'atha, described as a village (qaryah). Hanafi response: in early usage, qaryah meant any settlement including cities (cf. Quran 43:31). Also, Ju'atha was a fortress (qal'ah), implying a city with a ruler.
Linguistic and historical analysis.
5
Examine the third opposing proof and the Hanafi response
Opponents use qiyas on other prayers valid anywhere. Hanafi response: the ruling on Jumu'ah location is established contrary to qiyas based on transmitted authority (Ali's statement). Therefore qiyas is invalid here.
This highlights the role of naql over qiyas.
6
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis consider Jumu'ah in a village invalid (must pray Zuhr); Shafi'is consider it valid.

شہر سے متصل اہل شہر کی مصالح کے لئے بنایا گیا ہو جیسے قبرستان، گھوڑ دوڑ کا میدان، چراگاہ، عیدگاہ ، نذریج اور ہمارے زمانہ میں پارک وغیرہ۔ فناء شہر کی تحدید: فناء شہر کی تقدیر اور تحدید کے بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ امام محمد نے ایک غلوۃ کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے اور غلو کا اطلاق تین سو ذراع سے چار سو ذراع تک ہوتا ہے یعنی آبادی سے باہر چار سو ذراع تک فنا شہر کہلائے گا۔ امام ابو یوسف نے ایک میل با دو میل کی ادا کر دے۔ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر کوئی میر شہر میں کھڑا ہو کر چیخ مارے یا مؤذن اذان دے تو جہاں تک آواز پہنچے گی وہاں تک فنا شہر کہلائے گا۔ صورت مسئلہ: اس تفصیل کے بعد ملاحظہ ہو کر صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نماز جمعہ شہر اور فناء شہر دونوں جگہ جائز ہے۔ البتہ گاؤں میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ امام مالک اور امام شافعی گاؤں کے اندر بھی جو از جمعہ کے قائل ہیں۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ جس گاؤں میں چالیں آزاد مقیم لوگ آباد ہوں خانہ بدوش کی طرح گرمی اور سردی کے موسم میں وچ نہ کرتے ہوں تو ان پر جمعہ فرض ہو گا۔ کہ جب جمعہ کے دن جمعہ کی اذان ہو تو لوگ فورا حاضر ہوں ۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ جمعہ کے لئے کسی خاص قسم کی بستی ہونے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے بلکہ ہرجگہ جمعہ پڑھنا جائز ہے خواہ شہ ہو یا کاؤں خواہ بڑا گاؤں ہو یا چھوٹا گاؤں۔ دوسری دلیل ابن عباس سے مروی ہے ان اول جمعة جمعت في الاسلام بعد المدينة ما جمعت بجواثا وهى قرية فى البحرين يعنى اسلام میں مدینہ منورہ کے بعد سب سے پہلا جمعہ جوانا میں پڑھا گیا اور جواثا بحرین کا ایک قریہ (گاؤں) ہے۔ تیسری دلیل قیاس ہے وہ یہ کہ جمعہ ایک نماز ہے پس دوسری نمازوں کی طرح اس کا بھی ہر جگہ پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ ہماری دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول لا جمعة ولا تشریق الحدیث ہے۔ یعی جمعہ کی نماز تکبیرات تشریف' عید الفطر اور عید النخی مصرف شہر میں جائز ہے۔ اس قول کو صاحب ہدایہ نے آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول قرار دیا ہے مگر صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ یہ آنحضرت کا قول نہیں بلکہ حضرت علی کا قول ہے جیسا کہ صاحب فتح القدیر نے تحریر کیا ہے کہ ابن ابی شیبہ نے اس قول کو حضرت علی پر موقوف کیا ہے۔ امام مالک اور امام شافعی کی پہلی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آیت فاسعوا الى ذکر اللہ آپ کے نزدیک بھی اپنے اطلاق پ نہیں ہے کیونکہ آیت کا اطلاق تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ جمعہ ہر جگہ جائز ہو آبادی میں بھی اور جنگل میں بھی حالانکہ خود آپ کے نزدیک جعد نہ جنگل میں جائز ہے۔ اور نہ ایسی بستی میں جس کے باشندے گرمی یا سردی کے زمانے میں کوچ کر جاتے ہوں۔ پس آیت میں بالاتفاق مخصوص جگہ مراد ہے آپ نے مخصوص جگہ سے گاؤں مراد لیا اور ہم نے شہر مراد لیا ہے۔ شہر مراد لینا انسب ہے۔ کیونکہ حضرت علی کا قول اس کا مؤید ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یعنی حدیث ابن عباس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں قریہ سے مراد شہر ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ابتداء زمانہ میں قریہ کا اطلاق ہر پر کیا جاتا تھا جیسا کہ خود قرآن حکیم میں ہے وَقَالُوا لَوْلَا نُزِلَ هَذَا الْقُرْآنُ عَلَى رَجُلٍ مِّنَ الْقَرْيَتَيْنِ عَظِيمٍ. قریتین سے مراد کہ اور طائف ہیں اور مکہ بالیقین شہر ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ حدیث کے اندر قریہ سے مراد شہر ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ جواثا بحرین کے ایک قلعہ کا نام ہے۔ اور قلعہ کے لئے حاکم اور عالم کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ پس اس سے بھی اس کا شہر ہونا ثابت ہوا۔ اسی کی نفی کی ہے مثلاً گاؤں میں اور جنگل میں حضرت علی مکا بعض جگہوں پر جمعہ کو جائز کہنا اور بعض جگہوں پر جواز کی نفی کرنا یہ حضور صلے اللہ علیہ وسلم سے سن کر ہی ہو سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ خلاف قیاس ہے۔ پس جب شہر کے اندر جمعہ کا جواز اور گاؤں میں عدم جو از خلاف قیاس ہو تو اس کو دوسری نمازوں پر قیاس کرنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ والحكم غير مقصور على المصلی الخ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جمعہ کی نماز جس طرح عید گاہ میں جائز ہے کیونکہ وہ فتا شہر ہے۔ اسی طرح شہر کے چاروں طرف جہاں جہاں تک فنا شہر کا اطلاق ہوتا ہے نماز جمعہ جائز ہے کیونکہ اہل شہر کی ضروریات پوری کرنے کے سلسلہ میں فناء شہر شہر کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔
Chapter of Friday Prayer. What is built adjoining the city for the needs of the city dwellers, such as cemetery, racecourse, pasture, Eidgah, sacrificial site, and in our time parks etc. Definition of fina al-shahr: There is disagreement about the measure and definition of fina al-shahr. Imam Muhammad restricted it to one arrow-shot, and arrow-shot applies from 300 to 400 cubits – so up to 400 cubits outside the inhabited area is called fina al-shahr. Imam Abu Yusuf defined it as one or two miles. Thus it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that if due to the imam's need he goes out with the city dwellers up to two miles until the time of Jumu'ah comes, then it is permissible for him to pray Jumu'ah there. Some scholars said that if a person stands in the city and shouts, or the mu'adhdhin gives the adhan, then wherever the sound reaches is called fina al-shahr. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i hold that Jumu'ah is valid even in a village. Imam Shafi'i said: In any village where forty free resident people live, who do not migrate like nomads in summer and winter, then Jumu'ah is obligatory upon them. Because on Friday when the adhan for Jumu'ah is given, they immediately attend. From this it is understood that no specific type of settlement is required for Jumu'ah; rather it is permissible to pray Jumu'ah everywhere, whether city or village, large or small. Their second proof: Narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'The first Jumu'ah gathered in Islam after Medina was gathered at Ju'atha, which is a village in Bahrain.' Meaning after Medina, the first Jumu'ah was prayed at Ju'atha, and Ju'atha is a village in Bahrain. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no Jumu'ah nor Tashriq' – the hadith. Meaning Jumu'ah prayer and the takbirs of tashriq of Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha are only valid in the city. The author of Hidayah considered this as the Prophet's statement, but the correct view is that it is not the Prophet's statement but rather the saying of Ali (RA), as authored in Fath al-Qadir: Ibn Abi Shaybah recorded it as Mawquf on Ali. So the verse unanimously refers to a specific place. You took that specific place as village, and we took it as city. Taking it as city is more appropriate because the saying of Ali supports it. The answer to the second proof, the hadith of Ibn Abbas: The word qaryah in the hadith means city. Because in early times qaryah was used for every settlement, as in the Quran itself: 'And they said: Why was this Quran not sent down upon a great man from the two towns (al-qaryatayn)?' The two qaryatayn refer to Mecca and Ta'if, and Mecca is certainly a city. So it is proven that in the hadith qaryah means city. Second answer: Ju'atha is the name of a fortress in Bahrain, and a fortress necessarily has a ruler and a scholar. So this also proves it is a city. For this reason al-Mabsut says Ju'atha is the name of a city in Bahrain. The answer to the third proof (qiyas): The verse indicates the permissibility of Jumu'ah everywhere, but despite that, Ali (RA) negated its permissibility in some places, e.g., village and wilderness. Ali's (RA) affirming it in some places and negating it in others can only be from hearing the Prophet (peace be upon him), because it is contrary to qiyas. So when the permissibility of Jumu'ah within the city and its impermissibility in the village is contrary to qiyas, then analogizing it to other prayers is incorrect. The meaning of 'And the ruling is not restricted to the musalla' etc. is that just as Jumu'ah is valid in the Eidgah because it is in the fina of the city, similarly wherever the fina applies around the city, Jumu'ah is valid because fina al-shahr has the status of the city in fulfilling the needs of the city dwellers.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of Jumu'ah in villages. The Hanafi position is that Jumu'ah is only valid in a city (shahr) or its immediate environs (fina al-shahr), not in a village or open country. The author begins by defining fina al-shahr – the area adjoining a city used for its needs – noting a difference between Imam Muhammad (300-400 cubits) and Imam Abu Yusuf (one or two miles). A third view ties it to the range of a shout or adhan. The ruling: Jumu'ah is valid in the city and its fina, but not in a village. The opponents (Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i) argue it is valid anywhere, offering three proofs: (1) the Quranic command 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' is general; (2) the first Jumu'ah after Medina was at Ju'atha, described as a village; (3) qiyas to other prayers which are valid everywhere. The Hanafi response: (1) The verse is not unrestricted; even the opponents restrict it to settlements that are permanently inhabited, not nomadic; the dispute narrows to what constitutes a 'specific place' – they say village, Hanafis say city, supported by Ali's statement. (2) The word qaryah in the hadith historically meant any settlement, including cities (cf. Quran 43:31 where 'al-qaryatayn' refers to Mecca and Ta'if). Also, Ju'atha is a fortress, which requires a ruler, indicating a city. (3) Qiyas is invalid because the ruling is established contrary to qiyas based on transmitted authority (Ali's statement). Thus the Hanafi school insists on the condition of a city for Jumu'ah validity.

Key Terms
شہر (shahr): A city or large town where Jumu'ah is valid; defined by having a ruler, market, and permanent population.
فناء شہر (fina' al-shahr): The area adjoining a city used for its needs, such as cemeteries, parks, etc. Its extent is debated: 300-400 cubits (Muhammad) or one to two miles (Abu Yusuf).
قریہ (qaryah): A village or rural settlement; in this context, a settlement that does not meet the criteria of a city.
مصر (misr): A city or large town; used in the saying of Ali (RA).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main Hanafi proof for restricting Jumu'ah to cities?
A) Quran 62:9
B) The hadith of Ju'atha
C) The saying of Ali (RA)
D) Qiyas on other prayers

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi restriction on Jumu'ah to cities is based on transmitted evidence from Ali (RA) and linguistic interpretation of qaryah as city.

Jumu'ah in Mina: Conditional Validity in Hajj Season
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Jumu'ah in Mina.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid Jumu'ah in Mina according to the Sheikhayn and evaluate Imam Muhammad's objection.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah in Mina is valid only if the ruler has general authority; the dispute hinges on whether Mina is a city or village.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi disagreement about the validity of Friday prayer in Mina during the Hajj season. The core issue is whether Mina's temporary transformation into a bustling city suffices to meet the conditions for Jumu'ah, and which type of ruler can establish it. We will examine the positions of the Sheikhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) versus Imam Muhammad, along with their proofs and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
State the Hanafi ruling on Jumu'ah in Mina and the specific condition mentioned in the matn (presence of Amir of Hijaz or Caliph).
This is the majority view of the Sheikhayn.
2
Examine the intra-Hanafi objection
Explain Imam Muhammad's position that Jumu'ah is not valid in Mina, and his evidence (Mina is a village, no Eid prayer).
Remember that this is a genuine ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Analyze the Sheikhayn's counter-proof
Understand their reasoning: Mina becomes a city (tamassur) during Hajj, and the absence of Eid is a dispensation, not a proof of village status.
The argument is based on customary change (urf) and practicality.
4
Differentiate types of rulers
Distinguish between the Amir of Hijaz (general authority), the Caliph (supreme authority), and the Amir of the season (limited to Hajj affairs).
Only the first two have the wilayah needed to establish Jumu'ah.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
State the difference: under Sheikhayn, Jumu'ah is valid and fulfills the obligation; under Muhammad, Zuhr must be prayed instead.
The mufta bihi is the Sheikhayn's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منی میں جمعہ کا حکم
ويجوز بمنى ان كان الامير امير الحجاز او كان الخليفة مسافراعند ابي حنيفة وابويوسف وقال محمد لا جمعة بمنى لانها من القرى حتى لا يعيدبها ولهما انها تتمصر فى ايام الموسم وعدم التعييد للتخفيف ولا جمعة بعرفات فى قولهم جميعا لانها فضاء وبمنى ابنية والتقييد بالخليفة وامير الحجاز لان الولاية لها اما امير الموسم فیلی امور الحج لاغير
ترجمہ اور مقام منی میں جمعہ پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ اگر امیر حجاز کا امیر ہو۔ یا خلیفہ المسلمین خود مسافر کے طور پر یہاں موجود ہو ( یہ جواز ) ابوحنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ منی میں جمعہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ منی تو گاؤں میں سے ایک گاؤں ہے حتی کہ اس میں بقر عید کی نماز نہیں پڑھی جاتی ۔ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منی موسم حج میں شہر بن جاتا ہے اور نماز عید وہاں نہ ہونا آسانی دینے کے پیش نظر ہے۔ اور عرفات میں بالاتفاق جمعہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ عرفات تو خالی میدان ہے اور منی میں مکانات بنے ہوئے ہیں۔ اور خلیفہ اور امیر حجاز کے موجود ہونے کی قید لگانا اس لئے ہے کہ ولایت تو انہیں دونوں کی ہے۔ رہا امیر موسم تو فقط حج کے امور کا متولی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ایام حج ہنی کے اندر جمعہ کی نماز ادا کرنا جائز ہے مگر اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ امیر حج وہ شخص ہو جو صو بہ حجاز کا حاکم ہے صرف حج کرانے کے لئے امیر نہ بنایا گیا ہویا خلیفہ المسلمین بذات خود حج کے ارادے سے سفر کر کے یہاں موجود ہو، خلیفہ کے ساتھ مسافر ہونے کی قید اس لئے لگائی ہے کہ خلیفہ اگر منی میں مقیم ہوتو بدرجہ اولی جمعہ کی نماز پڑھنا جائز ہوگا۔ دوم اس وہم کو دور کرنے کے لئے کہ امیر موسم اگر مسافر ہو تو وہ جمعہ قائم نہیں کر سکتا پس اس طرح خلیفہ بھی مسافر ہونے کی صورت میں جمعہ قائم نہیں کر سکتا، صاحب قدوری نے اس وہم کو دور کرنے کے لئے فرمایا کہ امیر موسم مسافر ہونے کی صورت میں بلا شبہ جمعہ قائم نہیں کرسکتا، لیکن خلیفہ المسلمین مسافر ہونے کے باوجود جمعہ قائم کر سکتا ہے اس سے یہ بھی ظاہر ہوا کہ خلیفہ بابا دشاہ اگر اپنی مملکت میں دورہ کرے تو ہر شہر میں اس پر جمعہ واجب ہوگا۔ پس جس شہر میں جمعہ کا دن پڑ جائے اسی میں جمعہ ادا کرائے دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب اس کے حکم سے دوسروں کو امام جمعہ مقرر کرنا جائز ہے تو خود اس کو جمعہ کی امامت کرنا بدرجہ اولی جائز ہوگا اگر چہ مسافر ہو۔ بہر حال شیخین کے نزدیک اس شرط کے ساتھ منی میں جمعہ جائز ہے۔ حضرت امام حمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ منی میں قطع جمعہ جائز نہیں ہے
Ruling of Jumu'ah in Mina: It is permissible in Mina if the ruler is the Amir of Hijaz or the Caliph is a traveler – according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: No Jumu'ah in Mina because it is one of the villages, so much so that Eid prayer is not performed there. Their (the two shaykhs) proof: Mina becomes a city during the season; the absence of Eid prayer there is for ease. And there is no Jumu'ah at Arafat unanimously because it is an open plain, while Mina has buildings. The restriction to the Caliph and Amir of Hijaz is because authority belongs to them. As for the Amir of the season, he only manages Hajj affairs. Translation and commentary: It is permissible to pray Jumu'ah in Mina if the Amir of Hijaz (the governor of the province of Hijaz) is present, or the Caliph himself is there as a traveler. This permissibility is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad said that Jumu'ah is not valid in Mina because it is one of the villages, so much so that Eid prayer is not performed there. The proof of the two shaykhs: Mina becomes a city during the Hajj season; the fact that Eid prayer is not performed there is for convenience. And Jumu'ah is unanimously not valid at Arafat because it is an open plain, while Mina has buildings. The restriction to the Caliph and Amir of Hijaz is because authority belongs to them. As for the Amir of the season, he is only in charge of Hajj affairs. Explanation: According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, during the days of Hajj it is permissible to perform Jumu'ah in Mina, but with the condition that the Amir of Hajj is the person who is the governor of the province of Hijaz, not someone appointed only for performing Hajj, or the Caliph himself travels with the intention of Hajj and is present there. The restriction that the Caliph be a traveler is included because if the Caliph is a resident in Mina, then a fortiori it is permissible to pray Jumu'ah. Secondly, to remove the misconception that if the Amir of the season is a traveler then he cannot establish Jumu'ah, similarly the Caliph, if a traveler, cannot establish Jumu'ah. Sahib al-Quduri said to remove this misconception: The Amir of the season, if a traveler, certainly cannot establish Jumu'ah, but the Caliph, even if a traveler, can establish Jumu'ah. This also shows that if the Caliph (king) travels in his kingdom, Jumu'ah becomes obligatory upon him in every city. So in whichever city Friday occurs, he should perform Jumu'ah there. The proof is: When it is permissible to appoint others as imam of Jumu'ah by his order, then a fortiori it is permissible for him to lead Jumu'ah himself, even if he is a traveler. In any case, according to the two shaykhs, with this condition Jumu'ah in Mina is permissible. Imam Muhammad (al-Hasan) said that Jumu'ah is not valid in Mina.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of Jumu'ah in Mina during the Hajj season. The base ruling from the matn states that Jumu'ah is permissible in Mina if the ruler is the Amir of Hijaz or the Caliph (even if a traveler). This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (Sheikhayn). Imam Muhammad disagrees, arguing Mina is a village (qaryah) and thus Jumu'ah is not valid there; he points out that Eid prayer is not performed in Mina. The Sheikhayn's reasoning: During Hajj season, Mina effectively becomes a city due to the large gathering and buildings. The fact that Eid prayer is not performed there is a dispensation, not proof of its village status. The condition of the Amir of Hijaz or Caliph is because only they possess the general authority (wilayah) to establish Jumu'ah for the public; the Amir of the season (only appointed for Hajj) lacks that authority. The commentary clarifies that if the Caliph is a resident, it is even more permissible. Moreover, the Caliph's ability to lead Jumu'ah while traveling is unique: unlike the Amir of the season, the Caliph's authority extends throughout the realm, so he can lead Jumu'ah anywhere even as a traveler. The relied-upon position is that of the Sheikhayn: Jumu'ah in Mina is valid with the specified condition. Imam Muhammad's view is noted as an objection but the text tends to support the Sheikhayn.

Key Terms
امیر الحجاز (amir al-hijaz): The governor or ruler of the province of Hijaz, who has general authority beyond just Hajj affairs.
خلیفہ (khalifah): The head of the Islamic state (caliph/king) with supreme authority. His presence, even as a traveler, validates Jumu'ah in Mina.
منی (mina): A location about 5 km from Mecca, with buildings, where pilgrims stay during Hajj. Its status as city or village is debated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Any imam appointed by the local mosque committee.

C) A minimum of 40 resident males.
D) Building a proper mosque.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah in Mina is valid per the Sheikhayn when the ruler with general authority (Amir of Hijaz or Caliph) is present; Imam Muhammad's contrary view is not the operative position.

The Ruling of Jumu'ah in Mina: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute with proofs and resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on Jumu'ah in Mina, explain the proofs for each, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Mina's temporary city-status during Hajj determines Jumu'ah's validity—but Imam Muhammad disagrees.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a well-known disagreement within the Hanafi school: can Jumu'ah prayer be performed in Mina during the Hajj season? The two senior imams—Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf—answer yes, provided the ruling authority is present. But Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it is never valid. Their dispute centers on whether Mina qualifies as a city (misr) or its surrounding area (fina') for the purpose of establishing Jumu'ah. The practical consequence is significant for pilgrims and authorities. Let us examine the arguments and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the two Hanafi positions
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) and the ruling of Imam Muhammad. Note the conditions for validity according to each.
The two shaykhs: Jumu'ah valid in Mina during Hajj with amir al-Hijaz or caliph present. Muhammad: never valid.
2
Analyze the key proofs
For each position, identify the main evidence: the two shaykhs rely on Mina becoming a city during Hajj and the Quranic verse (5:95) linking Mina to the Ka'bah. Muhammad relies on Mina being a village and the absence of 'Id prayer.
Also note the definition of fina' (surrounding area) – Muhammad limits it to 400 cubits, making Mina outside.
3
Examine the counter-argument on 'Id prayer
Muhammad argues that since 'Id prayer is not performed in Mina, it is not a city. The two shaykhs respond that this is a concession for pilgrims, not a legal indicator.
This shows the importance of reasoning (ta'lil) in fiqh disputes.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If one follows Muhammad, Jumu'ah in Mina is invalid and must be repeated. If one follows the two shaykhs, it is valid and no repetition is needed.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that of the two shaykhs.
5
Understand the authority condition
The two shaykhs require the amir al-Hijaz or the caliph to authorize Jumu'ah. The amir al-mawsim (Hajj season official) does not have the required authority.
This condition is derived from the general principle that Jumu'ah requires a ruler's permission.

Source Text

ويجوز بمنى ان كان الامير امير الحجاز او كان الخليفة مسافراً عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف وقال محمد لا جمعة بمنى لانها من القرى حتى لا يعيد بها ولهما انها تتمصر في ايام الموسم وعدم التعييد للتخفيف ولا جمعة بعرفات في قولهم جميعا لانها فضاء وبمنى ابنية والتقييد بالخليفة وامير الحجاز لان الولاية لها اما امير الموسم فيلي امور الحج لاغير

ترجمہ اور مقام منی میں جمعہ پڑھنا جائز ہے۔ اگر امیر حجاز کا امیر ہو۔ یا خلیفہ المسلمین خود مسافر کے طور پر یہاں موجود ہو ( یہ جواز ) ابوحنیفہ اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ منی میں جمعہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ منی تو گاؤں میں سے ایک گاؤں ہے حتی کہ اس میں بقر عید کی نماز نہیں پڑھی جاتی ۔ اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منی موسم حج میں شہر بن جاتا ہے اور نماز عید وہاں نہ ہونا آسانی دینے کے پیش نظر ہے۔ اور عرفات میں بالاتفاق جمعہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ عرفات تو خالی میدان ہے اور منی میں مکانات بنے ہوئے ہیں۔ اور خلیفہ اور امیر حجاز کے موجود ہونے کی قید لگانا اس لئے ہے کہ ولایت تو انہیں دونوں کی ہے۔ رہا امیر موسم تو فقط حج کے امور کا متولی ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ایام حج منی کے اندر جمعہ کی نماز ادا کرنا جائز ہے مگر اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ امیر حج وہ شخص ہو جو صوبہ حجاز کا حاکم ہے صرف حج کرانے کے لئے امیر نہ بنایا گیا ہو یا خلیفہ المسلمین بذات خود حج کے ارادے سے سفر کر کے یہاں موجود ہو، خلیفہ کے ساتھ مسافر ہونے کی قید اس لئے لگائی ہے کہ خلیفہ اگر منی میں مقیم ہو تو بدرجہ اولی جمعہ کی نماز پڑھنا جائز ہوگا۔ دوم اس وہم کو دور کرنے کے لئے کہ امیر موسم اگر مسافر ہو تو وہ جمعہ قائم نہیں کر سکتا پس اس طرح خلیفہ بھی مسافر ہونے کی صورت میں جمعہ قائم نہیں کر سکتا، صاحب قدوری نے اس وہم کو دور کرنے کے لئے فرمایا کہ امیر موسم مسافر ہونے کی صورت میں بلا شبہ جمعہ قائم نہیں کرسکتا، لیکن خلیفہ المسلمین مسافر ہونے کے باوجود جمعہ قائم کر سکتا ہے اس سے یہ بھی ظاہر ہوا کہ خلیفہ بادشاہ اگر اپنی مملکت میں دورہ کرے تو ہر شہر میں اس پر جمعہ واجب ہوگا۔ پس جس شہر میں جمعہ کا دن پڑ جائے اسی میں جمعہ ادا کرائے دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب اس کے حکم سے دوسروں کو امام جمعہ مقرر کرنا جائز ہے تو خود اس کو جمعہ کی امامت کرنا بدرجہ اولی جائز ہوگا اگر چہ مسافر ہو۔ بہر حال شیخین کے نزدیک اس شرط کے ساتھ منی میں جمعہ جائز ہے۔ حضرت امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ منی میں قطعاً جمعہ جائز نہیں ہے

و امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منی نہ تو شہر ہے اور نہ فنا شہر ہے بلکہ ایک گاؤں ہے اور گاؤں میں جمعہ جائز نہیں۔ اس لئے منی میں جائز نہ ہوگا ایک وجہ یہ ہے کہ منی میں بقر عید کی نماز نہیں ادا کی جاتی۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک منی فناء شہر (مکہ) میں اس لئے داخل نہیں ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک فناء کا اطلاق ایک غلوۃ (چار سو ذراع) ہے اور منی ایک غلوۃ کی مقدار سے زائد ہے۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منی با اشبہ شہر نہیں ہے لیکن حج کے موسم میں شہر بن جاتا ہے کیونکہ وہاں موسم حج میں بازار لگ جاتے ہیں بادشاہ یا اس کا نائب اور قاضی اس موسم میں وہاں موجود ہوتے ہیں۔ چونکہ موسم حج کے علاوہ میں یہ سب شرطیں نہیں پائی جاتیں اس لئے موسم حج کے علاوہ وہاں جمعہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ منی کے اندر بقر عید کی نماز نہیں پڑھی جاتی تو اس کی وجہ منی کا موسم حج میں شہر ہونا نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس روز حاجی لوگ مناسک حج میں ذبیح، حلق وغیرہ میں مشغول ہوتے ہیں اور وقت تنگ ہو اس لئے آسانی کے پیش نظر حجاج کو عید الاضحی کی نماز نہ پڑھنے کی اجازت دیدی گئی۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ منی چونکہ حرم میں شامل ہے اس لئے منی فناء مکہ میں سے ہے۔ اللہ رب العزت کا ارشاد ہے هَدْيًا بَالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ اس آیت میں منی کو کعبہ کے ساتھ تعبیر کیا گیا حالانکہ عملی طور پر قربانی اور ہدی کے جانور مکہ میں ذبح نہیں کئے جاتے بلکہ منی میں ذبح کئے جاتے ہیں اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ منی مکہ کے حکم میں ہے یا فناء مکہ کے اور جمعہ ادا کرنا جس طرح شہر کے اندر جائز ہے اسی طرح فنا شہر کے اندر بھی جائز ہے۔ میدان عرفات میں بالاتفاق جمعہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ عرفات تو فقط میدان ہے آبادی و غیرہ کچھ بھی نہیں اور فناء مکہ میں بھی داخل نہیں ہے اس لئے عرفات نہ شہر ہے اور نہ فنا شہر تو وہاں جمعہ قائم کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔

صاحب قدوری نے منی کے اندر جواز جمعہ کے لئے امیر حجاز یا خلیفہ ہونے کی قید اس لئے لگائی ہے کہ جمعہ قائم کرنے کی ولایت انہیں دونوں کو ہے۔ اور رہا وہ امیر جس کو امیر موسم کہتے ہیں وہ تو حج کے امور کا متولی ہوتا ہے نہ کہ اس کے علاوہ کا اس لئے اس کو ولایت حاصل نہیں ہے۔
It is permissible to pray Jumu'ah in Mina if the amir is the amir of the Hijaz or the caliph is traveling, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: There is no Jumu'ah in Mina because it is among the villages, so much so that the 'Id prayer is not performed there. Their proof is that it becomes a city during the season, and the omission of 'Id prayer is for ease. There is no Jumu'ah in 'Arafat by unanimous agreement because it is an open space, while Mina has buildings. The restriction to the caliph and amir of Hijaz is because authority belongs to them. As for the amir of the season, he only attends to Hajj affairs. Explanation: According to the two imams, Jumu'ah is permissible in Mina during Hajj days, provided the amir of Hajj is the ruler of the Hijaz province, not just appointed for Hajj, or the caliph himself travels for Hajj and is present. The condition of travel for the caliph is to indicate that if the caliph is resident, it is even more permissible. Also to remove the misunderstanding that if the amir of the season cannot establish Jumu'ah when traveling, the caliph also cannot. Sahib Quduri clarifies that the amir of the season cannot, but the caliph can even while traveling. This shows that if the caliph king tours his kingdom, Jumu'ah becomes obligatory on him in every city. The proof is that if he can appoint others as imams for Jumu'ah, then a fortiori he can lead it himself, even if traveling. In short, according to the two shaykhs, Jumu'ah in Mina is permissible with this condition. Imam Muhammad said it is absolutely not permissible. And Imam Muhammad's proof is that Mina is neither a city nor its surrounding area; it is a village, and Jumu'ah is not valid in a village. One reason is that the 'Id prayer is not performed there. According to him, Mina is not part of the fina' of Mecca because fina' is one ghalwa (400 cubits), and Mina exceeds that. The two shaykhs' proof is that Mina is not like a city, but during the Hajj season it becomes a city due to markets, the ruler, and the qadi. Outside the season, these conditions are absent, so Jumu'ah is not valid then. The absence of 'Id prayer is a concession for pilgrims occupied with rites, not due to lack of city status. Another proof: Since Mina is in the Haram, it is part of the fina' of Mecca. Allah says: 'هديا بالغ الكعبة' (a sacrificial offering reaching the Ka'bah). This verse associates Mina with the Ka'bah, yet sacrifices are done in Mina, showing Mina has the same ruling as Mecca or its fina'. Just as Jumu'ah is valid in the city, it is valid in the fina'. In 'Arafat, Jumu'ah is unanimously invalid because it is an empty plain, not part of the fina' of Mecca. Sahib Quduri restricted the permissibility to the amir of Hijaz or caliph because authority belongs to them; the amir of the season only handles Hajj affairs.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of Jumu'ah in Mina. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf hold that Jumu'ah is permissible in Mina during the Hajj season provided that the ruling authority (the amir of Hijaz or the caliph) is present. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, asserting that Mina is a village, not a city or its surrounding area, and Jumu'ah is not valid in villages. The dispute centers on whether Mina effectively becomes a city during Hajj due to the gathering of people and authorities. The two shaykhs argue that the presence of markets, the ruler, and the qadi transform it into a city temporarily. They also use the Quranic verse (5:95) mentioning the Ka'bah in connection with Mina to show Mina has the same status as Mecca. Imam Muhammad limits the definition of fina' to a specific distance (one ghalwa = 400 cubits) and considers Mina beyond it. The disagreement also touches on the absence of 'Id prayer in Mina, which the two shaykhs explain as a concession for pilgrims, not because Mina fails to be a city. The passage also clarifies that 'Arafat is unanimously invalid for Jumu'ah due to being empty land. Finally, it explains the condition of authority: only the caliph or the amir of Hijaz can authorize Jumu'ah in Mina, not the amir al-mawsim who only manages Hajj rituals.

Key Terms
فناء شہر (fanā' al-madīnah): The surrounding area of a city, within which Jumu'ah is valid; differs in definition between scholars.
غلوۃ (ghalwah): A unit of distance, approximately 400 cubits (about 200 meters).
امیر حجاز (amīr al-Ḥijāz): The governor/ruler of the Hijaz region, who has authority to establish Jumu'ah in Mina.
امیر موسم (amīr al-mawsim): The official appointed specifically to manage the Hajj season, lacking broader authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, under what condition is Jumu'ah valid in Mina?
A) At any time if there is a large gathering.
B) Only if the caliph is resident, not traveling.
C) During the Hajj season with the amir al-Hijaz or caliph present.
D) Only if the amir al-mawsim gives permission.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah in Mina is valid during Hajj with proper authority according to the relied-upon Hanafi position, despite Imam Muhammad's objection.

The Sultan's Permission: A Condition for Jumu'ah
Stating and explaining the requirement of the Sultan for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of the Sultan for Jumu'ah, explain the rationale (talil), and distinguish the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires the ruler's authorization to prevent disputes—without it, the prayer is invalid in the Hanafi school.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes that the Sultan's permission is a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah. The reason given is that Jumu'ah involves a large gathering, and without a designated authority, conflicts over leadership and organization could arise. The Hanafi school considers this authorization essential, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds it unnecessary. We will explore the evidence, the definition of Sultan, and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the central ruling: Jumu'ah is not permissible (la yajuz) except with the Sultan or his authorized deputy. This is a condition for validity (shart).
The condition is for the prayer to be valid, not just recommended.
2
Examine the rationale (talil)
The text gives a reason: because Jumu'ah is established with a great congregation (bi jamiʿ ʿaẓim) and disputes (mumāzaʿa) may occur over precedence and organization. The condition completes the affair (tatmīman li-amrihā).
The 'illa is the potential for discord, which is avoided by a central authority.
3
Define the Sultan and delegation
The Sultan is the supreme ruler (caliph) with no higher authority. He may delegate to amirs, qadis, or khatibs provided they have his permission to establish Jumu'ah.
The condition is about authorization, not that the ruler himself must lead.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The passage notes that Imam al-Shafi'i does not require the Sultan's permission. His proof (though cut off here) is based on practice at the time of the caliphs where permission was not always formalized.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both schools have evidence.
5
Apply to a modern scenario
Consider a Muslim community in a non-Muslim country. The Hanafi ruling would require an appointed leader (e.g., an imam consented to by the community) to avoid disputes, though not necessarily a political ruler.
Modern application may interpret 'Sultan' as the recognized authority within the community.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور جمعہ قائم کرنا جائز نہیں مگر خلیفہ کے لئے یا اس کے لئے جس کو خلیفہ نے اجازت دیدی ہو۔ کیونکہ جمعہ ایک عظیم جمان کے ساتھ قائم کیا جاتا ہے اور کبھی آگے بڑھنے اور آگے بڑھانے میں جھگڑ واقع ہو جاتا ہے کبھی اس کے علاوہ اور بات میں جھگڑا ہو جاتا ہے تو جمعہ کا کام پورا کرنے کے لئے خلیفہ یا اس کے نائب کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔

And it is not permissible to establish it (Jumu'ah) except for the Sultan or one whom the Sultan has commanded, because it is established with a great gathering, and disputes may occur concerning precedence and leadership, and other matters, so it is necessary for the completion of its affair.

Translation: Jumu'ah is not permissible except for the caliph or for one whom the caliph has authorized, because Jumu'ah is established with a great congregation, and sometimes disputes arise in moving forward and backward, and sometimes in other matters, so the caliph or his deputy is necessary to complete the affair.

Explanation: For the performance of Jumu'ah, the presence of the Sultan is a condition. The Sultan is a ruler who has no other ruler above him, like the caliph, or a person whom the Sultan has ordered and authorized, such as an amir, qadi, or khatib, provided they have permission to establish Jumu'ah. Imam al-Shafi'i says that the Sultan or his deputy is not a condition for performing Jumu'ah. (From 'Inayah) Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that at a time when the caliph...
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage establishes that Jumu'ah prayer requires the authorization of the ruler (Sultan) or his deputy. The reason is that Jumu'ah involves a large congregation, and without an appointed leader, conflicts could arise over who leads or organizes the prayer. Therefore, the ruler's permission ensures order and legitimacy. The Hanafi school considers this a condition for validity. The Sultan is defined as the supreme authority, and he may delegate to others like amirs, qadis, or khatibs. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the condition is not necessary, but his full argument is cut off in this text. The Hanafi position is that the Sultan's permission is essential to prevent disputes.

Key Terms
سلطان (sulṭān): The supreme ruler (caliph) who has authority over all and can delegate to others.
ولایت (wilāyah): Legal authority to establish Jumu'ah, held by the Sultan or his authorized deputy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school require the Sultan's permission for Jumu'ah?
A) Because Jumu'ah is a political obligation.
B) To prevent disputes and maintain order in the large congregation.
C) Because only the Sultan can perform the khutbah.
D) Because Jumu'ah must be performed in the presence of the ruler.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, Jumu'ah is valid only with the authorization of the Sultan or his deputy, a condition grounded in preventing communal discord.

Jumu'ah in Mina During Hajj: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on City Periphery
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Jumu'ah in Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on Jumu'ah in Mina, identify the proofs of the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad, and apply the condition of the ruler's authority.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah in Mina is valid only during Hajj according to the Shaykhayn, but Imam Muhammad rejects it entirely.

A central condition for valid Jumu'ah in the Hanafi school is that it be performed in a city (misr) or its periphery (fina'). But what if a location changes its character seasonally? Mina, a valley near Makkah, becomes a bustling hub during Hajj but is otherwise a village. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether Jumu'ah can be held in Mina, focusing on the proofs of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) versus Imam Muhammad, and the additional condition of ruler authority imposed by al-Quduri.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi condition for Jumu'ah locality
Recall that Jumu'ah is wajib and must be held in a city or its periphery (fina'). The fina' is defined as the area up to a bowshot (ghalwah, ~400 cubits) from the city limits. Identify that this condition is part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
The dispute is whether Mina falls within the fina' of Makkah or becomes a city during Hajj.
2
Identify Imam Muhammad's position and proof
Imam Muhammad argues that Mina is a village, not a city or its periphery. He defines the fina' of Makkah as only one bowshot, and Mina exceeds that distance. Therefore Jumu'ah is not valid in Mina at any time.
He also cites the omission of Eid al-Adha prayer in Mina as supporting evidence.
3
Analyze the Shaykhayn's counter-proof
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf concede that Mina is not a permanent city, but during the Hajj season it acquires the attributes of a city: markets, a ruler, and a judge. Thus Jumu'ah becomes permissible only during that season.
They also address the Eid prayer objection: it is omitted due to pilgrims' preoccupation, not because Mina is not a city.
4
Examine the Quranic proof for fina' status
The Shaykhayn cite Quran 5:95 (hadyan baligh al-ka'bah) to show that Mina is treated as part of Makkah's periphery, because sacrificial animals are slaughtered there even though they are 'brought to the Ka'bah'.
This verse establishes that Mina is in the same legal territory as Makkah for certain rulings.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Outside Hajj season – no Jumu'ah in Mina by all. During Hajj – valid according to Shaykhayn (with ruler authority per al-Quduri), invalid according to Imam Muhammad. The student must understand why the ruler's permission matters.
Al-Quduri adds that only the ruler of Hijaz or the caliph can authorize Jumu'ah in Mina, not the Amir al-Mawsim (Hajj official).

Source Text

اور امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منی نہ تو شہر ہے اور نہ فنا شہر ہے بلکہ ایک گاؤں ہے اور گاؤں میں جمعہ جائز نہیں۔ اس لئے منی میں جائز نہ ہوگا کہیں وجہ ہے کہ منی میں بقر عید کی نماز نہیں ادا کی جاتی۔
امام محمد کے نزدیک منی فناء شہر (مکہ) میں اس لئے داخل نہیں ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک فناء کا اطلاق ایک غلوۃ ( چار سو ذراع) مکہ ہے اور منی ایک غلوۃ کی مقدار سے زائد ہے۔ شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منی با اشبہ شہرنہیں ہے لیکن حج کے موسم میں شہر بن جاتا ہے کیونکہ وہاں موسم حج میں بازار لگ جاتے : بادشاہ یا اس کا نائب اور قاضی اس موسم میں وہاں موجود ہوتے ہیں۔ چونکہ موسم حج کے علاوہ میں یہ سب شرطیں نہیں پائی جاتیں اک ۔ موسم حج کے علاوہ وہاں جمعہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ منی کے اندر بقر عید کی نماز نہیں پڑھی جاتی تو اس کی وجہ منی کا موسم حج میں کو ہونا نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس روز حاجی لوگ مناسک حج می ذبیح، حلق وغیرہ میں مشغول ہوتے ہیں۔ اور وقت تنگ ہو۔ اس لئے آسانی کے پیش نظر حجاج کو عید الاضحی کی نماز نہ پڑھنے کی اجازت دیدی گئی۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ منی چونکہ حرم میں شامل ہے ؟ لئے منشی فناءمہ میں سے ہے۔ اللہ رب العزت کا ارشاد ہے هَدْيَا بَالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ اس آیت میں منی کو کعبہ کے ساتھ تعبیر کیا گہاں بائیں طور پر قربانی اور ہدی کے جانور مکہ میں ذبح نہیں کئے جاتے بلکہ مٹی میں ذبح کئے جاتے ہیں اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مٹی مکہ کے حکم میں ہے یا فناء مکہ کے اور جمعہ ادا کرنا جس طرح شہر کے اندر جائز ہے اسی طرح فنا شہر کے اندر بھی جائز ہے۔ میدان عرفات میں بالاتفاق بعد جائز نہیں ہے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ عرفات تو فقط میدان ہے۔ آبادی و غیرہ کچھ بھی نہیں اور فناء مکہ میں بھی داخل نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے عرفات " میں ہے نہ حرم میں، پس جب عرفات نہ شہر ہے اور نہ فنا شہر تو وہاں جمعہ قائم کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب قدوری نے منی کے اندر جو از جمعہ کے لئے امیر حجاز یا خلیفہ ہونے کی قید اس لئے لگائی ہے کہ جمعہ قائم کرنے کی ولایت انہیں دونوں کو ہے۔ اور رہا وہ امیر جس کو امیر موسم کہتے ہیں وہ تو حج کے امور کا متولی ہوتا ہے نہ کہ اس کے علاوہ کا اس لئے اس کو ولایت جو حاصل نہیں ہے۔
And Imam Muhammad's proof is that Mina is neither a city nor the periphery of a city, but rather a village, and Jumu'ah is not permissible in a village. Therefore it will not be permissible in Mina. Another reason is that the prayer of Eid al-Adha is not performed in Mina. According to Imam Muhammad, Mina is not included in the periphery of Makkah because in his view the periphery (fina') extends to a bowshot (four hundred cubits) from Makkah, and Mina exceeds that distance. The proof of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that Mina is undoubtedly not a city, but during the Hajj season it becomes a city because markets are set up, the king or his deputy and the judge are present there during that season. Since these conditions are not found outside the Hajj season, Jumu'ah is not permissible there except during Hajj. As for the fact that Eid al-Adha prayer is not performed in Mina, the reason is not that Mina is not a city during Hajj, but rather that on that day pilgrims are occupied with the rites of Hajj, sacrifice, shaving, etc., and the time is short. Therefore, for ease, the pilgrims were permitted not to pray Eid al-Adha. The second proof is that since Mina is included in the Haram, it is part of the periphery of Makkah. Allah Almighty said: 'hadyan baligh al-ka'bah' (the sacrificial animal reaching the Ka'bah). In this verse, Mina is expressed as being with the Ka'bah, because generally sacrificial animals are not slaughtered in Makkah but in Mina. This shows that Mina is in the same ruling as Makkah or its periphery, and Jumu'ah is permissible in the periphery just as in the city. In the plain of Arafat, it is unanimously not permissible. The reason is that Arafat is only a plain with no population or anything else, and it is not included in the periphery of Makkah. Therefore, since Arafat is neither a city nor its periphery, establishing Jumu'ah there is not permissible. Imam al-Quduri placed the condition of the ruler of Hijaz or the caliph for Jumu'ah in Mina because the authority to establish Jumu'ah rests with them. As for the emir called 'Amir al-Mawsim', he is only in charge of Hajj affairs, not other matters, so he does not have that authority.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of Jumu'ah in Mina. Imam Muhammad holds that Jumu'ah is not valid in Mina because it is a village, not a city or its periphery, and Jumu'ah requires a city or its periphery (fina'). The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that during the Hajj season, Mina becomes like a city due to the presence of markets, the ruler, and the judge, so Jumu'ah is permissible then but not outside Hajj. The text then addresses an objection about Eid al-Adha not being prayed in Mina, explaining it is due to pilgrims' preoccupation with Hajj rites, not because Mina is not a city. A second proof for Mina being part of the periphery of Makkah is drawn from the Quranic verse 'hadyan baligh al-ka'bah' (5:95), where sacrificial animals are brought to the Ka'bah but slaughtered in Mina, indicating Mina is treated as part of Makkah's periphery. The passage also notes that Arafat is unanimously invalid for Jumu'ah. Finally, al-Quduri's condition of the ruler of Hijaz or caliph for Jumu'ah in Mina is explained as necessary because they hold the authority to establish Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
فناء (fina'): The periphery of a city that extends up to a bowshot (ghalwah, approximately 400 cubits) from the city limits. In Hanafi fiqh, this area is legally considered part of the city for purposes like Jumu'ah.
غلوۃ (ghalwah): A bowshot, a unit of distance equal to about 400 cubits (approx. 200 meters). Used in Hanafi fiqh to define the extent of a city's periphery.
امیر موسم (Amir al-Mawsim): The official appointed to oversee the Hajj season. In the text, he is distinguished from the ruler of Hijaz or caliph, as he does not have the authority to establish Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), why is Jumu'ah valid in Mina during the Hajj season?
A) Because Mina is a permanent city with a large population.
B) Because during Hajj, Mina has markets, a ruler, and a judge, making it functionally a city.
C) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed Jumu'ah there.
D) Because Mina is within a bowshot of Makkah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits Jumu'ah in Mina only during the Hajj season, based on the Shaykhayn's recognition of temporary city attributes, subject to the ruler's authorization.

Ruler's Permission as a Condition for Jumu'ah
States the Hanafi ruling that a ruler or his deputy is required for Jumu'ah and rebuts Shafi'i's objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi condition of the ruler's permission for Jumu'ah, identify the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the precedent of Ali's Jumu'ah during Uthman's siege.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires the ruler's permission to prevent fitna; necessity overrides if permission is impossible.

This lesson examines a key condition for Jumu'ah according to the Hanafi school: the presence or authorization of the ruler (sultan). The Hanafi view is that without the ruler's permission, the Jumu'ah prayer is not valid. However, Imam al-Shafi'i and even Imam Abu Yusuf within the Hanafi school disagree. The debate centers on the historical incident of Ali leading Jumu'ah during Uthman's siege. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi emphasis on order and authority in congregational worship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its condition
Identify the exact condition: the Sultan or his deputy must authorize Jumu'ah. Note that this is a condition for validity, not obligation.
The condition applies whether the ruler is just or unjust.
2
Identify the opposing school's proof
State Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: Ali led Jumu'ah during Uthman's siege without explicit permission, suggesting the condition is not required.
This is a dalil naqli (narrative evidence).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response offers two possibilities: either Ali had implicit permission, or necessity (impossibility of obtaining permission) made it permissible.
This shows the Hanafi school does not disregard the incident but explains it within its framework.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the Sultan's presence is not a condition. This is a minority view within the school.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the majority view.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, under a ruler, Jumu'ah requires his permission unless impossible. Without a Muslim ruler, the condition may drop or be fulfilled by a local authority.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of the dispute).

Source Text
