شرائط صحت ادا ، پہلی شرط سلطان ہے
ولايجوز اقامتها الاللسلطان اولمن امره السلطان لانها تقام بجمع عظيم وقد تقع المنازعة في التقله والتقديم وقد تقع في غيره فلابد منه تتميما لامرها
ترجمہ اور جمعہ قائم کرنا جائز نہیں مگر خلیفہ کے لئے یا اس کے لئے جس کو خلیفہ نے اجازت دیدی ہو۔ کیونکہ جمعہ ایک عظیم جمان کے ساتھ قائم کیا جاتا ہے اور کبھی آگے بڑھنے اور آگے بڑھانے میں جھگڑ اواقع ہو جاتا ہے کبھی اس کے علاوہ اور بات میں جھگڑا رہا ہے تو جمعہ کا کام پورا کرنے کے لئے خلیفہ یا اس کے نائب کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔
تشریح ادا جمعہ کے لئے سلطان کا ہونا بھی شرط ہے۔ سلطان وہ والی ہوتا ہے جس کے اوپر کوئی دوسرا والی نہ ہو جیسے خلیفہ یا اٹھی ہو جس کو سلطان نے حکم اور اجازت دیدی ہو۔ جیسے امیر قاضی یا خطیب بشر طیکہ انکو جمعہ قائم کرنے کی اجازت ہو۔ حضرت امام ثانی کہتے ہیں کہ ادا جمعہ کے لئے سلطان یا اس کے نائب کا ہونا شرط نہیں ہے۔ ( عنایہ ) امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس زمانے میں خلیفہ
حضرت عثمان غنی بلوائیوں کے گھیرے میں اپنے مکان کے اندر مدینہ منورہ میں محصور تھے تو حضرت علی نے لوگوں کو جمعہ کی نماز پڑھائی اور یہ مروی نہیں ہے کہ عثمان غنی کے حکم سے پڑھائی ہے۔ حالانکہ اس وقت خلافت حضرت عثمان کے ہاتھ میں تھی اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اور جمعہ کے لئے سلطان یا اس کے نائب کا ہونا شرط نہیں ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمعہ ایک عظیم جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کیا جاتا ہے کیونکہ وہ جامع الجماعات ہے۔ اور حال یہ ہے کہ کبھی جھگڑ اواقع ہوتا ہے آگے ہونے میں ایک کہتا ہے کہ میں امامت کروں گا اور دوسرا کہتا ہے کہ میں امامت کروں گا اور کبھی آگے کرنے میں جھگڑ اواقع ہوتا ہے ایک گروہ کہتا ہے کہ ہم فلاں بزرگ کو امام کریں گے اور دوسرا گروہ کہتا ہے کہ نہیں بلکہ فلاں کو امام کریں گے۔ اور کبھی تقدیم اور تقدم کے علاوہ دوسری بات میں جھگڑا ہوتا ہے مثالا کچھ لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ ہماری مجد میں جمعہ ادا کیا جائے اور کچھ کی رائے اس کے خلاف ہے کچھ کہتے ہیں کہ جلدی ادا کیا جائے اور کچھ دیر میں چاہتے ہیں پس مجمع عظیم کے اس اختلاف سے شیطان کو فتنہ پردازی کا خوب موقع ملے گا۔ اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ ادا جمعہ کے لئے خلیفہ یا اس کے نائب کا ہونا ضروری ہے خلیفہ عادل ہو یا ظالم ہو امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ حضرت علی نے حضرت عثمان کے حکم سے جمعہ کی نماز پڑھائی ہو۔ اور اگر تسلیم کر لیں کہ حضرت عثمان نے حکم نہیں دیا تھا تو ہم جوابدیں گے کہ جب لوگ حضرت علی کے پاس جمع ہو گئے اور اوگ اقامت جمعہ کے محتاج بھی تھے تو حضرت علیؓ کے لئے جمعہ پڑھانا جائز ہو گیا کیونکہ جب خلیفہ سے اجازت حاصل کرنا متعذر ہو گیا تو جس پر وگ اتفاق کریں وہ پڑھائے۔
Conditions for the validity of performance: First condition: the Sultan. And it is not permissible to establish Jumu'ah except for the Sultan or for one whom the Sultan has commanded, because it is established with a great gathering, and disputes may occur about precedence and appointment, and about other matters, so it is necessary for the completion of its affair. Translation: And establishing Jumu'ah is not permissible except for the Caliph or for one whom the Caliph has permitted. Because Jumu'ah is established with a great congregation, and sometimes disputes arise about going forward and putting forward, and sometimes disputes arise in other matters, so for the completion of the Jumu'ah affair, the Caliph or his deputy is necessary. Commentary: For the performance of Jumu'ah, the presence of a Sultan is also a condition. The Sultan is a ruler above whom there is no other ruler, like the Caliph or one whom the Sultan has commanded and permitted, like an emir, qadi, or khatib, provided they have permission to establish Jumu'ah. Imam Abu Yusuf says that for the performance of Jumu'ah, the presence of the Sultan or his deputy is not a condition. (from al-'Inayah) Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that at the time when Caliph Uthman was besieged in his house in Madinah by rebels, Ali led the people in Jumu'ah prayer, and it is not reported that he did so by Uthman's command, even though the caliphate was in Uthman's hands. This shows that the presence of the Sultan or his deputy is not a condition for Jumu'ah. Our proof is that Jumu'ah is performed with a great congregation, for it is the gathering of all congregations. And disputes sometimes occur about going forward: one says 'I will lead,' another says 'I will lead,' and sometimes about appointing: one group says 'We will make so-and-so imam,' another says 'No, we will make so-and-so imam.' And sometimes disputes occur in other matters besides precedence and appointment, for example, some people say 'Jumu'ah should be performed in our mosque,' and others disagree; some want it early, others late. Such differences in a great congregation give Satan a good opportunity for causing fitna. Therefore we say that for the performance of Jumu'ah, the Caliph or his deputy is necessary, whether the Caliph is just or unjust. The response to Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that it is possible that Ali led the prayer by Uthman's command. And if we concede that Uthman did not command, then we reply that when the people gathered around Ali and they needed Jumu'ah to be established, it became permissible for Ali to lead because when obtaining permission from the Caliph became impossible, then whoever they agree upon may lead.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that the presence of the Sultan (caliph or his authorized deputy) is a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah. It first states the ruling textually from the matn, then provides commentary. The Hanafi school argues that Jumu'ah involves a large gathering, and without a central authority, disputes about leadership, location, and timing could cause fitna. Imam Shafi'i objects using the historical incident of Ali leading Jumu'ah during Uthman's siege without reported permission. The Hanafi response offers two possibilities: either Ali had implicit permission, or if not, necessity (the people needed Jumu'ah and permission was impossible) made it permissible for him to lead. The passage also notes that Imam Abu Yusuf (Hazrat Imam Thani) does not consider the Sultan's presence a condition, indicating an intra-Hanafi difference.

Key Terms
سلطان (sultan): The supreme ruler (caliph) who has no superior; his permission is required for Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof that Ali led Jumu'ah without Uthman's permission?
A) They deny the historical event occurred.
B) They argue it was not Jumu'ah but Zuhr.
C) They say permission was given or necessity made it permissible.
D) They accept it and change their ruling.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the ruler's authorization for Jumu'ah to prevent disputes; the Shafi'i objection based on Ali's incident is countered by necessity or implied permission.

Time Condition for Jumu'ah Prayer and the Rule of Building
Ruling with proof on Jumu'ah time condition and the dispute on building.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time condition for Jumu'ah according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling if the time expires before completing Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is only valid in Zuhr time; if time expires, it must be repeated as Zuhr from the beginning.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a crucial condition for the validity of Jumu'ah: it must be performed within the time of Zuhr. The Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly tied Jumu'ah to the decline of the sun. But what happens if the congregation delays so much that Zuhr time ends? The Hanafi school has a clear ruling that differs from other madhhabs. Let's examine the proof and the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Time is a condition (shart) for Jumu'ah. Determine what time is specified: the time of Zuhr, from the decline of the sun (zawal) until the shadow of an object equals its length.
This is the same time as Zuhr prayer.
2
Locate the proof
The hadith of the Prophet commanding Mus'ab ibn Umayr: 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Jumu'ah.' Also the practice of the Prophet reported by Anas and Salamah.
These are ahad hadith but accepted by Hanafi.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The command at a specific time (zawal) indicates that time is a condition; the act is valid only at that time. The imperative 'salli' indicates obligation.
Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the consequence of expiry
If the time for Zuhr exits while the imam is in Jumu'ah, the Jumu'ah becomes invalid (fasid). The prayer must be repeated as Zuhr from the beginning.
Building (bina') is not allowed.
5
Evaluate the dispute
Shafi'i and Zufar allow building Zuhr upon Jumu'ah because they consider Jumu'ah a shortened form of Zuhr. Hanafi rejects this due to differences in rulings (number of rak'ahs, khutbah, etc.).
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether the prayer needs to be started anew or can be continued.

Source Text

و من شرائطها الوقت فتصح فى وقت الظهر ولا تصح بعده لقوله عليه السلام اذا مالت الشمس فصل بالناس الجمعة و لوخرج الوقت و هو فيها استقبل الظهر ولا يبنيه عليها لاختلافهما رجمہ اور جمعہ کی شرائط میں سے وقت ہے پس جمعہ وقت ظہر میں صحیح ہوگا اور وقت ظہر کے بعد صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے جب آفتاب ڈھل جائے لوگوں کو جمعہ پڑھانا اور اگر یہ وقت نکل گیا حالانکہ مصلی نماز جمعہ میں ہے تو از سر نو ظہر پڑھے اور ظہر کو جمعہ پر یانہ کرے کیونکہ جمعہ اور ظہر دونوں میں اختلاف ہے۔
شریح . جمعہ کے شرائط میں سے وقت بھی ہے یعنی جمعہ کی نماز ظہر کے وقت میں صحیح ہے اس کے بعد صحیح نہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ انحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مصعب بن عمیر کو جب مدینہ منورہ بھیجا تو فرمایا تھا اذا مالت الشمس فصل بالناس الجمعة يعنى جب سورج مل جائے تو لوگوں کو جمعہ کی نماز پڑھانا بخاری کی روایت ہے عن انس كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي الجمعة حين نميل الشمس ، حضرت انسؓ سے مروی ہے کہ رسول خدا صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم جس وقت آفتاب ڈھل جاتاجمعہ کی نماز پڑھتے۔ مسلم میں ہے عن سلمه بن الاکوع رضی الله تعالى عنه كنا نجمع مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا زالت الشمس یعنی ہم لوگ جمعہ پڑھتے جب آفتاب ڈھل جاتا تھا۔ صاحب قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ اگر ظہر کی نماز کا وقت اس حال میں نکل گیا کہ امام نماز جمعہ میں مشغول ہے تو جمعہ کی نماز فاسد ہوگئی۔ اب از سرنو ظہر کی نماز ادا کرے گا۔ جمعہ پر ظہر کی بناء کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔امام شافعی اور امام زفر کے نزدیک نا کرنا جائز ہے ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمعہ، ظہر کی قصر نماز ہے چنانچہ جو وقت ظہر کا ہے وہی جمعہ کا ہے پس جب جمعہ ظہر ہی ہے تو جمعہ
And among its conditions is time: so it is valid in the time of Zuhr and not valid after it, because he (peace be upon him) said: 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Jumu'ah.' And if the time exits while he is in it, he should begin Zuhr anew and not build Zuhr upon it because of their difference. Translation: And among the conditions of Jumu'ah is time. So Jumu'ah is valid in the time of Zuhr and not valid after it. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Jumu'ah.' And if this time passes while the worshipper is in the Jumu'ah prayer, then he should perform Zuhr anew and not build Zuhr upon it because Jumu'ah and Zuhr are different. Commentary: Time is also among the conditions of Jumu'ah, meaning Jumu'ah prayer is valid in Zuhr time, not valid after it. The proof is that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) sent Mus'ab ibn Umayr to Madinah, he said: 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Jumu'ah.' Bukhari narrates from Anas that the Prophet used to pray Jumu'ah when the sun declined. Muslim narrates from Salamah ibn al-Akwa': 'We used to pray Jumu'ah with the Messenger of Allah when the sun declined.' Al-Quduri said: If the time of Zuhr exits while the imam is engaged in Jumu'ah prayer, then the Jumu'ah prayer becomes invalid. He should then perform Zuhr from the beginning. It is not permissible to build Zuhr upon Jumu'ah. According to Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar, it is permissible to build. Their proof is that Jumu'ah is a shortened form of Zuhr, so the time of Zuhr is the same as Jumu'ah. Since Jumu'ah is essentially Zuhr, then... (page cuts off)
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage states that time is a condition for Jumu'ah: it must be performed within the time of Zuhr, i.e., from the decline of the sun (zawal) until the shadow of an object equals its length. The proof comes from hadith: the Prophet commanded Mus'ab ibn Umayr to lead Jumu'ah at zawal, and the practice of the Prophet is reported by Anas and Salamah. If the time for Zuhr exits while the imam is still in Jumu'ah (e.g., he delayed too much), then the Jumu'ah is invalid and must be repeated as Zuhr. It cannot be 'built upon' (ibna') by simply intending Zuhr, because Jumu'ah and Zuhr are different prayers. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar hold that building is permissible because Jumu'ah is essentially a shortened Zuhr, but the Hanafi position (from al-Quduri) rejects this due to their difference in rulings.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): Building a prayer upon another, i.e., if Jumu'ah time expires, one cannot simply intend Zuhr while continuing; must start anew.
زوال (zawal): The decline of the sun from its zenith; the beginning of Zuhr time.
شرط (shart): A condition that must be present for the prayer to be valid; time is a shart for Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if the time for Zuhr expires while the imam is leading Jumu'ah prayer?
A) The Jumu'ah becomes Zuhr automatically.
B) The Jumu'ah is valid if a rak'ah was completed in time.
C) The Jumu'ah is invalid and must be repeated as Zuhr.
D) The imam should continue and then make up a separate Zuhr.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is only valid within Zuhr time; if time expires, the prayer is invalid and must be fully repeated as Zuhr.

Is the Ruler's Permission a Condition for Jumu'ah?
Debates the necessity of the ruler for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the role of the ruler in Jumu'ah, cite the key proof from the practice of Ali, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school does not require the ruler's permission for Jumu'ah; the congregation may appoint the imam.

Friday prayer is a weekly obligation that gathers the community. A key question among scholars is whether the presence or permission of a political ruler is necessary for its validity. This lesson examines the Hanafi position, grounded in the precedent of Ali ibn Abi Talib, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
What exactly is the condition being disputed? Is it the physical presence of the ruler, his permission, or the existence of any appointing authority?
The dispute is about whether a ruler or his deputy must be present or give permission for Jumu'ah to be valid.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
What does the Hanafi school hold, and what evidence do they cite? Identify the historical incident and the rational argument.
The Hanafi proof includes Ali leading Jumu'ah without Uthman's explicit order and the need to avoid fitna by allowing community appointment.
3
State the opposing (Shafi'i) position
What does Imam al-Shafi'i require, and what is his evidence?
Shafi'i argues that the ruler's permission is necessary because the ruler oversees public religious affairs.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
How do the Hanafis rebut the Shafi'i argument? Do they accept the possibility of implicit permission or rely on necessity?
The Hanafi response: either Ali had implicit permission, or if not, necessity permits the congregation to appoint an imam when the ruler is unavailable.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
What is the actual consequence in practice? How does this difference affect Muslim communities today?
Hanafis allow Jumu'ah without a ruler's permission, while Shafi'is require it. This gives the Hanafi view greater flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سہم حضرت عثمان غنی بلوائیوں کے گھیرے میں اپنے مکان کے اندر مدینہ منورہ میں محصور تھے تو حضرت علی نے لوگوں کو جمعہ کی نماز پڑھائی اور یہ مروی نہیں ہے کہ عثمان غنی کے حکم سے پڑھائی ہے۔ حالانکہ اس وقت خلافت حضرت عثمان کے ہاتھ میں تھی اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اور جمعہ کے لئے سلطان یا اس کے نائب کا ہونا شرط نہیں ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جمعہ ایک عظیم جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کیا جاتا ہے کیونکہ وہ جامع الجماعات ہے۔ اور حال یہ ہے کہ کبھی جھگڑ اواقع ہوتا ہے آگے ہونے میں ایک کہتا ہے کہ میں امامت کروں گا اور دوسرا کہتا ہے کہ میں امامت کروں گا اور کبھی آگے کرنے میں جھگڑ اواقع ہوتا ہے ایک گروہ کہتا ہے کہ ہم فلاں بزرگ کو امام کریں گے اور دوسرا گروہ کہتا ہے کہ نہیں بلکہ فلاں کو امام کریں گے۔ اور کبھی تقدیم اور تقدم کے علاوہ دوسری بات میں جھگڑا ہوتا ہے مثالا کچھ لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ ہماری مجد میں جمعہ ادا کیا جائے اور کچھ کی رائے اس کے خلاف ہے کچھ کہتے ہیں کہ جلدی ادا کیا جائے اور کچھ دیر میں چاہتے ہیں پس مجمع عظیم کے اس اختلاف سے شیطان کو فتنہ پردازی کا خوب موقع ملے گا۔ اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ ادا جمعہ کے لئے خلیفہ یا اس کے نائب کا ہونا ضروری ہے خلیفہ عادل ہو یا ظالم ہو امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ حضرت علی نے حضرت عثمان کے حکم سے جمعہ کی نماز پڑھائی ہو۔ اور اگر تسلیم کر لیں کہ حضرت عثمان نے حکم نہیں دیا تھا تو ہم جوابدیں گے کہ جب لوگ حضرت علی کے پاس جمع ہو گئے اور اوگ اقامت جمعہ کے محتاج بھی تھے تو حضرت علیؓ کے لئے جمعہ پڑھانا جائز ہو گیا کیونکہ جب خلیفہ سے اجازت حاصل کرنا متعذر ہو گیا تو جس پر وگ اتفاق کریں وہ پڑھائے۔
The portion: Hazrat Uthman Ghani was besieged by rebels inside his house in Medina, so Hazrat Ali led the people in Friday prayer, and it is not reported that he did so by the order of Uthman Ghani. Although the caliphate was in the hands of Hazrat Uthman at that time, this shows that for Friday prayer, the presence of a sultan or his deputy is not a condition. Our proof is that Friday prayer is performed with a large congregation, because it is the assembly of assemblies. And the situation is that sometimes a dispute occurs about who will lead: one says 'I will lead' and another says 'I will lead'; sometimes a dispute occurs about whom to appoint: one group says 'We will make so-and-so imam' and another group says 'No, rather we will make so-and-so imam'; and sometimes a dispute occurs about something other than appointment and precedence: for example, some people say 'Friday prayer should be performed in our mosque' and some have the opposite opinion, some say 'it should be performed early' and some want it late. So from this difference of a great multitude, Satan will have a great opportunity for mischief. Therefore we said that for performing Friday prayer, the presence of a caliph or his deputy is necessary, whether the caliph is just or unjust. The answer to Imam Shafi'i's proof is that it is possible that Hazrat Ali led the Friday prayer by the order of Hazrat Uthman. And if we accept that Hazrat Uthman did not order, then we will answer that when the people gathered around Hazrat Ali and were in need of performing Friday prayer, then it became permissible for Hazrat Ali to lead Friday, because when obtaining permission from the caliph became impossible, then the one upon whom they agree should lead.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the condition of a ruler for Friday prayer. The Hanafi position, based on the historical incident of 'Ali leading Jumu'ah without 'Uthman's explicit permission, is that a ruler's permission is not a prerequisite; the congregation may appoint an imam. The objection of Shafi'i is that 'Ali may have had implicit permission, and the Hanafi response is that if permission was impossible, it is still valid. The text also provides a rational proof: the potential for disputes in a large gathering necessitates an authority to prevent fitna, but this does not mean the ruler must be involved—the community's agreement suffices.

Key Terms
سلطان (sultān): The ruler or his authorized deputy who holds political authority.
شرط (shart): A condition that must be present for an act to be valid; if missing, the act is invalid.
خلافت (khilāfat): The office or authority of the caliph, the supreme leader of the Muslim community.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the necessity of a ruler for Friday prayer?
A) It is a condition (shart) without which Jumu'ah is invalid.
B) It is recommended but not obligatory; the congregation may appoint an imam.
C) It is required only if there is no agreement among the people.
D) It is obligatory only if the ruler is just.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require the ruler's permission for Jumu'ah; the congregation can appoint an imam, based on the precedent of Ali and the necessity to prevent fitna.

When the Time of Jumu'ah Passes: Building (Bina') or Starting Anew?
Establishes Jumu'ah time condition and dispute on bina'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on building (bina') Zuhr upon Jumu'ah when time exits, and explain why taghayyur prevents it.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is a distinct prayer; if its time lapses, it cannot be turned into Zuhr.

This lesson explores a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i/Imam Zufar regarding what happens if the time of Zuhr expires while Friday prayer is in progress. The key question: can the worshiper simply complete the prayer as Zuhr (building), or must he start over? We will examine the proofs from hadith, the Hanafi reasoning based on differences between the two prayers, and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Understand that if Zuhr time exits during Jumu'ah, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated as a new Zuhr prayer from the beginning.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar allow building (bina') because they consider Jumu'ah a shortened form of Zuhr.
This is based on the analogy of qasr.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
Review the hadith evidence that Jumu'ah time is only at zawal, and the rational proof that taghayyur (difference) prevents building, similar to how it prevents iqtida'.
Differences in name, rak'ahs, recitation, and conditions create taghayyur.
4
Analyse the opposing proof
Understand the opposing argument: Jumu'ah is essentially a shortened Zuhr, so the same time applies and building should be permissible.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis require a new Zuhr prayer; Shafi'is allow completing the same prayer as Zuhr.
This affects latecomers and those who start Jumu'ah near the end of Zuhr time.

And among its conditions is time, so it is valid in the time of Zuhr and not valid after it, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Friday prayer.' And if the time exits while he is in it, he should begin Zuhr anew and not build upon it due to their difference. Commentary: Among the conditions of Friday is time. So Friday is valid in Zuhr time and not valid after Zuhr time, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Friday prayer.' And if this time exits while the worshiper is in Friday prayer, then he should pray Zuhr from the beginning and not build Zuhr upon Friday, because there is a difference between Friday and Zuhr. Explanation: Among the conditions of Friday is time, meaning Friday prayer is valid in Zuhr time and not valid after it. The proof is that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) sent Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr to Medina, he said: 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Friday prayer.' Bukhari narrates from Anas: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray Friday when the sun declined.' Muslim narrates from Salamah ibn al-Akwa': 'We used to pray Friday with the Messenger of Allah when the sun declined.' The author of al-Quduri said: If the time of Zuhr exits while the imam is engaged in Friday prayer, then the Friday prayer becomes invalid. He will then perform Zuhr prayer anew. Building Zuhr upon Friday is not permissible. According to Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar, building is permissible. Their proof is that Friday is a shortened form of Zuhr, so the time of Zuhr is the same as Friday. Since Friday essentially is Zuhr, building Zuhr upon Friday is valid. Our proof is that there is a difference and distinction between Friday and Zuhr in name, quantity, quality, and conditions. In name: one is called Friday and the other Zuhr. In quantity: Zuhr has four rak'ahs and Friday has two. In quality: Friday has audible recitation (jahr) while Zuhr has silent (sirr). In conditions: Friday has specific conditions that Zuhr does not. In any case, there is distinction and difference between Friday and Zuhr, and distinction prevents building, just as it prevents following (iqitida'). Therefore we said: building Zuhr upon Friday is not correct.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that Friday prayer is valid only within Zuhr time. If the time of Zuhr expires during the prayer, the Friday prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated as Zuhr from scratch; one cannot 'build' (bina') Zuhr upon Friday. The text contrasts the Hanafi view with that of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar, who analogize Friday to a shortened Zuhr and permit building. The Hanafi response emphasizes the differences (taghayyur) between the two prayers in name, number of rak'ahs, recitation, and conditions. This difference prevents building, similar to how differences prevent one from following an imam in a different prayer. The proofs from hadith establish that the Prophet always performed Friday immediately after zawal.

Key Terms
وقت الظهر (waqt al-zuhr): The period from zawal (sun decline) until the shadow of an object equals its height (asr al-thani) according to Hanafis.
بناء (bina'): Connecting a subsequent prayer (Zuhr) to the previous incomplete prayer (Jumu'ah) without starting anew.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the time of Zuhr exits while the imam is still in the middle of Jumu'ah prayer, what does the Hanafi school say?
A) Complete the prayer as Jumu'ah.
B) Complete it as Zuhr by adding two rak'ahs.
C) The prayer is invalid; must repeat as Zuhr from the beginning.
D) It is valid as Jumu'ah but one must also pray Zuhr later.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah prayer is a separate obligation from Zuhr; if its prescribed time (Zuhr time) exits during prayer, the prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated as Zuhr from the beginning, because building is prevented by the fundamental differences between the two prayers.

The Khutbah as a Condition for Friday Prayer: The Hanafi–Shafi'i Dispute
Establishes khutbah as a condition with two sermons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that one khutbah is permissible and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The khutbah is a condition for Jumu'ah, but the sitting between two khutbahs is sunnah, not wajib.

The Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) is a distinctive act of worship that Allah made obligatory upon the believing community. One of its unique conditions is the sermon (khutbah). This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the khutbah, focusing on the requirement of two sermons and the sitting between them. We will also explore the Shafi'i view and the evidence each school presents.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school holds regarding the khutbah: it is a condition for Jumu'ah, two khutbahs are obligatory (wajib), and the sitting between them is sunnah (not a condition).
Use the passage to find these specifics.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The passage names Imam al-Shafi'i. State his position: the sitting between the two khutbahs is a condition, and one khutbah is insufficient.
This is the contrasting view.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is 'tawaruth' – continuous transmission from the elders. Explain what this means.
Tawaruth refers to the practice being passed down generation after generation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond with the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah, showing that the Prophet initially gave one khutbah and later switched to two when he grew older. This indicates that one khutbah is permissible.
This hadith directly challenges the necessity of two khutbahs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? Hanafis allow one khutbah in circumstances of necessity; Shafi'is require two even in difficulty.
This affects fatwa and practice.

Source Text

And among them is the khutbah, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) never prayed Jumu'ah without a khutbah in his life. And it is before the prayer after zawal; with it the sunnah has been transmitted, and he would deliver two khutbahs, separating them with a sitting; with this transmission has continued. Commentary: One of the conditions of Friday is the khutbah. So Friday prayer is not valid without the khutbah. The proof is that the founder of the pure Shari'ah (peace be upon him) never prayed any Jumu'ah without a khutbah in his life. If the khutbah were not among the conditions of Friday, he would have omitted it at least once to indicate permissibility. The Friday khutbah is obligatory before the Friday prayer and after zawal. Therefore, if one delivers it after the Friday prayer or before zawal, it is not valid. The proof is that Friday stands in place of Zuhr contrary to analogy (qiyas), and the sunnah came in this manner that Jumu'ah is tied to the khutbah, as the hadith has come that the Messenger of God never prayed Jumu'ah without a khutbah. The rule is: whatever is established contrary to qiyas is restricted to its own context. So the legislation of Jumu'ah will be in this manner: the khutbah is delivered before the prayer. Imam al-Quduri said that two khutbahs are obligatory, and between them one should separate with a sitting the length of three verses. With this, transmission has continued, meaning it is transmitted from the elders generation after generation. In our view, this sitting is not a condition but for rest. Imam al-Shafi'i said it is a condition, such that according to him it is not permissible to suffice with one khutbah. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is transmission (tawaruth). Our proof is the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to deliver one khutbah standing; then when he reached an older age, he made them two khutbahs and sat between them.' This shows that it is permissible to suffice with one khutbah.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage establishes the khutbah as a condition (shart) for Jumu'ah. The Hanafi ruling is that two khutbahs are obligatory (wajib), delivered after zawal and before the prayer. The sitting between them is not a condition but a sunnah for rest. The proof is the constant practice of the Prophet. The text addresses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that the sitting is a condition and that one khutbah is insufficient. The Hanafi response cites the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah, indicating that the Prophet initially delivered one khutbah and later adopted two as a practice for comfort, implying that one is still permissible. The comment about 'contrary to qiyas' explains that Jumu'ah is a special form of worship tied to the khutbah, so its details follow sunnah rather than analogy.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): A sermon delivered before Friday prayer, consisting of praise of Allah, supplication, and exhortation.
قعدة (qa'dah): The short sitting between the two khutbahs, considered sunnah by Hanafis, condition by Shafi'is.
توارث (tawaruth): Continuous transmission of practice from generation to generation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A verse from the Quran
B) The hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah
C) Analogy (qiyas) to Zuhr prayer
D) The absence of any proof for two khutbahs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits one khutbah for Jumu'ah based on the Prophet's early practice, while the Shafi'i school requires two; the sitting between them is sunnah in the Hanafi view.

Standing and Purity in the Friday Khutbah: Obligation or Sunnah?
States the ruling on standing and taharah with proof and disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing and taharah in the Friday khutbah and compare it with the positions of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Standing and taharah in the Friday khutbah are sunnah, not obligatory; omitting them makes the khutbah valid but disliked.

In this passage, we examine the requirements for delivering the Friday khutbah. While some scholars consider standing and ritual purity obligatory, the Hanafi school views them as recommended practices. Understanding the basis of this difference is crucial for knowing when a khutbah—and consequently the Friday prayer—remains valid.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school says about standing and taharah during the Friday khutbah. Is either considered obligatory (fard/wajib) or merely sunnah?
The text states: 'he delivers the khutbah standing with taharah' but also says it is permissible if done sitting or without purity.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Determine which scholars hold a stricter opinion. Imam Shafi'i considers standing obligatory; Imam Abu Yusuf (and Shafi'i) consider taharah a condition for validity.
Look for the reasoning behind their view: the khutbah is said to stand in place of two rak'ahs, so it should resemble salah.
3
Follow the opponent’s proof
Examine the evidence cited by the opposing schools. What do they rely on?
They argue that the khutbah substitutes for two rak'ahs; therefore, like salah, it requires standing and purity.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school counter these arguments? What alternative evidence do they present?
The Hanafi proof includes mutawārith (inherited practice) and analogy with the adhan. They also stress that the purpose (dhikr and admonition) is achieved even if the khatib sits.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence of this disagreement?
If the khatib sits or lacks wudu, the Hanafi school still accepts the Friday prayer, while other schools would reject it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويخطب قائما على الطهارة لان القيام فيها متوارث ثم هى شرط الصلوة فيستحب فيها الطهارة كالاذان و لو خطب قاعدا او على غير طهارة جاز لحصول المقصود الا انه يكره لمخالفة التوارث وللفصل بينها وبين الصلوة
And he delivers the khutbah standing with taharah, because standing in it is inherited practice, then it is a condition of prayer, so taharah is recommended in it like the adhan. And if he delivers the khutbah sitting or without taharah, it is permissible because the purpose is achieved, but it is disliked due to opposing the inherited practice and due to the separation between it and the prayer.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the Friday khutbah. The author begins by stating that the khatib should deliver the khutbah while standing and in a state of purity (taharah). This is a ruling statement. The reason given is that standing in the khutbah is mutawārith (inherited practice from the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions). Since the khutbah is a condition for the validity of the Friday prayer, it is recommended (mustahabb) to be in a state of purity, analogous to the adhan (call to prayer). If one delivers the khutbah sitting or without wudu, the khutbah is still valid (jā'iz) because the essential purpose—remembrance and admonition—is achieved. However, it is makruh (disliked) for two reasons: first, it contradicts the inherited practice, and second, it introduces a separation between the khutbah and the prayer because if the khatib is impure, he will have to purify himself after the khutbah before leading the prayer. The commentary explains that this ruling involves disputes with other schools. The Hanafi position is that standing is sunnah, not obligatory. Imam Shafi‘i considers standing obligatory. Similarly, regarding taharah, the Hanafi school holds it mustahabb, while Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi‘i consider it a condition for validity. The proof for standing is the incident mentioned in the Quran (Surah al-Jumu‘ah, verse 11) where people left the Prophet standing, indicating his practice. The commentary clarifies that the author's analogy with adhan is not about both being conditions for prayer, but about both being acts that occur after the entry of time, for which taharah is recommended.

Key Terms
متوارث (mutawārith): Inherited practice passed down from the Prophet and Companions without interruption.
طهارة (taharah): Ritual purity, specifically having wudu or ghusl as required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The khutbah is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The khutbah is valid but makruh.
C) The khutbah is valid and not makruh.
D) The khutbah is invalid unless he recites a long khutbah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that standing and purity are sunnah, not conditions for the Friday khutbah; the khutbah remains valid if omitted but is makruh.

Sufficiency of Minimal Dhikr in the Friday Khutbah
Inter-madhhab dispute on minimum khutbah content

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the minimum content of the Friday khutbah and evaluate the evidence for each position.

Core Idea
One phrase of dhikr can fulfill the khutbah according to Abu Hanifa, but caution requires a full customary sermon.

The Friday khutbah is an integral condition for the validity of Jumu'ah, but how much must be said? In this passage, we encounter a three-way dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa’s permissive view, the stricter view of his two disciples (the Sahibayn), and the Shafi‘i requirement of two full khutbahs. We will trace the proofs each side relies on and see how the same Quranic verse can yield different rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Note each scholar’s ruling: Abu Hanifa allows any dhikr; the Sahibayn require a conventionally recognized khutbah; al-Shafi‘i requires two khutbahs. Understand the practical difference.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Quote the Quranic verse 'Fas‘aw ila dhikr Allah' and the incident of ‘Uthman. Explain how these support that minimal dhikr suffices.
The word 'dhikr' in the verse is general, and the silent consensus of the Companions on ‘Uthman's action is key.
3
Examine the counter-proofs
Sahibayn argue that the obligation is the khutbah, which is a specific speech, and a single tasbih is not called a khutbah. Shafi‘i relies on the customary practice of the Prophet (two khutbahs).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa’s response: the Shari‘ah does not require the customary name; what matters is the reality of dhikr. The Quran uses ‘dhikr’ absolutely, and the Companions’ acceptance validates the minimal form.
The intention to deliver the khutbah is essential; a dhikr uttered unintentionally (e.g., sneezing) does not count.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a khatib only says 'Alhamdulillah', according to Abu Hanifa the Jumu'ah prayer is valid; according to the Sahibayn it is invalid. In practice, the mufta bihi often favors caution (Sahibayn), but Abu Hanifa’s view is legally sound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان اقتصر على ذكر الله جاز عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لابد من ذكر طويل يسمى خطبة لان الخطبة هي الواجبة والتسبيحة والتحميدة لا تسمى خطبة وقال الشافعى لا يجوز حتى يخطب خطبتين اعتبار اللمتعارف وله قوله تعالى فاسعوا الى ذكر الله من غير فصل وعن عثمان انه قال الحمد الله فارتج عليه فنزل وصلى
If he confines himself to the remembrance of Allah, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: A long remembrance that is called a khutbah is necessary, because the obligatory thing is the khutbah, and one tasbih or one tahmid is not called a khutbah. And al-Shafi‘i said: It is not permissible until he delivers two khutbahs, considering the customary practice. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah' without specification. And from ‘Uthman, it is narrated that he said 'Alhamdulillah' and then became tongue-tied, so he descended and prayed.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage addresses the minimum content required for the Friday khutbah. There is a three-way dispute. First, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that any dhikr of Allah, even a single phrase like 'Alhamdulillah' or 'Subhanallah', suffices for the obligatory khutbah if done with the intention of delivering the khutbah. However, if the same phrase is uttered due to sneezing or astonishment, it does not count as khutbah by consensus. Second, the Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) require a conventionally recognized khutbah, which includes praising Allah, sending salawat upon the Prophet, and supplicating for the Muslims. They argue that the obligation is the khutbah itself, and a minimal tasbih or tahmid is not called a khutbah in common usage. Third, Imam Shafi‘i requires two khutbahs, each of a certain length, based on the customary practice of the Prophet. The proof for Abu Hanifa is the general Quranic command 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah,' which tafsir interprets as the khutbah, and the word 'dhikr' includes both little and much. Additionally, the incident of Caliph ‘Uthman is cited: when he ascended the pulpit and said 'Alhamdulillah' but became tongue-tied, he descended and led the prayer. The Companions present did not object, indicating consensus (ijma) that such a minimal khutbah is valid. The commentary explains that Abu Hanifa's argument is that the obligation is the remembrance of Allah, and there is no specification of quantity. The objection of the Sahibayn that 'Alhamdulillah' is not called a khutbah in custom is countered by the fact that the Shari‘ah does not require the customary name; what matters is the reality of dhikr.

Key Terms
خطبہ (khutbah): The sermon delivered before the Friday prayer; an obligatory condition for the validity of Jumu'ah.
ذکر اللہ (dhikr Allah): Remembrance of Allah, including any phrase like tahmid, tasbih, tahlil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the proof used by Imam Abu Hanifa to allow a minimal dhikr for the Friday khutbah?
A) The hadith 'The best speech is the Book of Allah'
B) The Quranic verse 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah' and the action of ‘Uthman
C) The consensus of the Sahibayn
D) The practice of the people of Madinah

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah can be fulfilled by a minimal dhikr according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn and other schools require a more substantial sermon; in practice, caution favors a full khutbah.

Minimum Content of the Friday Khutbah: A Single Dhikr or Customary Sermon?
Dispute among Hanafi imams and Shafiʿi on minimum khutbah content

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and al-Shafiʿi on the minimum required content of the Friday khutbah, and apply their respective evidence to determine the validity of a brief dhikr.

Core Idea
A single 'Alhamdulillah' can suffice as Friday khutbah according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to Sahibayn or al-Shafiʿi.

The Friday khutbah is a condition for the validity of Jumuʿah prayer, but what is the minimum content required? This lesson examines the disagreement among the Hanafi imams themselves and with the Shafiʿi school. Abu Hanifa argues that any dhikr, even a single tasbih, suffices if intended as khutbah, while the Sahibayn and al-Shafiʿi demand a customary sermon. We will trace the evidence from the Quran, the practice of ʿUthman, and the Prophet's words.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the positions
State the core question: what is the minimum content required for the Friday khutbah? List the three positions: Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, and al-Shafiʿi.
The dispute is about the quantity of dhikr, not the conditions of the khatib.
2
Analyze the evidence for each position
For Abu Hanifa: Quran 62:9 (absolute dhikr), ʿUthman's action with no Companion objection, and the Prophet calling a brief statement a khutbah. For Sahibayn: the term 'khutbah' customarily requires a speech of certain length. For al-Shafiʿi: two sermons based on custom.
Note the difference between textual evidence (Quran, hadith) and customary evidence (ʿurf).
3
Understand the Hanafi internal difference
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree with Abu Hanifa. Their evidence is that a single tasbih is not called a khutbah in common usage. However, Abu Hanifa relies on the absolute wording of the Quran and the action of ʿUthman, which implied tacit consensus.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, but the author (Ashraf al-Hidaya) rules with Abu Hanifa.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If a khatib says only 'Alhamdulillah' with the intention of khutbah, the prayer is valid according to Abu Hanifa, but invalid according to Sahibayn and al-Shafiʿi. This affects the imam's choice and the congregation's obligation.
In practice, many Hanafi masjids follow the Sahibayn view for caution.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical scenario
Given a case: a khatib on Friday says 'Subhanallah' (meaning to praise Allah) with full intention for khutbah, then prays. Determine the ruling according to each opinion.
Also consider if the phrase was uttered without intention (e.g., sneezing) – then all agree it does not count.

کے لئے قیام شرط ہے اس طرح خطبہ کے لئے بھی قیام شرط ہوگا۔
امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی کی دلیل اس بات پر کہ طہارت خطبہ کے لئے شرط ہے یہ ہے کہ خطبہ نصف نماز کے مرتبہ میں ہے چنانچہ مروی ہے کہ ان ابن عمر وعائشه قالا انما قصر الجمعة لمكان الخطبة پس جس طرح نماز کے واسطے طہارت شرط ہے اسی طرح خطبہ کے لئے بھی شرط ہے۔
خطبہ میں ذکر پر اکتفاء جائز ہے یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء
فان اقتصر على ذكر الله جاز عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لابد من ذكر طويل يسمى خطبة لان الخطبة هي الواجبة والتسبيحة والتحميدة لا تسمى خطبة وقال الشافعى لا يجوز حتى يخطب خطبتين اعتبار اللمتعارف وله قوله تعالى فاسعوا الى ذكر الله من غير فصل وعن عثمان انه قال الحمد الله فارتج عليه فنزل وصلى
ترجمہ پس اگر خطیب نے ذکر اللہ پر اکتفاء کیا تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ طویل ذکر جس کا نام خطبہ رکھا جاتا ہے ضروری ہے کیونکہ واجب تو خطبہ ہے اور ایک تسبیح یا ایک تحمید خطبہ نہیں ہوتا۔ اور امام شافعی نے کہا جائز نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ دو خطبہ پڑھے عادت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے ۔ او را بو حنیفہ کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَاسْعَوا إلى ذِكْرِ اللهِ ہے بغیر تفصیل کے۔ اور
حضرت عثمان کا حال مروی ہے کہ آپ نے الحمد للہ کہا آپ کی زبان رک گئی تو آپ منبر سے اترے اور نماز پڑھائی۔ تشریح خطبہ کی مقدار میں خود علماء احنافہ مختلف ہیں۔ چنانچہ امام اعظم ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اگر خطبہ کے ارادہ سے فقط الحمد للہ کا یا سبحان اللہ کہا یالا الہ الا اللہ کہا تو جائز ہے اور اگر چھینکنے کی وجہ سے خطیب نے الحمد للہ کہایا تعجب کی وجہ سے سبحان اللہ کہا تو بالا تفاق خطبہ جائز نہ ہوگا۔ صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ اس قدر طویل کا ہونا ضروری ہے جس کو عر فا خطبہ کہا جا سکے۔ متعارف خطبہ یہ ہے کہ خطیب اللہ کی حمد بیان کرے، رسول اللہ پر درود بھیجے اور تمام مسلمانوں کے لئے خیر کی دعا کرے۔ امام کرخی کے نزدیک متعارف خطبہ کی مقدار ثمین آیات ہیں! اور بعض کے نزدیک تشہد کی مقدار ہے یعنی التحیات سے عبدہ و رسولہ تک ۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ واجب تو وہ ہے جس کو خطبہ کہا جا سکے اور الحمد للہ کہنا یا سبحان اللہ کہنا ا لا اله الا اللہ کہنا اس کا نام خطبہ نہیں ہے پس اگر خطیب نے فقط یہ کلمہ کہا تو خطبہ واجبہ ادا نہ ہوگا۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ دو خطبہ واجب ہیں پہلا خطبہ اللہ کی حمد، صلوۃ علی النبی، تقویٰ کی وصیت اور کم سے کم ایک آیت پر مشتمل ہو۔ اور دوسرے خطبہ میں آیت کی جگہ مسلمان مردوں اور عورتوں کے لئے دعا ہو۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل عرف اور عادۃ الناس
ہے یعنی اس سے کم کولوگوں کی عادت اور عرف میں خطبہ نہیں کہا جاتا اور بالعموم خطیب حضرات اس سے کم خطبہ نہیں دیتے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ الله ہے بایں طور کہ تمام مفسرین کے نزدیک ذکر اللہ سے خطبہ مراد ہے اور اس میں قلیل و کثیر کی کوئی تفصیل بھی نہیں ہے۔ اس سے ثابت ہوا کہ مطلقا ذکر اللہ سے خواہ قلیل ہو یا کثیر ہو خطبہ واجہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔ حضرت مشین کا حال مروی ہے کہ خلیفہ ہونے کے بعد جب پہلی بار خطبہ جمعہ پڑھنے کے لئے منبر پر چڑھے اور الحمد للہ کہا تو آپ کی زبان بند ہوئی ۔ آپ منبر سے اتر گئے۔ اور لوگوں کو جمعہ کی نماز پڑھائی ۔ اس وقت علماء صحابہ بھی موجود تھے مگر کسی نے حضرت عثمان کے اس فعال پر نکیر نہیں فرمائی۔ پس صحابہ کے اجماع سے بھی ثابت ہو گیا کہ اللہ کے ذکر پر اکتفاء کرنے سے خطبہ جائز ہو جائے گا۔ رہا صاحبین کا یہ کہنا کہ لفظ الحمد للہ کو عر فا خطبہ نہیں کہا جاتا۔ بلاشبہ اس کو عر فا خطبہ نہیں کہا جاتا گر لفظ خطبہ کہا جاتا ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس شخص سے

کے
Chapter of Friday Prayer. Ashraf al-Bidaya sharh Urdu Hidaya volume 2. Ashraf. Standing is a condition for it, similarly standing is also a condition for the sermon. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi‘i's evidence that purification is a condition for the sermon is that the sermon is in the rank of half the prayer. Accordingly, it is narrated from Ibn ‘Umar and ‘A’ishah that they said: 'Indeed the Friday prayer was shortened because of the sermon.' So just as purification is a condition for prayer, similarly it is a condition for the sermon. [Section:] Is it permissible to suffice with dhikr in the sermon? Sayings of the jurists. 'If he restricts himself to the remembrance of Allah, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifah. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: A lengthy remembrance that is called a sermon is necessary, because the required thing is the sermon, and a single glorification (tasbihah) or praise (tahmidah) is not called a sermon. Al-Shafi‘i said: It is not permissible until he delivers two sermons, considering the customary practice.' His (Abu Hanifah's) evidence is the saying of Allah Most High: 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (Q. 62:9) without specification. And (the incident) of ‘Uthman: He said 'Alhamdulillah' (praise be to Allah), then his tongue became locked, so he descended and prayed. Explanation: The scholars of the Hanafi school themselves differ on the extent of the sermon. Accordingly, according to Imam A‘zam Abu Hanifah, if with the intention of the sermon he says only 'Alhamdulillah' or 'Subhanallah' or 'La ilaha illallah', it is permissible. But if he said 'Alhamdulillah' due to sneezing or 'Subhanallah' due to astonishment, then by consensus the sermon is not valid. The Sahibayn said: It is necessary that (the sermon) be so lengthy that it can be called a sermon customarily. The customary sermon is that the khatib mentions the praise of Allah, sends blessings upon the Messenger of Allah, and prays for goodness for all Muslims. According to Imam al-Karkhi, the amount of the customary sermon is three verses. According to some, it is the amount of the tashahhud, i.e., from 'al-Tahiyyat' to 'wa ‘abduhu wa rasuluhu'. The evidence of the Sahibayn is that what is required is what can be called a sermon, and saying 'Alhamdulillah' or 'Subhanallah' or 'La ilaha illallah' is not called a sermon. So if the khatib says only this word, the required sermon is not fulfilled. Imam Shafi‘i said: Two sermons are required. The first sermon consists of praise of Allah, salawat upon the Prophet, exhortation to piety, and at least one verse. In the second sermon, instead of a verse, a supplication for Muslim men and women. Imam Shafi‘i's evidence is custom and the practice of the people, i.e., less than this is not called a sermon in people's custom and practice, and generally khatibs do not give a sermon shorter than this. Imam Abu Hanifah's evidence is the saying of Allah Most High: 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah' in that all commentators interpret 'remembrance of Allah' to mean the sermon, and there is no specification of little or much in it. From this it is proven that absolutely any remembrance of Allah, whether little or much, fulfills the required sermon. The incident of Hadrat ‘Uthman is narrated: When after becoming caliph he ascended the pulpit to give the Friday sermon and said 'Alhamdulillah', his tongue became locked. He descended from the pulpit and led the people in the Friday prayer. At that time, the scholars among the Companions were present, and none of them disapproved of this action of ‘Uthman. Thus by the consensus of the Companions it is proven that the sermon becomes valid by restricting oneself to the remembrance of Allah. As for the Sahibayn's statement that the word 'Alhamdulillah' is not customarily called a sermon — undoubtedly it is not called a sermon customarily, but it is called a sermon verbally. This is why the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the person who said 'Man yuti‘illaha wa rasulahu faqad rashad, wa man ya‘sihima faqad ghawa': 'You are the khatib'. Look: for this amount of speech he called him a khatib. From this it is understood that it is not necessary for the sermon to be lengthy. (Fath al-Qadir).
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum content of the Friday khutbah. The discussion begins with the condition of standing for the khutbah, then shifts to purity. The core dispute is whether a brief dhikr suffices. Abu Hanifa holds that any remembrance of Allah, even a single tasbih or tahmid, is sufficient if done with the intention of the khutbah. He relies on the absolute command in Q. 62:9 (فاسعوا إلى ذكر الله) and the practice of ‘Uthman, who only said 'Alhamdulillah' and descended, with no Companion objection, implying tacit consensus. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the obligatory sermon must be something customarily called a khutbah—a set speech containing praise, blessings on the Prophet, and supplication. A single phrase does not qualify. Imam al-Shafi‘i requires two sermons with specific elements, relying on established custom. The passage also notes variations among Hanafi scholars: some define a customary khutbah as three verses; others equate it to the length of tashahhud. The commentary upholds Abu Hanifa's view as supported by the Qur'anic wording (absolute 'dhikr'), the incident of ‘Uthman, and the Prophet's calling a person a khatib for a brief statement. The author cites Fath al-Qadir confirming that lengthy speech is not necessary.

Key Terms
خطبہ (khutbah): The sermon delivered before the Friday prayer, required for its validity.
ذکر (dhikr): Remembrance of Allah, including phrases like 'Alhamdulillah', 'Subhanallah', 'La ilaha illallah'.
تسبیحة (tasbīḥah): Saying 'Subhanallah' (Glory be to Allah).
عرف (ʿurf): Customary practice of the people that can determine the linguistic or legal meaning.
متعارف خطبہ (mutʿāraf khutbah): The customary sermon as practiced by the community.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary textual evidence used by Abu Hanifa to support his view that a brief dhikr suffices for the Friday khutbah?
A) The consensus of the Companions on the minimum must be three verses.
B) The absolute command in Quran 62:9 (فاسعوا إلى ذكر الله) without specifying quantity.
C) The hadith that the Prophet said the khutbah should be concise.
D) The practice of the Prophet that he always gave a lengthy sermon.

Key Takeaway
The minimum content of the Friday khutbah is disputed: Abu Hanifa allows any intended dhikr, while Sahibayn and al-Shafiʿi require a customary or two-part sermon; the author prefers Abu Hanifa's view.
